Chapter 1
App Introduction

Regalia v1.0.8 is a powerful Android chess playing and analysis application. v1.0.8, following the "Personified Chess Move Animation" and "Personified Chess Sound Effects" reference documents, completely redesigns the move animation and sound system (each piece has a unique personified motion characteristic and matching timbre), and adds light mode support following the "Android Dark Theme Design Principles" and "Android Light Theme Design Principles" (light/dark mode switches automatically with the system global setting; the king icon on the loading overlay and main header toolbar switches between ♔/♚ based on theme). This version is built around the world-class open-source engine Stockfish 18 (arm64-v8a-dotprod native build) and provides a professional-grade playing, review, and training experience for everyone from beginners to advanced players. v1.0.4 introduces Fischer Random Chess (Chess960) mode, Time Control, standardized PGN import/export (compliant with the 1994 PGN specification), heatmap-control-based statistics, Seldepth (selective depth) display, visual annotations (NAG & [%csl]/[%cal]), Web Worker parallel computation, a PGN cache manager, player renaming, bilingual Chinese/English UI, resign (🏳️ Resign), and many other improvements. v1.0.5 adds sensor-fusion board anti-shake (OIS principle), high aspect-ratio screen adaptation, notch/cutout/R-corner adaptation, phase analysis precision (opening/middlegame/endgame multi-criteria detection), review arrow shrink optimization, and more. v1.0.6 adds Chess960-mode ECO opening recognition suppression, PGN with FEN header round-trip preservation, per-move selection on the stats page, unified gray-out styling, portrait New Game dialog optimization, scroll-position preservation, engine-eval FEN sanitization, the king-then-rook castling gesture (essential for Chess960), Chess960 castling detection overhaul, and explicit SL skill-level display. v1.0.7 focuses on code-quality and stability maintenance: it fixes several latent bugs uncovered by three independent code reviews (critical-move cache not invalidated on undo, lightweight board update path missing the castling-rook marker, engine-notification throttle cache staleness, stats-page PGN comment XSS risk, cross-game eval-cache pollution, CSP potentially blocking Blob Workers), adds clickable GitHub repository links for DroidFish and Stockfish in the About dialog, further refines portrait full-screen layout and Android back-button handling, and merges the duplicated HTML-escape functions. v1.0.7 Phase 2 adds a main-screen "Quick Toolbar" (moving the Undo/Redo/Flip/AI Hint/Control Range buttons from the top toolbar to below the board), setup-mode 🔁 manual castle-rights marker button and ⚡ manual en-passant marker button (removing the auto-grant behavior in favor of fully manual control, validated against the Fischer Random Chess castling rule), and first-principles root-cause fixes for slim-phone portrait right-edge clipping and dialog-centering issues. v1.0.7 Phase 17 fixes the Chess960 castling "king self-capture" critical bug (when the king's starting position happens to be its castling destination) and the review "Analyze All" button state not auto-refreshing, and adopts 5 reasonable suggestions from the Kimi audit report (_escFEN backtick escaping, _cloneStatsState replacing JSON deep clone, .bgrid gets content-visibility:auto, animateMove honors prefers-reduced-motion on the JS side too, stats board max-width modestly relaxed). v1.0.7 Phase 18 implements the two remaining architectural suggestions from the Kimi audit: _reviewEvalCache LRU eviction (MAX_ENTRIES=2000 soft cap, skips the currently-viewed step, persistence preserves LRU order) and a review move-list virtual list (>80 moves triggers windowed rendering, only the viewport + 10-row overscan is rendered as DOM nodes, with dynamic row-height measurement), plus 11 bug fixes including Chess960 unmakeMv board corruption, makeMvInPlace castling-rights not cleared, and animateMove race condition. v1.0.7 Phase 19 performs the most comprehensive first-principles code review to date: 7 subagents reviewed all 20 source files (28,281 lines) in parallel, implementing 20+ critical fixes including _reviewEvalCache corruption race, cross-mode stale callback race, PGN [%eval] placeholder offset, StockfishNative thread safety (volatile fields), stopAndWaitForBestmove timeout discard, ChessApp Error handling, and stats.html CSP addition. v1.0.7 Phase 3 redesigns the portrait UI from scratch (switching to @media(orientation:portrait) with no width threshold + vw/clamp() auto-scaling font sizes), and fixes multiple first-principles bugs: 🔁/⚡ markers not displaying outside Setup mode, double-stepped pawns not auto-receiving the ⚡ marker, marked pieces not receiving their legal moves, and incorrect FEN reverse-mapping for en-passant targets. It also ensures that FEN/PGN exported from Setup mode automatically switches to Shredder castling notation when pieces are on non-standard squares, guaranteeing lossless round-trip.

18 Stockfish Engine Version
6+SL AI Difficulty Levels
960 Chess960 Start Positions
8 MultiPV Lines

Core Features

  • Built-in Stockfish 18 engine, arm64-v8a-dotprod native build, automatically utilizing the NEON accelerated instruction set
  • Fischer Random Chess (Chess960 / Fischer Random Chess): 960 randomized start positions, compliant with the official Chess960 castling rules. PGN import/export includes the [Variant "Chess960"] header tag and Shredder-FEN castling-rights encoding v1.0.4
  • Time Control: supports 5 clock modes — Untimed / Sudden Death / Fischer Increment / Bronstein Delay / US Delay. The AI uses the go wtime/btime/winc/binc UCI command so Stockfish 18 manages its own time allocation v1.0.4
  • Standardized PGN handling: export contains the Seven Tag Roster, ~78-column line wrapping, [%eval] and [%clk] embedded tags, [%csl]/[%cal] visual annotations, and NAG numeric glyphs ($1-$6 move quality, $10-$18 position evaluation) v1.0.4
  • Seldepth (SD) display: the eval bar and AI opponent bar now show the D15 SD22 format (main iterative depth + selective search depth), fully reflecting the engine's tactical search depth v1.0.4
  • Heatmap statistics: the statistics page now includes a "Heatmap Control Statistics" block that walks every real position in the game, computes per-square attacker counts for both sides, and renders an 8×8 average-control heatmap plus strongest/weakest-square stats v1.0.4
  • Resign (🏳️ Resign): the toolbar gains a 🏳️ button; on resign, engineStop() is called first to hard-stop the engine v1.0.4
  • PGN cache manager (📚): the review interface adds a 📚 button that opens a cache manager modal, supporting save/import/rename/add-tag/search/filter/batch-delete of PGN cache entries. Stored in the app private directory /data/data/com.Regalia/files/pgn_cache/, not cleared by HyperOS 3 cache cleaner v1.0.4
  • Player renaming (📝): PGN header [White] / [Black] player names can be renamed. Exported PGN AI opponent names now include the difficulty tier suffix (e.g. [Black "AI Opponent Lv.4"]) v1.0.4
  • Bilingual Chinese/English UI (🌐 ↔️中 / ↔️EN): the toggle button on the left of the eval bar switches language mode in one tap. All UI text (toolbar, AI opponent bar, side panel, New Game dialog, Engine Configuration, Toast notifications, About page, Foreground Service Notification) is fully bilingual v1.0.1
  • Web Worker parallel computation: a new worker-pool.js offloads PGN parsing, statistics computation, and control-map computation to a Web Worker thread to avoid blocking UI rendering v1.0.4
  • 6 preset AI difficulty levels + SL tier (custom Skill Level) + ⚙️ manual settings, suitable for players of all levels
  • AI thinking progress bar displays search depth, node count, speed, and evaluation score in real time
  • Ponder (predictive) mode — AI keeps thinking during the opponent's turn. Recommended to enable while charging for faster subsequent moves
  • MultiPV multi-line analysis (1-8 lines), displaying multiple engine-recommended variations simultaneously
  • Variation system: engine-predicted continuations and alternative variations displayed in move record and review (controlled by the 💬 Variations toggle)
  • Full review mode: step-by-step navigation, evaluation trend chart, move classification and key-move annotation, Analyze All
  • ECO opening library with search, opening recommendations, and family filter
  • Syzygy online endgame tablebase query (win/draw/loss determination for 7-piece and below endgames)
  • WDL win/draw/loss probability display (enabled by default), intuitively understanding position advantage
  • Evaluation score includes the SF18 engine badge, search depth D indicator, Seldepth SD indicator, plus node and speed information
  • Square control range heatmap (🌈/🌗 toggle), with arrow indicators and square control info panel
  • AI hint multi-line display, showing all recommended moves and scores (SAN format)
  • Chess principles panel, providing real-time top 10 chess principle reminders (bilingual)
  • Engine configuration export/import (key=value text format), convenient for multi-device sync
  • FEN copy/import, supporting quick restoration of any position
  • Setup mode, freely edit board positions with undo/redo/reset/clear
  • Compatible with Android 5.0 through Android 15, adapted for Xiaomi HyperOS 3

Implementation Details: Module Architecture

The app adopts a multi-module layered architecture. Source code is located in the assets/chess.src/ directory and merged into a single chess.html file via the build script build-chess.py, loaded and run by Android WebView:

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │ MainActivity.java (Android Host) │ │ ├─ ChessWebView ← loads chess.html │ │ ├─ StatsActivity ← loads stats.html (statistics page) │ │ ├─ StockfishNative.java (UCI engine mgmt + PGN cache) │ │ │ ├─ Process start/stop, UCI comms, engine switch │ │ │ ├─ engine_jni.cpp (chmod / renice) │ │ │ ├─ PGN Cache: listPGNCaches / savePGNCache / │ │ │ │ getPGNCache / deletePGNCaches │ │ │ ├─ Persistent Store: persistentGet / persistentSet │ │ │ ├─ getEngineSkillLevel() [v1.0.6 NEW] │ │ │ └─ setChess960Mode() / isChess960Mode() [v1.0.4] │ │ ├─ StabilizationHelper.java (sensor anti-shake) [v1.0.5]│ │ │ └─ TYPE_LINEAR_ACCELERATION translation stabilization│ │ └─ AndroidBridge (JS↔Java bridge interface) │ └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ ↕ JavaScript↔Java Bridge ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │ chess.html (WebView single-page app) │ │ ├─ index.html.tpl (CSS style template) │ │ ├─ game-logic.js (pure chess logic, no UI/engine) │ │ │ ├─ Board repr, move gen, legality check │ │ │ ├─ Zobrist hash, FEN gen/parse │ │ │ ├─ AI_LEVELS, ELO_MATCH, control range calc │ │ │ ├─ Chess principles _principlesHTML() (i18n) │ │ │ ├─ Language preference: toggleLang() + persistence │ │ │ ├─ _castleSide() castling detection [v1.0.6 NEW] │ │ │ ├─ makeMv/makeMvInPlace rook save [v1.0.6 FIX] │ │ │ └─ pseudoMoves() castle flag [v1.0.6 NEW] │ │ ├─ chess960.js (Chess960 rules) [v1.0.4 NEW] │ │ │ ├─ SP-ID generator (0..959) │ │ │ ├─ Shredder-FEN castling-rights encode/decode │ │ │ ├─ isChess960CastlingLegal() │ │ │ └─ chess960CastlingRookMove() / findCastlingRooks() │ │ ├─ pgn-standard.js (standardized PGN) [v1.0.4 NEW] │ │ │ ├─ Seven Tag Roster │ │ │ ├─ ~78-column wrapping, result marker │ │ │ ├─ Tolerant parse: nested comments, unclosed, 0-0→O-O│ │ │ ├─ NAG_MAP / nagToSymbol / formatNagToken │ │ │ ├─ formatCslTag / formatCalTag / parseCslTag / │ │ │ │ parseCalTag (visual annotations) │ │ │ └─ TimeControl parse/format (6 formats) │ │ ├─ worker-pool.js (Web Worker parallel) [v1.0.4 NEW] │ │ │ ├─ workerParsePGN() │ │ │ ├─ workerComputeHeatmapStats() │ │ │ ├─ workerGetCtrlMap() │ │ │ ├─ terminateWorker() (pagehide/beforeunload) │ │ │ └─ Sync fallback (when Worker unavailable) │ │ ├─ ai-bridge.js (engine communication layer) │ │ │ ├─ UCI param config, export/import (key=value) │ │ │ ├─ Engine callbacks: onBestMove / onEngineEval / │ │ │ │ onEngineProgress / onPonderProgress │ │ │ ├─ Eval state mgmt, WDL conversion, seldepth parse │ │ │ ├─ Review eval cache _reviewEvalCache (no cap) │ │ │ ├─ Engine heartbeat, crash recovery │ │ │ ├─ _sanitizeFenForEngine() FEN sanitize [v1.0.6 NEW] │ │ │ └─ _aiOpponentNameWithLevel() SL mode display [v1.0.6]│ │ ├─ tablebase.js (Syzygy endgame tablebase query) │ │ ├─ eco-data.js (ECO opening library data) │ │ └─ ui.js (rendering & interaction) │ │ ├─ render() full render + incremental update │ │ ├─ _updateChangedSquares() lightweight update [v1.0.6]│ │ ├─ _getSqBg() control heatmap coloring │ │ ├─ _updateArrows() SVG arrow overlay │ │ ├─ _buildEvalTrendSVG() review trend chart │ │ ├─ _classifyMove() move classification │ │ ├─ playSound() Web Audio API sound synthesis │ │ ├─ Time-control clock UI render (gameClocks) │ │ ├─ PGN cache manager UI (📚) │ │ ├─ King-then-rook castling gesture [v1.0.6 NEW] │ │ │ ├─ _getCastlingRookSquares() mark castling rook │ │ │ ├─ _computeCastlingRookSetForSelection() │ │ │ └─ castle-ring golden dashed ring marker │ │ ├─ _updateSingleSq() castling-rook marker sync [v1.0.7 FIX]│ │ ├─ Scroll position preservation [v1.0.6 NEW] │ │ ├─ handleBackPress() promotion/save-prompt priority [v1.0.7]│ │ └─ Touch/click/swipe event handling │ └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Data flow between modules follows strict unidirectional dependency: ui.js calls pure functions from game-logic.js to obtain game state, communicates with the engine via ai-bridge.js, and ai-bridge.js interacts with the Java-layer Stockfish process through AndroidBridge. Heavy compute tasks (PGN parsing, statistics, heatmap) are delegated to a Web Worker thread via worker-pool.js to avoid blocking UI rendering.

build-chess.py — Build Script Core Logic # Merge JS modules → chess.html modules = [ "game-logic.js", "chess960.js", # v1.0.4 NEW "pgn-standard.js", # v1.0.4 NEW "worker-pool.js", # v1.0.4 NEW "ai-bridge.js", "tablebase.js", "eco-data.js", "ui.js", ] with open("index.html.tpl","r",encoding="utf-8") as f: html = f.read() js = "\n".join( open(f"chess.src/{m}","r",encoding="utf-8").read() for m in modules ) html = html.replace("/*__JS__*/", js) with open("chess.html","w",encoding="utf-8") as f: f.write(html)

Chapter 3
Installation & Launch

System Requirements

ItemRequirement
Operating SystemAndroid 5.0 (API 21) through Android 15 (API 35)
CPU Architecturearm64-v8a (dotprod instruction set recommended)
Storage SpaceApprox. 200 MB (excluding PGN cache)
Compatible SystemsXiaomi HyperOS 3 (Android 14 base) verified

APK Signing

This version's APK uses a v1 / v2 / v3 triple signing scheme, ensuring proper installation and verification on all supported Android versions:

  • v1 Signing (JAR Signing): compatible with Android 5.0-6.0 devices
  • v2 Signing (APK Signature Scheme v2): Android 7.0+ incremental verification, faster installation
  • v3 Signing (APK Signature Scheme v3): Android 9.0+ key rotation support
Tip: Xiaomi HyperOS 3 has strict APK signature verification; v2+v3 signing ensures the installation passes system verification smoothly. If you encounter installation issues, please allow "Install unknown apps" in system settings.

Installation Steps

  1. Transfer the APK file to your Android device
  2. Tap the APK file in your file manager
  3. If the system prompts "unknown source", go to settings to allow installation
  4. Follow the installation wizard to complete installation
  5. Launch the app — the engine will initialize automatically

First Launch

On first launch, the app displays a loading screen: ♔ King icon ( #E8E8F0) + app name + progress bar ( #d4a017→#ffd700 gradient). The engine binary is automatically extracted to the app's private directory and granted execute permission. Once the progress bar reaches 100%, "Engine Ready!" is displayed and the loading screen fades out over 0.5 seconds.

Implementation Details: Engine Initialization Flow

StockfishNative.java copies the engine binary from assets to the app's private directory (context.getFilesDir()) in onCreate(), granting execute permission via a JNI call to nativeChmod(). After WebView loads chess.html, the JS layer calls AndroidBridge.startEngine() to start the UCI process; once the engine returns uciok via stdout, _engineReady=true is set.

ai-bridge.js — Engine Ready Callback function onEngineReady(){ _engineReady=true; _needNewGameForEngine=true; // Need to re-issue ucinewgame after crash recovery _updateLoadingStatus('Engine Ready!',100); // 0.5s fade out loading screen setTimeout(function(){_hideLoadingOverlay()},500); }

Foreground Service Notification v1.0.1 Enhanced

While the engine process is running, the app displays a Foreground Service Notification that continuously shows engine status information in the system notification bar. Its purpose is to inform the Android system that the engine process is performing important computation, preventing the system from terminating the engine process due to memory reclamation or power-saving policies, and ensuring that play and analysis are not interrupted.

v1.0.1 Simplified state: The notification now shows only three engine states — "Engine Ready!" (ready), "Analyzing" (AI thinking / Ponder / review analysis in progress), and "Engine error: ..." (truncated error message on failure). Search depth, node count, and speed are no longer displayed. Detailed depth/nodes/speed/score data is still shown in real time in the in-app top eval bar; the notification is intentionally minimal to avoid frequent-update distractions.
Click-to-open: Tapping the notification opens the app's main screen (PendingIntent + FLAG_ACTIVITY_NEW_TASK | SINGLE_TOP | CLEAR_TOP), allowing the user to quickly return to the game from any other app.
Non-removable: The notification sets setOngoing(true) + FLAG_NO_CLEAR; under normal conditions it cannot be swiped away by the user. On Android 14+ (including Xiaomi HyperOS 3), the system may allow manual dismissal, but the foreground service itself keeps running, and the notification auto-restores on the next status update.
Bilingual notification: The text content of the Foreground Service Notification is bilingual, following the app's current language setting (stored in SharedPreferences, synced from JS via saveLangPref). In Chinese mode the notification text is Chinese; in English mode it is English, consistent with the interface language.
Notification permission: On Android 13 (API 33) and above, the app proactively requests Notification Permission (POST_NOTIFICATIONS) when the engine is first launched, to ensure the Foreground Service Notification can be displayed normally. If the user denies permission, the engine still runs normally, but the system notification bar will not display engine status information, slightly increasing the risk of the engine process being terminated by the system.
Chapter 4
Interface Layout

The app interface consists of four regions: the top title bar, the toolbar, the board area, and the side panel. The overall design follows a dark-theme color system:

Title Bar

The title bar is at the very top of the screen and contains the app identifier, the language toggle button, and real-time evaluation info. The eval bar now shows the D15 SD22 format (main iterative depth + selective search depth), fully reflecting the engine's tactical search depth:

Title Bar (with D15 SD22 seldepth display)
♔ Regalia v1.0.7 ℹ️
↔️EN
😊 Advantage (+0.85) SF18 D15 SD22 4.5M 1.2M/s

D15 is the main iterative depth (depth); SD22 is the selective search depth (seldepth). SD is shown only when > 0 and > depth.

Control Heatmap

Tap the 🌗 toolbar button to enable control-range display (the 🌗 button becomes 🌈 when enabled; tap again to disable) — board squares are dynamically colored by the control strength of each side. The heatmap uses the HSL color space, encoding control information via three dimensions: hue, saturation, and lightness.

Heatmap Coloring Algorithm

The heatmap color is determined by three parameters:

  • Advantage direction (adv): (own control count − opponent control count) ÷ total control count. adv > 0 = own advantage; adv < 0 = opponent advantage. Determines hue.
  • Control strength (str): total control count ÷ 8 (capped at 1.0). Determines saturation and lightness.
  • No control: when neither side has any control, the fixed color #3a2020 is used.
ParameterFormulaRangeEffect
Hueadv≥0: 280 − adv×60
adv<0: 280 − adv×80		≈220°~340°Purple-blue = balanced; bluer = own advantage; redder = opponent advantage
Saturation0.50 + str×0.4050%~90%More control = more vivid
Lightness0.48 − str×0.1236%~48%More control = darker

Hue Meaning Reference

Hue RangeColorMeaningSample
H ≈ 220°Blue-purpleOwn strong control hsl(220,80%,36%)
H ≈ 260°PurpleBalanced / moderate control hsl(260,65%,42%)
H ≈ 280°Purple-redSlight advantage / baseline color hsl(280,55%,46%)
H ≈ 320°Red-purpleOpponent moderate control hsl(320,70%,38%)
H ≈ 340°RedOpponent strong control hsl(340,80%,36%)
—Dark red-brownNo control from either side #3a2020

Arrow Meanings

On hovering or selecting a square, an SVG arrow overlay appears above the board, showing which pieces control that square:

Arrow ColorHexSampleMeaning
Warm gold#D4A017Own side (mover) piece control arrow — from the controlling piece to the target square
Cool silver-blue#8A9BAEOpponent piece control arrow — from the opponent piece to the target square

Arrows are 0.85 opacity, 4px wide, drawn with SVG <line> elements with triangular arrowhead markers. The arrow starts at the controlling piece center and ends 14px offset from the target-square center, avoiding overlap with the piece.

Implementation Details: Control Heatmap

getCtrlMap() in game-logic.js walks every square on the board; for each occupied square it calls attacked() to get the piece's attack targets, aggregating them into an 8×8 control matrix. Each matrix cell records {white: [{piece, position}], black: [{piece, position}]}.

_getSqBg() in ui.js computes the HSL color from the control matrix and overrides the board-square background; _updateArrows() draws control arrows on the SVG overlay using persistent SVG elements to avoid recreating DOM. Heavy compute (such as full-game heatmap traversal on the statistics page) is delegated to a Web Worker via worker-pool.js to avoid blocking the UI.

game-logic.js — getCtrlMap() control-range calculation function getCtrlMap(b){ const cm=[]; for(let r=0;r<8;r++){ cm[r]=[]; for(let c=0;c<8;c++) cm[r][c]={white:[],black:[]}; } for(let r=0;r<8;r++) for(let c=0;c<8;c++){ const p=b[r][c]; if(p){ const atks=attacked(b,{row:r,col:c}); for(const a of atks){ cm[a.row][a.col][p.color].push( {piece:p,position:{row:r,col:c}}); } } } return cm; }
ui.js — _getSqBg() heatmap coloring algorithm function _getSqBg(rr,cc,cm,isL,lastMove){ let bg=isL?SQ_LIGHT:SQ_DARK; let ctrlBg=null; if(cm){ const e=cm[rr][cc]; if(e){ const wc=e.white.length, bc=e.black.length; const myC=playerColor==='white'?wc:bc; const opC=playerColor==='white'?bc:wc; const net=myC-opC; const total=myC+opC; const adv=total>0?net/total:0; const str=Math.min(1,total/8); let hue; if(myC===0&&opC===0){ ctrlBg='#3a2020'; // no control }else{ if(adv>=0) hue=280-adv*60; else hue=280-adv*80; if(hue>=360) hue-=360; const sat=0.50+str*0.40; // 50%~90% const lit=0.48-str*0.12; // 36%~48% ctrlBg=`hsl(${Math.round(hue)},${Math.round(sat*100)}%,${Math.round(lit*100)}%)`; } } } if(ctrlBg) bg=ctrlBg; return bg; }

Making Moves

The app uses tap-to-move: tap the piece you want to move (the piece is highlighted and legal moves are shown), then tap the target square to complete the move. When a pawn reaches the back rank, a promotion dialog appears (Queen → Rook → Bishop → Knight). In Chess960 mode, castling follows the official Chess960 rules: King ends on g1/c1, Rook ends on f1/d1, but starting positions are randomized.

Implementation Details: Making Moves & Setup

sqClick() in ui.js handles board tap events, dispatching to different logic depending on the current mode (move/setup). In move mode, it calls legalMoves() from game-logic.js to generate the legal-move set; once the target square is tapped, makeMvInPlace() is called to execute the move. In Chess960 mode, chess960.js's isChess960CastlingLegal() / chess960CastlingRookMove() / findCastlingRooks() hook into the gameVariant==='chess960' branches of pseudoMoves, makeMv, and makeMvInPlace.

In setup mode, setupClick() places a piece on the target square according to setupPiece and setupColor; when placing a King, the existing same-color King is automatically removed. On exiting setup mode, validateSetupPosition() validates the position legality.

game-logic.js — Move execution core function makeMvInPlace(state, move){ state.board[move.from.row][move.from.col]=null; state.board[move.to.row][move.to.col]=move.piece; if(move.enPassant){ const epRow=move.piece.color==='white'? move.to.row+1:move.to.row-1; state.board[epRow][move.to.col]=null; } if(move.castling){ // Chess960: rookFrom / rookTo computed by chess960CastlingRookMove() // Standard chess: kingside → rookFromCol=7, rookToCol=5 const rookFromCol=move.castling==='kingside'?7:0; const rookToCol=move.castling==='kingside'?5:3; state.board[move.from.row][rookToCol]= state.board[move.from.row][rookFromCol]; state.board[move.from.row][rookFromCol]=null; } if(move.promotion){ state.board[move.to.row][move.to.col]= {type:move.promotion,color:move.piece.color}; } }

Ponder Mode v1.0.1

When enabled, the AI keeps thinking about the opponent's possible replies after making its own move. The AI opponent bar's row 2 right-aligns the ponder search info (does not show the predicted move); if AI Hint is also in use, the hint bar also shows ponder info and the predicted move. Recommended to enable while charging.

Implementation Details: AI Opponent & Engine Communication

AI move flow: ui.js calls doAIMove() → sends go depth N via AndroidBridge (or go wtime/btime/winc/binc during time control) → Java StockfishNative manages the UCI process → the engine returns bestmove via stdout → Java calls back JS onBestMove() → ui.js executes the move and updates the UI.

Evaluation flow: requestEngineEval() sends go depth 22 (first setoption MultiPV=1, setoption Contempt=0) → the engine calls back onEngineProgress() in real time via info lines (with seldepth) → finally calls back onEngineEval() with the full eval (including WDL, depth, seldepth) → restores play options (Contempt=24, original MultiPV).

v1.0.4 Rev32 eval-mode optimization: before evaluation search, force Contempt=0 (objective eval) + MultiPV=1 (max search depth) + UCI_ShowWDL=true (output WDL probability). After eval completes, restore play options.

ai-bridge.js — Engine eval callback (with seldepth) function onEngineEval(scoreCp,scoreMate,depth,seldepth, wdlW,wdlD,wdlL){ _lastEngineCallbackTime=Date.now(); // heartbeat if(reviewMode&&_reviewEvalRequestedStep!==reviewStep) return; // discard stale callback _evalLoading=false; _sfDepth=depth||0; _sfSeldepth=seldepth||0; // v1.0.4 Rev33 NEW _sfWdlW=(wdlW!=null&&wdlW>=0)?wdlW:-1; _sfWdlD=(wdlD!=null&&wdlD>=0)?wdlD:-1; _sfWdlL=(wdlL!=null&&wdlL>=0)?wdlL:-1; // Convert from mover's perspective to White's perspective if(_evalForBlackTurn&&_sfWdlW>=0){ const tmp=_sfWdlW; _sfWdlW=_sfWdlL; _sfWdlL=tmp; } // Cache review eval if(reviewMode){ _reviewEvalCache.set(reviewStep,{ eval:_sfEval,mate:_sfMateDistance, depth:_sfDepth,seldepth:_sfSeldepth, wdlW:_sfWdlW,wdlD:_sfWdlD,wdlL:_sfWdlL }); } }
ui.js — seldepth display logic (formatEval) // SD display rule: show when seldepth > 0 and seldepth > depth let depthStr = 'D' + _sfDepth; if (_sfSeldepth > 0 && _sfSeldepth > _sfDepth) { depthStr += ' SD' + _sfSeldepth; } // AI opponent bar row 2 uses localized label: 选深 / SelDepth let seldepthLabel = T('seldepth_label'); // zh:选深, en:SelDepth let searchInfo = 'D' + _sfDepth + ' ' + seldepthLabel + ':' + _sfSeldepth + ' ' + formatNodes(_sfNodes) + ' ' + formatNps(_sfNps) + ' (' + formatEval(_sfEval) + ')';

Configuration Export & Import

Supports exporting/importing key=value text-format configuration files. On export, it first writes to the public Downloads directory; if that fails, it falls back to the app-specific directory, then finally to the clipboard. On import, the config file can be selected in two ways:

  • Built-in file browser: browse the file-system directories; the Android back button navigates up one level, and pressing back at the root closes the browser. Navigation history is recorded for precise back-step traversal.
  • System file picker (recommended): tap "📂 System Picker" to invoke the Android system file picker, which correctly displays all file types (including .txt files). Especially recommended on Android 11+ scoped storage.
Configuration Export Sample # Regalia Engine Settings engine.threads=4 engine.hash=128 engine.multiPV=3 engine.moveOverhead=60 engine.ponder=true engine.showWDL=true engine.skillLevel=20 engine.limitStrength=false engine.elo=2800 engine.autoConfig=true

Implementation Details: Engine Configuration Management

ai-bridge.js maintains the engineSettingsData object holding the current config; each parameter change is immediately synced to the engine process via AndroidBridge. On export, it calls bridge.exportSettings() to get the key=value text, writes it preferentially to the public Downloads directory, falls back to the app-specific directory, and finally to the clipboard.

ai-bridge.js — export settings (simplified) function exportEngineSettings(){ _bridgeCall(function(bridge){ const txt=bridge.exportSettings(); let saved=false, savedPath=''; // Try 1: Public Downloads directory try{ saved=bridge.writeTextFile('/storage/emulated/0/Download/Regalia_engine_settings.txt',txt); if(saved) savedPath='/storage/emulated/0/Download/...'; }catch(e){} // Try 2: App-specific export directory (always works) if(!saved){ try{ savedPath=bridge.getExportPath()+'/Regalia_engine_settings.txt'; saved=bridge.writeTextFile(savedPath,txt); }catch(e){} } // Try 3: Clipboard fallback if(!saved){ try{navigator.clipboard.writeText(txt);}catch(e){} } },null,false); }
Chapter 8
Variation System

The variation system is controlled by the 💬 Variations toggle and displays engine-predicted continuations and alternative variations in the move record and review.

Variation Display Format
1. e4 e5 2. Nf3 Nc6 3. Bb5
🌿 Line 1 a6 4. Ba4 Nf6 5. O-O
🌿 Line 2 f5 4. Bxc6 dxc6 5. d3

Variation tag color #7eb8da. Variations are numbered by display order as Line 1, Line 2, Line 3… (no longer distinguishing main/alternate, ensuring unique labels).

Implementation Details: Variation Recording & Display

The engine returns multiple info lines via the MultiPV mechanism; onMultiPVResult() in ai-bridge.js parses each result into variation text and stores it in the move record's variations array. When ui.js renders the move list with showVariations=true, it calls _formatVariationGroups() to add 🌿 variation rows below each move. Variation row numbers are assigned by array order (1, 2, 3…) for uniqueness.

v1.0.2 fixes the PGN variation "incomplete fragment" issue: when the variation continuation loop encounters the first unparseable token, it now continues (skipping only that token and continuing to parse subsequent moves) instead of breaking; each token uniformly applies moveAlg tolerant matching. When the main PV in MultiPV variation extraction does not start with bestmove, it no longer fakes a "main line" — instead it is included as an independent alternate row in the MultiPV iteration.

ui.js — Variation rendering logic // Move-record card header h+='<div class="card">'; h+='<div class="card-t">'; h+='<span class="ico">📜</span>Move Record'; h+='<button onclick="copyMoveHistory()">📝 PGN</button>'; h+='<div class="toggle" onclick="showVariations=!showVariations;render()">'; h+='<span>💬Variations</span>'; h+='<div class="toggle-sw'+(showVariations?' on':'')+'"'; h+=' style="width:30px;height:16px"></div></div>'; h+='</div></div>';
Chapter 9
Review Analysis

Review mode uses a left/right split layout: the left panel contains the board + eval + trend chart + navigation, and the right panel is the move list. When navigating moves, the move list auto-scrolls to the currently selected move so the current step is always visible.

Evaluation Trend Chart

An SVG line chart — vertical axis is White-perspective eval, horizontal axis is move number. The ↹ Global toggle controls local/global view. The line color changes with the mover: White segments #E8E8F0, Black segments #1A1A2E, intersection points #888.

Landscape adaptation: The eval trend chart adapts to landscape orientation. The chart height is dynamically computed from available viewport space; the SVG rendering uses proportional scaling to ensure correct line shape without stretching distortion or content truncation. In landscape review, the board takes about 45% width of the left panel, and the right-side move list gains more space. The left-panel controls (eval bar, slider, trend chart, buttons) are compact-layout optimized — spacing and sizing are dynamically adjusted to landscape available height, ensuring the trend chart stays visible and is not pushed out of the viewport.
v1.0.3 review eval bar real-time search info: From v1.0.4 Rev33, the review eval bar now shows real-time search depth (D), tactical depth (SD), node count, and search speed. Previously the review eval bar only showed D (without node/speed info). Users now see the full engine search progress during review.

Move Classification

ClassConditionColorSample
BrilliantΔ ≥300 (good)#00cfff
GreatΔ 150-299 (good)#27ae60
GoodΔ 50-149 (good)#a0c060
StandardΔ <50var(--muted)
InaccuracyΔ 50-149 (bad)#f0c040
MistakeΔ 150-299 (bad)#e67e22
BlunderΔ ≥300 (bad)#c0392b

Key moves are highlighted with a gold left border 3px solid #ffd700. Eval delta: positive = green #27ae60, negative = red #c0392b, mate = →Mate green, escape-from-mate = ←Unmate red.

Implementation Details: Review & Evaluation Cache

enterReview() in ui.js saves the current game state as reviewBaseState and builds a snapshot array reviewStates for each move. Each time the user navigates to a new step, requestEngineEval() requests an engine eval, and the result is cached in _reviewEvalCache (from v1.0.4 Rev18 onward there is no cap — the previous LRU 200-entry cap has been removed to support cross-session review with the 📚 PGN cache manager).

Analyze All reviewAnalyzeAll() sends go depth 22 step by step in sequence, using a callback-driven mechanism to advance to the next step after each eval completes, avoiding concurrent requests that would confuse the engine. The cache is preserved after exiting review and is only cleared when a new game starts.

v1.0.4 Rev17 adds a persistence layer: the review eval cache is now persisted via AndroidBridge.persistentSet/persistentGet (SharedPreferences) to /data/data/com.Regalia/shared_prefs/RegaliaEngine.xml, avoiding cleanup by Xiaomi HyperOS 3 cache cleaner. The JS side uses a double-write + fallback-read pattern: writes go to both localStorage and persistent storage; reads first try localStorage (fast path), and on failure fall back to persistent storage (survival guarantee) and rewrite localStorage.

ui.js — Move classification algorithm function _classifyMove(evalDelta,isMoverWhite){ const isGood=isMoverWhite? (evalDelta>=0):(evalDelta<=0); const absD=Math.abs(evalDelta); if(absD>=300){ if(isGood) return{cls:'brilliant',label:'Brilliant',color:'#00cfff'}; return{cls:'blunder',label:'Blunder',color:'#c0392b'}; } if(absD>=150){ if(isGood) return{cls:'great',label:'Great',color:'#27ae60'}; return{cls:'mistake',label:'Mistake',color:'#e67e22'}; } if(absD>=50){ if(isGood) return{cls:'good',label:'Good',color:'#a0c060'}; return{cls:'inaccuracy',label:'Inaccuracy',color:'#f0c040'}; } return{cls:'book',label:'Standard',color:'var(--muted)'}; }
Chapter 10
Opening Library

Includes a built-in ECO opening library (A00-E99, 500 variations) with search, family filter, opening identification, and recommendations. Note: the ECO opening library is not used in Chess960 mode (no fixed opening theory).

Opening Identification Card

From v1.0.1, the ECO opening identification card and opening recommendation bar are shown only in the following cases:

  • Free opening mode: when no specific opening is selected, the ECO code is auto-identified based on the current position
  • Custom ECO opening: when a built-in ECO opening is selected in New Game Settings, the ECO info of the current opening is shown

When a game is started via FEN import or setup mode, the ECO opening identification and recommendation are not shown, avoiding misleading hints for non-standard openings.

ECO Opening Identification Card
📖 ECO Identification
C42 Petrov's Defense
Petrov family

ECO tag uses a purple gradient background linear-gradient(145deg,#8e44ad,#6c3483) + gold text #ffd700, border 1px solid rgba(255,215,0,.3).

Implementation Details: ECO Opening Library

eco-data.js exports the ECO_DATA array (500 opening records) and the ECO_BY_FAMILY family grouping map. During play, ui.js prefix-matches the current move sequence against the ECO data; on success it shows the identification card and recommendation bar in the side panel.

v1.0.4 Rev32 fix: when "AI prefers ECO opening moves" is enabled, after 3 consecutive AI moves from the opening book, _aiRetryCount no longer accumulates — book-provided moves reset _aiRetryCount=0, avoiding false "AI failed 3 times" detection that would stop the AI from moving.

eco-data.js — Data Structure const ECO_DATA=[ {id:'A00',name:'Polish Opening/Sokolsky Opening', moves:'b4',family:'Polish Opening'}, {id:'A01',name:'Nimzowitsch-Larsen Attack', moves:'b3',family:'Nimzowitsch-Larsen Attack'}, // ... 500 entries total ]; const ECO_BY_FAMILY={ 'Polish Opening':['A00'], 'Sicilian Defense':['B20','B21',...,'B99'], // ... };

AI Hint

When MultiPV > 1, multi-line display: ⭐ first line is gold #ffd700, subsequent lines are gray var(--muted). From v1.0.1, moves in multi-line analysis are shown in PGN Standard Algebraic Notation (SAN) format, not the engine's raw UCI format. For example Nf3 e5 d4 rather than g1f3 e7e5 d2d4.

🔮 Ponder Hint

When Ponder is enabled in engine config, the engine continues analyzing the opponent's possible replies after the AI makes a move. Ponder info is shown in different areas depending on the current state:

Display LocationTrigger ConditionDisplay Content
AI Opponent Bar Row 3 (right-aligned)Player's turn, AI Hint not in use🔮 Opponent pondered move (SAN, e.g. e5) + search depth, node count, eval change
AI Hint BarPlayer's turn, AI Hint in use🔮 Ponder search depth, node count, speed, eval change + pondered move (SAN, e.g. e5)
Tip: Ponder info is shown only after the AI moves and while the player is thinking. When the AI is thinking or hint-loading, the AI Opponent Bar's Ponder info is auto-hidden to avoid distraction. If the player makes the engine-predicted reply, the engine immediately reuses the already-analyzed result (Ponder Hit), achieving near-zero latency for the next response.
Conditional display: The pondered move in the AI Hint bar is shown in two scenarios: (1) When the user requests a hint (💡 AI Hint), if the engine's bestmove is followed by ponder info, the hint text shows both the recommended move and the pondered move (format: 🔦 Hint: Nf3 🔮 Ponder: e5); (2) AI Opponent Bar row 3 shows ponder info when the engine's background Ponder search is active. When there is no ponder info, no Ponder-related content is shown, keeping the UI clean.

🌐 Chinese/English Language Switching

v1.0.1 adds a global Chinese/English switching feature. Tap the toggle button on the left of the eval bar (outside the eval bar) to switch language mode:

Current ModeButtonSwitches To

After switching to English mode, all user-visible text is shown in English, including: toolbar button text, AI Opponent bar and player bar labels, side-panel card titles, all New Game dialog options, all Engine Configuration dialog labels and descriptions, game-end prompts, Toast notifications, About page info, and the Foreground Service Notification.

Auto-detect: On first launch, the app selects the interface language based on the Android system language: Chinese system defaults to Chinese mode; other languages default to English mode. The language preference is then saved to local storage; once manually switched, it no longer auto-changes.
v1.0.4 Rev17 persistence: The language preference is now persisted via SharedPreferences (kv_Regalia_lang), avoiding cleanup by HyperOS 3 cache cleaner. The JS side uses a double-write + fallback-read pattern.

Square Control Information

With 🌈 enabled, a 📍 Control Info card is shown: own side #4a90d9, opponent #c0392b. The piece names (PN) in the control info panel support i18n: Chinese mode shows Chinese piece names (King, Queen, Rook, Bishop, Knight, Pawn), English mode shows English abbreviations (K, Q, R, B, N, P), consistent with the interface language setting.

Chess Principles

The top 10 chess principles are organized under four strategic dimensions and switch automatically with the interface language: Chinese mode shows Chinese principles, English mode shows English principles.

English Chess Principles

I. Three Golden Opening Rules (Foundation of Victory)

  1. Center Control: Seize center squares (d4, d5, e4, e5) early to maximize piece efficiency and restrict the opponent's development
  2. Piece Development: Develop minor pieces (Knights, Bishops) quickly into battle; avoid moving the same piece twice; castle early to safeguard the King
  3. King Safety: Do not push kingside pawns (f, g, h) prematurely; castle early to tuck the King behind the pawn shield

II. Pawn Structure & Space Management (Soul of Positional Play)

  1. Pawn Structure: Avoid isolated, doubled, and backward pawns; maintain a mutually protective pawn chain to secure your position
  2. Space Advantage: Advance your pawn chain to squeeze the opponent's space, causing their pieces to interfere with each other
  3. Passed Pawns: Create and advance passed pawns (especially connected passed pawns) — they are the ultimate weapon in the middlegame and endgame

III. Piece Play & Coordination (Tactical Edge)

  1. Piece Coordination: Ensure pieces support each other and attack the same target; avoid sending a single piece deep without backup
  2. Open Files: Quickly occupy open and semi-open files with Rooks (or doubled Rooks) to invade the opponent's back rank

IV. Middlegame Strategy & Judgment (Advanced Wisdom)

  1. Flank Breakthrough: When the center is locked, launch a pawn break on the flank where your pawn chain points
  2. Exchange Principle: Simplify into a winning endgame when ahead; keep the position complex to find counterplay when behind

Implementation Details: Syzygy Endgame Tablebase

tablebase.js requests the Lichess Tablebase API (https://tablebase.lichess.ovh/standard) via fetch(), returning JSON endgame data. Query results are cached by FEN in _tbCache (Map) to avoid duplicate requests.

tablebase.js — Endgame tablebase query async function queryTablebase(fen){ const url='https://tablebase.lichess.ovh/standard?fen=' +encodeURIComponent(fen); const resp=await fetch(url); const data=await resp.json(); _tbCache.set(fen,data); // cache result return data; }

Implementation Details: Cache Backend Storage

Cache files are stored in the app's private directory /data/data/com.Regalia/files/pgn_cache/<name>.pgn. This directory is in the same app-private data area as SharedPreferences (/data/data/com.Regalia/shared_prefs/), not cleared by Xiaomi HyperOS 3 cache cleaner — only the app itself or the user's "Clear Data" action (not "Clear Cache") can delete it.

StockfishNative.java — PGN cache Java interface @JavascriptInterface public String listPGNCaches() { // Returns JSON: [{name, size, mtime}, ...] sorted by mtime desc File dir = new File(context.getFilesDir(), "pgn_cache"); File[] files = dir.listFiles(); // ... build and return JSON array ... } @JavascriptInterface public boolean savePGNCache(String name, String pgn) { String safe = _sanitizeCacheName(name); // strip path separators + control chars File file = new File(_pgnCacheDir(), safe + ".pgn"); // write UTF-8 text ... } @JavascriptInterface public String getPGNCache(String name) { /* read PGN text */ } @JavascriptInterface public int deletePGNCaches(String namesJson) { // Accepts JSON string array, batch deletes, returns count }

JS side calls the above methods via AndroidBridge.listPGNCaches/savePGNCache/getPGNCache/deletePGNCaches. All calls are wrapped in try/catch to ensure no crash if very old WebViews do not support the Java interface.

Cross-session review: Combined with the Rev17 SharedPreferences persistence layer, the cache manager enables a complete cross-session review workflow: 1) During a review, tap 📚 → "Save current PGN to cache" → name and save; 2) Exit the app, reboot the phone, run cache-cleaner — none of these clear the cache; 3) Next time you open the app → enter review → tap 📚 → tap a cache entry → one-tap import, instantly restoring the game.
Chapter 12
Fischer Random Chess (Chess960)

Fischer Random Chess (also called Chess960 / FR Chess) was proposed by former world champion Bobby Fischer in 1996, with the goal of eliminating the advantage of opening-theory memorization and forcing players to demonstrate practical creativity from move one. The core innovation: the back-rank pieces' starting position is randomly chosen from 960 legal arrangements, while preserving symmetry between the two sides and preserving the standard final squares of castling (King ends on g1/c1, Rook ends on f1/d1).

Naming of the 960 Start Positions

Each legal start position is identified by an SP-ID (Starting Position Identifier) numbered 0..959. SP-ID 518 is the standard chess start position (RNBQKBNR), used for regression testing and comparison.

SP-IDWhite Back-Rank ArrangementNotes
0BBQNNRKROne of the leftmost arrangements with bishops on opposite colors
518RNBQKBNRStandard chess start position (regression baseline)
959RKRNNQBBThe highest-numbered arrangement

Constraints on Legal Start Positions

A legal Chess960 start position must satisfy the following four rules (yielding 960 arrangements):

  • Bishops on opposite colors: the two bishops must be on a light and a dark square (avoiding same-color bishops)
  • King between rooks: the King must be between the two rooks (not at the leftmost or rightmost)
  • Symmetry: Black's back-rank arrangement mirrors White's (e.g. White BBQNNRKR ↔ Black bbqnnrkr)
  • Piece totals: each side has exactly 1 King, 1 Queen, 2 Rooks, 2 Bishops, 2 Knights on the back rank

SP-ID Selection Methods

When Chess960 is enabled in the New Game dialog, the "Fischer Random Chess" settings area appears below, offering three ways to choose an SP-ID:

  1. 🎲 Random button: uniformly random SP-ID from 0..959 (recommended, the purest Chess960 experience)
  2. Manual input: enter an integer 0..959 in the text box
  3. Preview: the back-rank piece diagram shows the starting arrangement for the current SP-ID in real time (SP-ID 518 shows ♖ ♘ ♗ ♕ ♔ ♗ ♘ ♖)

Chess960 Castling Rules v1.0.4 Rev34 Fix

Chess960 castling is the part most confusing for beginners. The core principle: after castling, the King and Rook final squares are exactly the same as in standard chess — kingside (O-O) King ends on g1, Rook ends on f1; queenside (O-O-O) King ends on c1, Rook ends on d1. But the starting positions vary by SP-ID.

ItemStandard ChessChess960
King start columnFixed e1 (column 4)SP-ID-decided (any column b1-g1)
Kingside Rook start columnFixed h1 (column 7)SP-ID-decided (nearest rook to the King's right)
Queenside Rook start columnFixed a1 (column 0)SP-ID-decided (nearest rook to the King's left)
King end squareg1 / c1g1 / c1 (same as standard)
Rook end squaref1 / d1f1 / d1 (same as standard)

Castling Legality Conditions

  1. Neither King nor Rook has moved (castling right intact)
  2. No pieces between King and Rook (clear path)
  3. The King's current square is not in check (cannot castle out of check)
  4. All squares on the King's castling path are not attacked by the opponent (King cannot "pass through" attacked squares)
  5. The King's destination square is not attacked by the opponent (cannot "land in" a checked square)
  6. Rev34 critical fix: in the union of the King path and the Rook path, every square must be empty except for the King's and Rook's respective starting squares — this is a Chess960-specific constraint because the King and Rook may start close together (e.g. King on b1, Rook on c1), and the King's path (b1→g1) passes through d1, e1, f1 etc. which may be occupied by other pieces
Rev34 critical bug fix: The original implementation only checked whether squares between King and Rook were empty, but did not check whether the King's destination and the Rook's destination had other pieces. In Chess960 the King and Rook may start close (e.g. King on b1, Rook on c1), and the King's path (b1→g1) extends far beyond the Rook's position — passing through d1, e1, f1 etc. which may be occupied. makeMv() would directly overwrite those squares, effectively destroying own pieces. The fix now checks the union of the King path and the Rook path.

Shredder-FEN Castling Rights Encoding

Chess960 FEN uses the Shredder-FEN format for castling rights (uppercase letters indicate White rook columns, lowercase letters indicate Black rook columns), unlike the standard FEN KQkq encoding:

FormatExampleNotes
Standard FENrnbqkbnr/pppppppp/8/8/8/8/PPPPPPPP/RNBQKBNR w KQkq - 0 1KQkq = White kingside/queenside + Black kingside/queenside castling rights
Shredder-FENrnbqkbnr/pppppppp/8/8/8/8/PPPPPPPP/RNBQKBNR w HAha - 0 1HAha = castling rights for White h1+a1 rooks + Black h8+a8 rooks (encoded by column letter)
SP-ID 518 Shredder-FENrnbqkbnr/pppppppp/8/8/8/8/PPPPPPPP/RNBQKBNR w HAha - 0 1Fully equivalent to standard chess (H/A rooks on h1/a1, equivalent to KQ)

PGN Header Tag Specification

Chess960 game PGN must include the following header tags to identify the variant:

Chess960 PGN Header Tag Example [Event "Casual Game"] [Site "Regalia"] [Date "2026.06.25"] [Round "1"] [White "Player"] [Black "AI Opponent Lv.4"] [Result "1-0"] [Variant "Chess960"] # Required: identifies Chess960 variant [SetUp "1"] # Required: identifies non-standard start position [FEN "rnbkrqnq/pppppppp/8/8/8/8/PPPPPPPP/RNBKRQNQ w HAah - 0 1"] # Shredder-FEN 1. d4 d5 2. Nf3 Nf6 ... 1-0

PGN import recognizes all of these Variant aliases: [Variant "Chess960"], [Variant "Fischerandom"], [Variant "Fischer Random"], [Variant "FRC"], and auto-derives the SP-ID.

Implementation Details: Chess960 Module Architecture

v1.0.4 adds the chess960.js module, encapsulating all Chess960 rule logic:

  • SP-ID generator: generates the corresponding legal start arrangement from 0..959
  • Shredder-FEN encode/decode: converts castling-rights field between HAah format and internal state
  • isChess960CastlingLegal(board, from, to): checks Chess960 castling legality (including Rev34 critical fix — King path ∪ Rook path empty check)
  • chess960CastlingRookMove(board, kingFrom, kingTo): computes Rook start/end from King start/end
  • findCastlingRooks(board, kingRow): scans the back rank to find the nearest two rooks on each side of the King

These functions hook into the gameVariant==='chess960' branches of pseudoMoves(), makeMv(), makeMvInPlace() in game-logic.js, including rookFrom!==rookTo guards and Chess960 castling-rights updates.

chess960.js — Castling legality check function isChess960CastlingLegal(state, kingFrom, kingTo) { // 1. Neither King nor Rook has moved (castling right) if (!hasCastlingRight(state, kingFrom.color, side)) return false; // 2. King is not currently in check if (isSquareAttacked(state, kingFrom, oppColor)) return false; // 3. Compute union of King path + Rook path (Rev34 fix) const rookFrom = findCastlingRook(state, kingFrom, side); const rookTo = chess960CastlingRookMove(kingFrom, kingTo); const path = new Set(); // King path for (let c = Math.min(kingFrom.col, kingTo.col); c <= Math.max(kingFrom.col, kingTo.col); c++) path.add(kingFrom.row + ',' + c); // Rook path for (let c = Math.min(rookFrom.col, rookTo.col); c <= Math.max(rookFrom.col, rookTo.col); c++) path.add(rookFrom.row + ',' + c); // 4. Every square in the path must be empty except for King and Rook start squares for (const sq of path) { if (sq === kingFrom.row+','+kingFrom.col) continue; if (sq === rookFrom.row+','+rookFrom.col) continue; const [r,c] = sq.split(',').map(Number); if (state.board[r][c]) return false; } // 5. Every square on the King path must not be attacked by opponent for (const sq of kingPath(state, kingFrom, kingTo)) if (isSquareAttacked(state, sq, oppColor)) return false; return true; }

UCI_Chess960 Engine Option

In Chess960 mode, AndroidBridge.setChess960Mode(true) calls Stockfish's setoption name UCI_Chess960 value true option. The engine (auto-)restart re-applies the 960 mode, avoiding setting loss on crash recovery. This option must be set after uciok and before ucinewgame.

Mutual-exclusion rule: Chess960 and the ECO opening book are mutually exclusive — enabling Chess960 grays out the ECO toggle, and vice versa. Reason: Chess960 has no fixed opening theory, and ECO codes (A00-E99) only apply to the standard chess start position.
Chapter 13
Time Control

Time Control is one of the core features added in v1.0.4. The New Game Settings dialog adds a "Time Control" section with a dropdown for 5 time modes. With time control enabled, the game UI shows both clocks (live countdown); when remaining time < 30 seconds, the clock turns red as a warning; flag-fall ends the game.

5 Time Modes

ModeIdentifierRuleTypical TimeControl Header
UntimedUntimedNo clock constraint; player may think as long as desiredNo [TimeControl] header
Sudden DeathSudden DeathFixed total time; running out loses; per-move actual time is deducted"1800" (30 minutes)
Fischer IncrementFischer IncrementBase total time + per-move increment; each move adds the increment seconds after the move"300+3" (5 minutes + 3 seconds per move)
Bronstein DelayBronstein DelayPer-move delay window; no deduction during delay window; actual time deducted after delay window"1800+10d" (30 minutes + 10 second delay)
US DelayUS DelayLike Bronstein but the delay window is "use-it-or-lose-it" — delay starts being deducted from total time at the start of the move; unused delay time is not refunded"1800+5D" (30 minutes + 5 second US delay)

Clock UI Display

With time control enabled, the game UI shows both clocks (live countdown) in the AI Opponent Bar row 1 and the player info bar:

Time Control Clock UI
🤖 AI Opponent Lv.4 ⏱ 05:23
⏳ Thinking
♔ Player ⏱ 00:18
Your turn

Remaining time < 30s turns red as warning; flag-fall ends the game

Stockfish 18 Time Management UCI Command v1.0.4 Rev35

In time control mode, AI moves now use the go wtime <ms> btime <ms> winc <ms> binc <ms> UCI command, letting Stockfish 18 manage its own time allocation (think longer in critical positions, shorter in simple ones), instead of fixed movetime. A new AndroidBridge.engineGoTimed() bridge method is added.

Implementation Details: 5 Time Modes Deduction Rules

Each time mode has its own deduction logic, all managed via the global gameClocks object:

ui.js — Time control deduction rules (pseudo-code) function applyMoveTimeControl(color, moveDurationMs) { const clk = gameClocks[color]; switch (timeControlMode) { case 'untimed': // No-op break; case 'sudden_death': // Deduct actual time per move clk.remaining -= moveDurationMs; break; case 'fischer': // Add increment after each move clk.remaining -= moveDurationMs; clk.remaining += incrementMs; break; case 'bronstein': // No deduction during delay window; actual time deducted after delay window if (moveDurationMs <= delayMs) { // Entire move within delay window — no deduction } else { clk.remaining -= (moveDurationMs - delayMs); } break; case 'us_delay': // Delay window "use-it-or-lose-it" — delay starts being deducted from total time at start; // unused delay time is not refunded const effective = Math.max(0, moveDurationMs - delayMs); clk.remaining -= effective; break; } // Flag-fall detection if (clk.remaining <= 0) { clk.remaining = 0; _onGameClockExpired(color); } }

Clock-Expiry Handling v1.0.4 Rev35

Rev35 fixes a serious bug where clock expiry did not send a stop command. The original _onGameClockExpired() only set the gameOver state, without sending a stop command to the engine. The engine continued searching based on its internal wtime estimate, potentially far exceeding the GUI's 0-second mark. The fix: _onGameClockExpired() now calls AndroidBridge.engineStop() to immediately hard-stop the engine, and clears isAIThinking and the AI safety timer.

Rev35 critical fix: JS calls engineGoTimed() while measuring the clock, but by the time the "go" command is actually sent (after stopAndWaitForBestmove + ucinewgame + readyok waits, up to 6 seconds), the real clock has already decreased. The engine over-allocates search time based on the stale (too-large) wtime. Fix: engineGoTimed() now records the JS call timestamp and deducts the setup overhead from wtime/btime before sending "go", plus a safety margin (engineMoveOverhead, min 50ms) to ensure the engine's bestmove returns before the GUI clock hits zero.

Ponder Time Control Compliance v1.0.4 Rev31

The original startPonder() only sent "go ponder" without time parameters — violating the UCI spec. The UCI spec requires go ponder to include wtime/btime/winc/binc parameters so the engine can switch to normal timed search on receiving ponderhit. Without time parameters, either: (a) the engine searches indefinitely on ponderhit (no time pressure), or (b) the engine instantly returns bestmove on ponderhit (panic mode) — both abnormal for time control. Rev31 fix: startPonder() takes 4 new time parameters; JS passes the current gameClocks values. For non-time-control games, all-zeros are passed, and Java detects this and sends "go ponder" (without time parameters).

PGN TimeControl Header

With time control enabled, PGN export includes a [TimeControl "..."] header (e.g. "300+3") and per-move [%clk HH:MM:SS] annotations. Without time control, PGN comments use [%emt HH:MM:SS] (per-move elapsed time) — the "Elapsed Move Time" tag defined in PGN spec §10.2.7.

Time Control PGN Export Example [Event "Casual Game"] [Site "Regalia"] [Date "2026.06.25"] [Round "1"] [White "Player"] [Black "AI Opponent Lv.4"] [Result "1-0"] [TimeControl "300+3"] # 5 minutes + 3 seconds per move increment 1. e4 {[%clk 00:05:03]} e5 {[%clk 00:05:02]} 2. Nf3 {[%clk 00:05:05]} Nc6 {[%clk 00:05:04]} 1-0
Non-time-control PGN Export Example ([%emt] tag) [Event "Casual Game"] [Site "Regalia"] [Date "2026.06.25"] [Round "1"] [White "Player"] [Black "AI Opponent Lv.4"] [Result "1-0"] 1. e4 {[%emt 0:00:02]} e5 {[%emt 0:00:03]} 2. Nf3 {[%emt 0:00:05]} Nc6 {[%emt 0:00:04]} 1-0

TimeControl Header Parse & Format

pgn-standard.js supports parsing and formatting all 6 TimeControl formats:

FormatExampleDescription
Sudden death"1800"Base time only (seconds), no increment
Fischer increment"300+3"Base + increment (seconds)
Bronstein delay"1800+10d"Base + delay (seconds, d suffix)
US delay"1800+5D"Base + delay (seconds, D suffix)
Staged"40/7200+30"40 moves in 7200 seconds + 30 seconds per move increment
Hourglass"*180"180-second hourglass (rarely used)
Chapter 14
PGN Import & Export

v1.0.4 introduces the pgn-standard.js module, implementing strict 1994-PGN-spec encoding and tolerant decoding. This chapter details the complete PGN import/export workflow, spec compliance, and tolerance strategy.

PGN Spec Compliance

ItemSpec RequirementRegalia Implementation
Seven Tag RosterMust have Event/Site/Date/Round/White/Black/ResultExport always contains the full Seven Tag Roster
Movetext wrapping~78-column wrappingExport wraps at 78 columns
Result markerLast token must be 1-0 / 0-1 / 1/2-1/2 / *Always the last token
Tag value escaping\ → \\, " → \", forced single-lineStrict escaping
SAN notationDisambiguation, castling O-O/O-O-O, promotion =Q/=R/=B/=N, check +/checkmate #Full SAN support
NAG numeric glyphs$1-$6 move quality, $10-$18 position evaluationNAG_MAP / nagToSymbol two-way conversion
Visual annotations[%csl ...] square highlight, [%cal ...] arrowsformatCslTag / formatCalTag / parseCslTag / parseCalTag
Evaluation annotations[%eval ...] Lichess/Chessbase standardformatEvalTag embeds eval data
Clock annotations[%clk HH:MM:SS] standard clock formatAuto-generated in time-control mode
Elapsed-time annotations[%emt HH:MM:SS] per-move elapsed timeAuto-generated in non-time-control mode
Variant support[Variant "..."] header tagSupports Chess960 / Fischerandom / Fischer Random / FRC
Non-standard start[SetUp "1"] + [FEN "..."] header tagsFEN uses Shredder castling-rights format

PGN Import

Regalia supports importing PGN (Portable Game Notation) game records via the 🗃️ Import button, fully restoring the game and showing variations in the move record. PGN import offers three methods:

  • Paste FEN: paste a FEN string from the clipboard to quickly restore any position. Useful for position codes copied from other chess apps or websites
  • Paste PGN: paste complete PGN game text from the clipboard. Supports standard PGN format including header tags (e.g. [FEN "..."]), moves, comments, and variations
  • 📂 Select PGN File: select a .pgn file from the device via the Android SAF file picker. Auto-detects FEN and PGN format

PGN Variation Support

Variations in imported PGN game records (i.e. moves inside parentheses, RAV — Recursive Annotation Variation) are automatically displayed in the move record as 🌿 lines, using the same display format as engine analysis lines. Variations are shown only as text move sequences and do not trigger engine evaluation or display on the board, keeping the UI clean and clear.

v1.0.2 fix: Fixed the PGN variation "incomplete fragment" issue. Previously, when a variation's middle SAN was non-standard (missing disambiguation, non-standard suffix, etc.), the variation continuation loop would break on the first unparseable token, discarding all subsequent moves from that token onward — showing up as "🌿 variation only displays the first half". v1.0.2 changes this to continue (skipping only that token and continuing to parse subsequent moves), and each token uniformly applies moveAlg tolerant matching.

PGN Parsing Flow

The PGN import parsing flow is carefully designed to ensure compatibility with various PGN formats:

  • Automatically removes BOM (byte-order mark) and header tags
  • Extracts FEN header (if present) to restore non-standard start positions
  • Removes comments (curly-brace content) and NAG symbols ($1, $2, etc.)
  • Before removing variation content, extracts and saves variations, associating them with the corresponding main move
  • Validates each move's legality, skipping unrecognizable moves instead of aborting
  • v1.0.1 Recursive variation-tree parsing: each ( opens a new variation frame attached to the "last move" in the parent context. Nested ( attaches to the correct move in the parent variation (not the main-line move), per PGN spec §8.2.5
  • v1.0.1 Triple-fallback variation first-token matching: Type A (same-side alternative) → Type A moveAlg fuzzy match → Type B (opponent reply) → Type B moveAlg fuzzy match. Handles non-standard SAN (missing disambiguator, +/# suffix, etc.)
  • v1.0.1 mainTokenIdx index tracking: even if a main-line move fails to parse and is skipped, subsequent variations still correctly associate with the corresponding main move
  • v1.0.1 Diagnostic logging: when a variation's first token fails to match, console.warn is output for troubleshooting PGN input issues

PGN Export (Seven Tag Roster)

Exported PGN always contains the Seven Tag Roster:

pgn-standard.js — Seven Tag Roster const SEVEN_TAG_ROSTER = [ 'Event', # Event name 'Site', # Site location 'Date', # Date YYYY.MM.DD 'Round', # Round 'White', # White player name (AI opponent includes difficulty tier suffix, e.g. "AI Opponent Lv.4") 'Black', # Black player name 'Result' # Result: 1-0 / 0-1 / 1/2-1/2 / * ];

NAG Numeric Glyph System

NAG (Numeric Annotation Glyphs) are numeric annotation symbols defined by the PGN spec, used to mark move quality and position evaluation:

NAGSymbolMeaningDescription
$1!Good moveGood move
$2?MistakeMistake
$3!!BrilliantBrilliant move
$4??BlunderBlunder
$5!?InterestingInteresting move
$6?!DubiousDubious move
$10=EqualEqual position
$11⩲White slightly betterWhite slightly better
$12⩱Black slightly betterBlack slightly better
$13±White clearly betterWhite clearly better
$14∓Black clearly betterBlack clearly better
$15+−White winningWhite winning
$16−+Black winningBlack winning

Visual Annotations ([%csl] / [%cal])

Visual annotations follow the Lichess/Chessbase de-facto standard format. Regalia auto-selects and caches per-move visual annotations. The v1.0.4 Rev48 complete 4-color arrow semantics are (further extended in v1.0.5 Rev54):

ColorAbbrSquare highlight [%csl] usageArrow [%cal] usage
Blue (B)BPlayer's net-control strong squaresMulti-threat: one side's piece simultaneously threatens multiple (>1) enemy pieces (arrows from threatening piece to each threatened piece). Rev54 extension: when the mover actively moves ANY piece into a threatened square, causing the other side to have any piece with 2+ threats on mover pieces, the corresponding blue arrows are priority-boosted (ensuring visibility).
Red (R)RAI opponent's net-control strong squaresCheck path (checker → checked king)
Yellow (Y)YSquares with high total control (both sides combined) (Rev54: yellow square style changed to rounded-rectangle inset overlay, top layer, with four-corner gaps)Queen threat (arrow from threatening piece to queen's square). Rev53 bidirectional: includes enemy's threats to mover's queen. Rev54 extension: when the mover actively moves their queen into a threatened square, the corresponding yellow arrows are priority-boosted (ensuring visibility).
Green (G)GCenter-area squares with no control from either sideEscape path (checked king position → escape square)

Rev48 addition: Blue arrows (multi-threat) and Yellow arrows (queen threat). Display order from left to right is: Blue, Red, Yellow, Green — vertically aligned with the same-color square cells (per user spec).

Rev54 addition (visual separation): Each of the four arrow colors now has a FIXED diagonal offset applied to BOTH start and end (so arrow direction is preserved), making overlapping arrows of different colors visually separable: Blue → Upper-Left, Yellow → Lower-Left, Red → Upper-Right, Green → Lower-Right. Offset magnitude is ~12% of cell size. The existing same-color multi-arrow angular fan (Rev49) is preserved on top of this per-color offset.

Review Board Visual Annotation Overlay v1.0.4 Rev48

When the control heatmap (🌗/🌈) is OFF, the review board displays the current move's [%csl]/[%cal] annotations:

  • Square highlights use CSS box-shadow inset (3px width, matching the main board's last-move hint)
  • Arrows drawn in an SVG overlay layer above the board (same style as the main board's heatmap-on selected-square arrows: 4px stroke, round linecap, 0.85 opacity, per-color arrowhead markers)
  • Data source: for just-played games, the cached selection results; for imported PGNs, the [%csl]/[%cal] from comments (Rev48 fix: now fully extracted at import time, no longer lost)

Statistics Page Conditional Display v1.0.4 Rev48

  • PGN without [%csl]/[%cal] → visual annotations section is hidden

Post-Import Behavior

After PGN import completes, the app performs the following operations:

  • The move record syncs to show all imported moves and variations
  • The board shows the final position of the game
  • Automatically requests engine evaluation of the current position
  • Does not auto-trigger AI moves; the user can freely browse or start a new game
  • Supports review mode for browsing the imported game
  • v1.0.1 Undo works correctly: after import, you can step-undo back to White's first move and clear the move record (fixes the v1.0.0 undo failure caused by an incorrect stateHistory snapshot ordering)

Implementation Details: Tolerant Parsing

PGN parser (tolerant mode):

  • Auto-fixes nested {} comments (spec violation)
  • Auto-closes unclosed comments
  • Normalizes 0-0 numeric zeros to O-O letter O (Chessbase compatibility)
  • Skips invalid SAN instead of failing the whole parse
  • Defaults missing Result to *
  • Silently tolerates missing [SetUp "1"]

v1.0.4 Rev16 fix: PGN comment-tag preservation. The header-tag stripping regex in parseStandardPGN changed from /\[[^\]]*\]/g to /^\[[^\]]*\]/gm (line-anchored), no longer incorrectly removing in-comment [%csl]/[%cal]/[%emt]/[%clk]/[%eval] tags.

pgn-standard.js — Tolerant regex fix // Old version (incorrectly removed in-comment [%csl] / [%cal] etc.) const text = pgn.replace(/\[[^\]]*\]/g, ''); // v1.0.4 Rev16 fix (line-anchored, only strips PGN header [Tag "Value"] tags) const text = pgn.replace(/^\[[^\]]*\]/gm, '');

Chapter 15
Statistics Page

The Statistics page (StatsActivity + stats.html) is a full-screen WebView Activity, opened via the 📊 button on the main UI move-record card or the 📊 button on the review toolbar. It is independent of the main-game WebView, ships with a minimal JS bridge, and isolates heavy PGN parsing logic from the main game. Heavy compute tasks (heatmap stats etc.) are delegated to a Web Worker via worker-pool.js.

Page Layout

The Statistics page top-to-bottom layout:

  1. Top title bar: left side "📊 Statistics" title, right side four buttons: 💾HTML (export entire page as HTML file), 🗃️ Import (paste PGN or select PGN file), 🗂️ Review (close stats page and notify main UI to enter review mode), Back.
  2. Selection hint banner (v1.0.3 NEW): shown only when the user selects a move. Main-line selection shows a gold banner ("Move N selected"), variation selection shows a blue banner ("Variation move N selected (replaced main-line move N)"), making clear which position the stats below correspond to.
  3. PGN text panel: fully renders the current game's PGN text, including move numbers, moves (♔/♚ etc. piece symbols styled like the main board), comments {} (dark-blue italic), variations () (gray), NAGs ($1 etc., light blue), result (1-0/0-1/1/2-1/2/*, gold bold). From v1.0.3, variation moves are also clickable.
  4. Position FEN panel (v1.0.3 NEW): below the PGN text panel. Monospace font shows the FEN of the position immediately after the currently selected move (auto-generated in the background via stateToFEN()). "Copy" button is in the lower-right corner (independent row, flexbox right-aligned) to avoid overlap with FEN text. When no move is selected, the initial position FEN + hint text is shown.
  5. Game metadata: table showing [Event], [Site], [Date], [Round], [White], [Black], [Result], [TimeControl] header tag content.
  6. Position statistics: total moves, final material, material difference.
  7. Move quality: White/Black accuracy (Chess.com-style CPL formula), average CPL, 6-tier classification counts (Brilliant/Best/Good/Inaccuracy/Mistake/Blunder). Shown only when eval data is available.
  8. Evaluation trend chart: SVG line chart, horizontal axis = move number, vertical axis = eval value (White's perspective, in centipawns).
  9. Material balance chart: SVG line chart, horizontal axis = move number, vertical axis = White-Black material difference.
  10. Piece activity: capture count, check count, castling count, promotion count; per-piece-type (Pawn/Knight/Bishop/Rook/Queen/King) move-count table for both White and Black.
  11. Phase analysis: phase determined by non-pawn non-king piece count on the board (Opening >8, Middlegame 4-8, Endgame <4), with per-phase ply counts.
  12. Key turning points: top 10 moves by eval change magnitude (with move number, eval delta, classification label).
  13. Time management (v1.0.3 upgrade): see 15.3.
  14. Opening analysis: first 8 moves sequence, White/Black minor-piece (Knight/Bishop) development count.
  15. Pawn structure: doubled/isolated/passed pawn counts (White and Black separately).
  16. Center control: White/Black move counts landing on center squares (d4/e4/d5/e5).
  17. King safety: White/Black check counts, King move counts.
  18. Position complexity: eval volatility (standard deviation), lead-conversion count, White/Black advantage move counts.
  19. Heatmap control statistics (v1.0.4 NEW): 8×8 average-control heatmap, each square showing (White avg / Black avg) attacker count, with HSL background indicating net control.
  20. Visual annotations (v1.0.4 NEW): NAG distribution, per-color arrow/square counts.

Selecting a Move for Per-Position Stats

Tap any move in the PGN text panel (main-line or variation), and all the statistics modules below (position statistics, move quality, eval trend chart, material balance chart, piece activity, phase analysis, key turning points, time management, opening analysis, pawn structure, center control, king safety, position complexity) automatically recompute, including only the move sequence up to that move. Tap the same move again to deselect and restore global statistics.
