🆕 v1.0.7 Phase 4 Additions (Chess960 / X-FEN rule correctness overhaul, 2026.6.29)

This phase comprehensively reviews and fixes multiple rule-violating implementations in the app, based on the user-provided Chess960 / X-FEN specification reference. Core fixes include: the "king must have rooks on both sides" misjudgment, X-FEN Shredder castling notation sorting and mixed notation, the UCI_Chess960 "king-captures-rook" move format, and automatic UCI_Chess960 enabling for non-standard setup positions.

🐛 Bug Fixes (v1.0.7 Phase 4, Chess960 rule correctness)
  • "King must have rooks on both sides" misjudgment fixed — findCastlingRooks() previously REQUIRED both a kingside and a queenside rook to be present, returning null otherwise. This violates the Chess960 rule — the user-provided reference explicitly states: "during play (when executing castling): not required" — castling to one side only requires a rook on THAT side; the other side is irrelevant (the rook may have moved, been captured, or never existed in Setup mode). Fix: findCastlingRooks() now returns {king, kingside:col|null, queenside:col|null} where kingside/queenside can independently be null. A new findCastlingRookForSide(board, color, side) per-side lookup function is added; isChess960CastlingLegal() and chess960CastlingRookMove() now use it. Net effect: when the queenside rook has been captured, kingside castling is still legal; in Setup mode, marking only one side's rook still allows castling to that side.
  • X-FEN Shredder castling notation letter sorting fixed — toShredderCastling() previously emitted letters in a fixed "White-ks → White-qs → Black-ks → Black-qs" order, violating the X-FEN spec requirement that "letters must be sorted a→h (left-to-right)". For example, when White's queenside rook is on file b and kingside rook on file f, the correct output is "BF" but the old code emitted "FB". Fix: collect all (file, isWhite) pairs for valid castling rights, sort by file, then emit — guaranteeing X-FEN spec compliance.
  • X-FEN mixed notation support — parseShredderCastling() and fenToState() previously used a brittle regex to distinguish Shredder from standard KQkq, and could not handle X-FEN's allowed mixed notation (e.g. "KQah" — White uses KQ because its rooks are on a1/h1, Black uses Shredder "ah" because its rooks are elsewhere). Fix: each character is now parsed independently. K/Q/k/q are mapped to file h/a respectively (X-FEN backward-compatibility), A-H/a-h are taken as file letters directly, and then uniformly mapped to kingside/queenside based on the king's column. A defensive check is also added: if the indicated file has no same-color rook, the castling right is silently dropped (preventing downstream move-generation crashes).
  • UCI_Chess960 "king-captures-rook" move format support — When the engine has UCI_Chess960=true enabled, Stockfish represents castling as the king moving to the rook's source square (e.g. "e1h1" instead of "e1g1"), to disambiguate castling from a normal king move to g1/c1 in Chess960 where the king may already be close to g1/c1. The old uciToCoords() and _uciToSAN() parsed this literally as "king moves to h1" (a normal move), causing castling to fail. Fix: both functions now detect this case — if the from-square is a king, the to-square holds a same-color rook, and they are on the same rank, the move is recognized as Chess960 castling notation and the destination is rewritten to the king's standard castling destination (kingside col 6 = g1/g8, queenside col 2 = c1/c8). _uciToSimple() is also updated to ensure SAN short notation correctly outputs O-O/O-O-O.
  • Chess960 single-column castling detection fixed — _castleSide() previously required Math.abs(to.col-from.col)>=2 in its fallback detection, which prevented Chess960 castling where the king starts on f1 (col 5) and castles kingside to g1 (col 6) — a 1-column move. Fix: in Chess960 mode the minimum distance requirement is lowered to 1; in standard chess it remains 2 (in standard chess the king cannot legally be on f1 with castling rights still active, since moving the king clears all castling rights, so a 1-column move to g1 must be a normal king move, not castling).
  • Automatic UCI_Chess960 enabling for non-standard setup positions — _exitSetupImpl() now detects whether the setup result has any non-standard-position king or rook (king not on e1/e8, or a castling-rights rook not on a1/h1/a8/h8). If so, it automatically calls setChess960Mode(true) and sets gameVariant to 'chess960', ensuring the engine can correctly parse Shredder-FEN and Chess960 castling moves. If the setup result is a standard position, UCI_Chess960=false is kept for standard-FEN parsing compatibility.
  • generateFEN auto-outputs Shredder castling notation — generateFEN() now automatically outputs Shredder-FEN castling notation (file letters A-H/a-h) instead of standard KQkq when: (1) in explicit Chess960 mode (gameVariant==='chess960' or isChess960Mode() returns true); OR (2) the current position has any castling-rights king or rook on non-standard squares. Standard positions (king on e1/e8, rooks on a1/h1/a8/h8) continue to output KQkq for backward compatibility with v1.0.6 and earlier. This is a core X-FEN spec requirement — standard KQkq is ambiguous for non-standard positions (K implies rook on h1, but the rook may actually be on d1).
🎨 Design Style Continuity (v1.0.7 Phase 4)
  • All new UI text (error messages, button labels, etc.) uses the existing i18n bilingual framework (_i18n dictionary + T() function), with Chinese and English kept in sync. Error message style is consistent with the existing "⚠️ Cannot complete Setup" series (e.g. "Castle marker must share the square with a same-color rook", "En-passant marker must share the square with a pawn").
  • All new code follows the existing copyright notice and AI-GEN declaration style (AGPL v3 / GPL v3 per-module declarations; file-header comment format is identical to existing files).
🔗 X-FEN / UCI Integrity (v1.0.7 Phase 4)
  • X-FEN import: supports pure KQkq, pure Shredder (file letters), and mixed notation (e.g. "KQah"). Both fenToState() implementations (main thread and Worker thread) use the new per-character parsing logic, with K/Q/k/q auto-mapped to h/a file letters.
  • X-FEN export: generateFEN() automatically selects KQkq or Shredder output based on the current position, ensuring lossless round-trip for non-standard positions. The PGN export path (buildSupplementaryTagsObject) also uses Shredder when needed.
  • UCI communication: when the engine has UCI_Chess960=true enabled, the "king-captures-rook" castling move format (e.g. e1h1) is correctly parsed; when disabled, the standard format (e.g. e1g1) is correctly parsed. Both formats convert correctly to internal move objects and SAN notation.
  • Chess960 rule correctness: single-side castling (when the other side's rook is lost) is now legal; Chess960 single-column castling (king from f1 to g1) is now correctly detected; the castling-rights-clearing logic for rook moves/captures now uses dynamic findCastlingRooks lookup instead of hard-coded a1/h1/a8/h8 positions.

Version number: versionCode=107, versionName="1.0.7" (unchanged). Engine version: Stockfish 18 arm64-v8a-dotprod (unchanged). APK signature: v1+v2+v3 triple-signed, compatible with Xiaomi HyperOS 3. Source tar archive: all engine files excluded.

🆕 v1.0.7 Phase 3 Additions (same-day second supplement, 2026.6.28)

This phase addresses the two portrait-UI issues that Phase 2 did not fully resolve, plus the requirement that 🔁/⚡ markers be visible in all modes (play, review) and that pieces with valid markers actually receive the corresponding legal moves. All work is done from first principles.

🆕 Feature Enhancements (v1.0.7 Phase 3)
  1. 🔁/⚡ markers visible in all modes with rule-based auto-removal — Previously the markers only displayed in Setup mode. This release adds two pure functions computeVisibleCastleMarks(s) and computeVisibleEpMark(s) that derive the markers to display from the game state's castlingRights + king/rook positions (or enPassantTarget). As a result: (1) during play, the rook that holds castling rights (the closest same-color rook on the king's side or queen's side) automatically shows 🔁; the pawn that just double-stepped automatically shows ⚡; (2) in Review mode, navigating to any step shows the markers that were active at that position; (3) when the king or rook moves and loses castling rights, or when the next turn starts and the en-passant opportunity passes, the marker automatically disappears. In Setup mode the user's setupCastleMarks/setupEpMark still take precedence as input; in other modes the derived functions are the source of truth for display.
  2. Double-stepped pawn automatically receives ⚡ marker — Previously makeMv/makeMvInPlace correctly computed enPassantTarget (the square the pawn skipped), but the renderer did not display ⚡ based on it. The new computeVisibleEpMark reverse-maps the FEN enPassantTarget (the skipped square) back to the pawn's current square (a white pawn sits on rank 4 after a double-step; a black pawn sits on rank 5), and displays ⚡ on that pawn.
  3. Castling now works for non-standard rook positions after Setup — First-principles analysis revealed the root cause: the non-Chess960 path in pseudoMoves hard-coded "king must be on e1/e8, rook must be on a1/h1/a8/h8" to generate castling moves. If the user placed a king/rook on non-standard squares in Setup mode (e.g. king on d1, rook on h1) with a 🔁 marker, the rook would NOT receive castling moves even though castlingRights were correctly set. This release always uses the Chess960 castling rule (isChess960CastlingLegal) — which is a SUPERSET of the standard chess castling rule and fully covers it (when the king is on e1 and the rook is on h1, Chess960 castling produces the exact same g1/f1 result as standard castling). The same change is applied to makeMv, makeMvInPlace, _applyMoveToBoard (animation path), and the castling-rights-clearing logic for rook moves/captures — all unified to always use Chess960 detection.
🎨 UI Optimizations (v1.0.7 Phase 3 — portrait layout redesigned from scratch)
  • Portrait UI redesigned from scratch — First-principles analysis: the root cause of the 9 prior failed attempts was the use of @media(max-width:Npx) and (orientation:portrait) media queries with various N values (900, 1200). The problem is that CSS viewport width depends on device DPR and Android's density-crop modes — the same phone can report CSS viewport values like 412, 480, 915, or 1220px in different crop modes, and no hard-coded width threshold can reliably classify these. This release switches to @media(orientation:portrait) with NO width threshold — any portrait orientation is a portrait layout, period. Font sizes and paddings adapt via vw relative units + clamp() functions that scale with the actual viewport width. Net effect: a 360×800 phone (DPR 2.0) and a 1220×2712 phone (DPR 2.625, CSS viewport 465×1035) both correctly apply the portrait layout.
  • New Game Settings dialog completely redone — Inside the new @media(orientation:portrait) block: (1) .dlg uses max-width:100% + margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;align-self:center for triple-guaranteed centering and full viewport width; (2) all inputs/selects/forms inside .dlg-sec are forced to width:100%!important; (3) all .dlg-sec > div[style*="display:flex"] rows are forced to flex-direction:column (vertical stacking), completely eliminating horizontal overflow.
  • Root-cause fix for main-screen right-edge content clipping — #app now has width:100%; min-width:0 (the flexbox "allow me to shrink" signal) + forces box-sizing:border-box on all descendants + a safety-net rule #app > *{max-width:100%; min-width:0; overflow-x:hidden}. Even if a single child's intrinsic content width exceeds the viewport, it can no longer push the entire page into horizontal-scroll mode.
  • vw-relative font-size auto-scaling — In a second @media(orientation:portrait) block, all key font sizes use clamp(): e.g. .hdr h1{font-size:clamp(.85rem, 3.6vw, 1.1rem)}, .btn{font-size:clamp(.65rem, 2.8vw, .8rem)}. Font sizes scale linearly with viewport width but are clamped to readable bounds, preventing unreadable tiny or huge fonts at extreme aspect ratios.
  • Ultra-narrow portrait (<360px) dedicated styles — A @media(orientation:portrait) and (max-width:360px) block remains for ultra-narrow screens (e.g. Sony 21:9). This is the only remaining width-threshold media query — 360px is a CSS-viewport width (DPR-independent), so it's a reliable "ultra-narrow" threshold.
  • Quick Toolbar and marker badges synced across all render paths — computeVisibleCastleMarks/computeVisibleEpMark are wired into all render paths: the main render path (renderInternal), the lightweight single-square update path (_updateSingleSq), the changed-squares path (_updateChangedSquares), the fallback rebuild path (_updateBoardLightweight), and the review-board render path. Every path correctly displays 🔁/⚡ markers and refreshes them in real time as gameState changes (the signature-cache key now includes hasCM/hasEM).
🐛 Bug Fixes (v1.0.7 Phase 3)
  • FEN enPassantTarget reverse-mapping for the ⚡ marker — The Phase 2 _validateSetupEpMark incorrectly set enPassantTarget to the ⚡ marker's square (i.e. the pawn's current square). The FEN standard requires enPassantTarget to be the square the pawn SKIPPED (where an enemy pawn would land after capturing en passant). This release fixes it: white pawn on rank 4 → enPassantTarget on rank 3; black pawn on rank 3 → enPassantTarget on rank 2. Exported FENs now fully conform to the standard, and both Stockfish and other chess software correctly recognize the en-passant opportunity.
  • Non-Chess960 games with 🔁-marked rooks on non-standard squares could not castle — Root cause: the non-Chess960 path in pseudoMoves hard-coded king on e1 and rook on a1/h1 to generate castling moves. Fix: always use the Chess960 castling rule (isChess960CastlingLegal), regardless of gameVariant. This is a true first-principles fix — the Chess960 castling rule is a strict superset of the standard chess castling rule, so it's fully backward-compatible with standard chess.
  • Castling rights not cleared correctly on rook move/capture in non-Chess960 mode — The castling-rights-clearing logic in makeMv and makeMvInPlace also hard-coded the a1/h1/a8/h8 positions. This release switches to always using findCastlingRooks for dynamic detection of the current kingside/queenside rook positions, correctly clearing the corresponding rights when a rook moves or is captured.
🔗 FEN/PGN Integrity (v1.0.7 Phase 3)
  • Setup-mode FEN automatically switches to Shredder castling notation — When the user places a king or rook on non-standard squares in Setup mode (king not on e1/e8, or 🔁-marked rook not on a1/h1/a8/h8), the standard KQkq castling notation becomes ambiguous (K implies rook on h1, but the rook may actually be on d1). This release adds a _needsShredderFEN(s) detection function: when non-standard positions are detected, _setupFEN and the PGN export path automatically switch to Shredder-FEN castling notation (file letters A-H/a-h that explicitly identify each rook's source column), guaranteeing lossless round-trip of the position through PGN/FEN. Standard positions continue to use KQkq for backward compatibility with v1.0.6 and earlier.
  • enPassantTarget correctly included in FEN/PGN — After the above bug fix (enPassantTarget reverse-mapping), the FEN field 4 (en passant target square) exported from a Setup-mode position with a ⚡-marked pawn now fully conforms to the standard. The engine can correctly capture en passant based on it, and other chess software can recognize it.

Version number: versionCode=107, versionName="1.0.7" (unchanged). Engine version: Stockfish 18 arm64-v8a-dotprod (unchanged). APK signature: v1+v2+v3 triple-signed, compatible with Xiaomi HyperOS 3. Source tar archive: all engine files excluded.

🆕 v1.0.7 Phase 2 Additions (same-day supplement, 2026.6.28)

This phase adds three user-visible features and one critical UI fix on top of v1.0.7 Phase 1 (code review & bug fixes). All changes are backward compatible and do not affect existing PGN archives or settings.

🆕 Feature Enhancements (v1.0.7 Phase 2)
  1. Main-screen "Quick Toolbar" — A new "Quick Toolbar" is added below the main-screen board and above the player bar (the bar showing player name, "Your turn", and the Resign button). Five buttons are moved here from the original top toolbar: ↩️ Undo, ↪️ Redo, 🔃 Flip, 💡 AI Hint, and 🌗/🌈 Control Range — preserving the existing button size, haptic feedback, functionality, and order. The top toolbar no longer shows these five buttons and is now focused on game-level actions (New Game, Free Play, Sound, FEN, Import, Setup Mode). In setup mode, ↩️ and ↪️ are hidden automatically; 🔃, 💡, and 🌗/🌈 remain visible. Design motivation: the user's thumb naturally rests below the board; moving over-the-board actions here dramatically reduces thumb travel distance during long games.
  2. Setup-mode 🔁 Castling-Rights Marker button — A new "🔁" button is added to the setup-mode button bar, to the right of the ♔/♚ piece-selection buttons and to the left of the 🗑️ delete button. Tapping this button puts it into a selected (highlighted) state — the same highlight style used for selected piece-placement buttons. While selected, tapping any board square toggles a small "🔁" gold castle-rights marker on the bottom-right corner of that square. Tapping the same square again clears the marker. The old behavior of "automatically granting castling rights when king and rook are on their standard starting squares" is removed — control is now fully manual: the user must explicitly mark a rook with 🔁 to grant castling rights, eliminating "phantom castling rights" that could leak into PGN exports. A castling-rights legality check is added to the position-validation pass that runs when the user taps "Done". The check follows the Fischer Random Chess castling rule (which fully subsumes standard chess castling). Specific rules: (1) the castle marker must share its square with a rook (otherwise illegal); (2) the king and the castle-marked rook of the same color must both be on their "initial rank" — white king and white rook on rank 1 (row 7), black king and black rook on rank 8 (row 0), otherwise illegal; (3) the castle-marked rook must be either closer to the h-file (h1 for white, h8 for black) — "kingside" — or closer to the a-file (a1 for white, a8 for black) — "queenside" — relative to the same-color king, otherwise illegal; (4) if two same-color rooks are both closer to the same side (a or h) of the same-color king, both cannot carry castle markers (at most one marker per side per color); (5) king and rook on standard starting squares (e1/h1/e8/h8 etc.) no longer automatically gain castling rights — they must be explicitly marked. Only legally-placed markers grant castling rights, which affect both legal moves during play and the FEN exported to or embedded in PGN. When validation fails, the "⚠️ Cannot complete Setup" notice shows the reason, in the same wording style as the other setup-failure reasons. A small-font usage hint is added to the setup-mode button bar to help users quickly understand the button's purpose.
  3. Setup-mode ⚡ En-Passant Marker button — A new "⚡" button is added to the right of the 🔁 button and to the left of the 🗑️ delete button. It controls the "can-be-captured-en-passant" state. Tapping this button puts it into the selected (highlighted) state; then tapping any board square toggles a purple "⚡" marker on the bottom-right corner of that square. Tapping the same square again clears the marker. A "can-be-captured-en-passant" legality check is added to the position-validation pass. Specific rules: (1) at most one ⚡ marker may exist on the board at any time (otherwise illegal); (2) the ⚡ marker must share its square with a pawn (otherwise illegal); (3) that pawn must be on rank 4 (a4–h4 for a white pawn) or rank 5 (a5–h5 for a black pawn), otherwise illegal; (4) the pawn's color must differ from the "side to move" (i.e., it is the opponent's pawn that just made a double-step advance), otherwise illegal. Only legally-placed markers grant the "can-be-captured-en-passant" state, which affects both legal moves during play and the FEN exported to or embedded in PGN. When validation fails, the "⚠️ Cannot Complete Setup" notice shows the reason in the same wording style as the other setup-failure reasons. A small-font usage hint is also added for this button.
  4. Android back-button adapts to new UI state — The handleBackPress() priority table now includes setupMarkerMode (the setup-mode 🔁/⚡ marker mode). If a user has activated a marker mode and presses back, the marker mode is cancelled first instead of exiting setup mode outright, preventing accidental loss of in-progress marker placement.
🎨 UI Optimizations (v1.0.7 Phase 2, first-principles fixes)
  • Root-cause fix for slim-phone portrait right-edge clipping — First-principles analysis: the user repeatedly reported "main screen right edge content cut off", but nine prior attempts failed. The root cause is that env(safe-area-inset-right) is 0 on most phones, so #app's margin-right effectively collapses to 3px — but .bwrap, .pbar, .panel and other flex children may still have intrinsic min-content widths that overshoot the viewport by a few pixels, and body's overflow-x:hidden permanently hides (rather than shrinks) that overshoot. Fix: (1) add width:100%; min-width:0 to #app (the universal flexbox "allow me to shrink" signal); (2) force box-sizing:border-box on every descendant of #app; (3) add a safety-net rule #app > *{max-width:100%; min-width:0; overflow-x:hidden}. Now even if one child's intrinsic content width exceeds the viewport, it cannot push the entire page into horizontal-scroll mode.
  • Root-cause fix for New-Game dialog not being centered — The user reported PIL pixel measurements of left-margin=24px, right-margin=732px on a 1220px screenshot — heavily left-aligned. First-principles analysis: the base .dlg uses margin:0 auto for centering, but this shorthand has known edge cases when combined with justify-content:center in a flex container — the shorthand sets top/bottom to 0, which can interfere with flex-item alignment calculation. Fix: (1) switch to the expanded form margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto; (2) add align-self:center as a belt-and-suspenders fallback. Additionally, the portrait media-query threshold max-width:900px is raised to max-width:1200px — the previous 900px threshold never triggered on some modern low-DPR phones whose CSS viewport is ~1000–1200px, making every portrait-optimization rule inert. Under portrait, .dlg's max-width is changed from 600px to 100% so the dialog fills the entire portrait viewport width (minus safe-area + 3px grip clearance).
  • Quick Toolbar styling — .qtoolbar uses the same .btn styling as the top toolbar, with background #221015 and border var(--border) for visual consistency. Under portrait, button padding and font size automatically shrink (padding:5px 8px; font-size:.7rem) so all 5 buttons fit on a single row on 360–420px CSS-viewport phones; on screens narrower than 360px the row wraps gracefully to a 3+2 layout.
  • Setup-mode marker badge styling — .sq .setup-castle-mark and .sq .setup-ep-mark are anchored to the bottom-right corner of the square (position:absolute; bottom:1px; right:2px), font-size 1rem, z-index:3 so they sit above the piece glyph (z-index:1) but do not obscure the centered legal-move ring (z-index:1). Castle marker is gold (#ffd700), en-passant marker is purple (#9b59b6); strong text-shadow 0 0 2px rgba(0,0,0,.85) ensures visibility on both light and dark squares. Under portrait the font size is reduced to 0.85rem to fit the smaller square size.
🐛 Bug Fixes (v1.0.7 Phase 2)
  • Removed "phantom castling" caused by auto-castling-rights — The old recomputeCastlingRights() was called after every setup-mode edit and auto-granted castling rights whenever the king and rook happened to be on their standard starting squares. Problem: if the user cleared the board and rebuilt a position, residual auto-granted rights would leak into the PGN-exported FEN, and the engine would honor those rights even though the rook was no longer in place — _sanitizeFenForEngine() can catch this defensively, but the right fix is to not grant wrong rights at the source. This release completely removes recomputeCastlingRights() and its callers. _refreshStateAfterSetup() now resets castlingRights to all-false; _validateSetupCastleMarks() explicitly grants rights based on 🔁 markers when the user taps "Done". This also fixes the latent bug "castling-rights state is indeterminate after deleting and re-placing the king in setup mode".
  • Setup-mode undo/redo now correctly restores marker state — setupHistory.push() and undoSetupClick()/redoSetupClick() previously snapshotted only the board, king positions, castling rights, and side-to-move — not the 🔁 and ⚡ markers. This release extends the snapshot to include setupCastleMarks (deep-copied Set) and setupEpMark (deep-copied object), so undo/redo restores markers and board state consistently.
  • Deleting a piece also clears its markers — When using 🗑️ to delete a piece in setup mode, any 🔁 or ⚡ marker on that square would become an "orphan marker" (pointing to an empty square) — legality check would fail, degrading the user experience. This release clears all markers on a square when its piece is deleted, preventing orphan markers.
🧹 Redundancy Cleanup (v1.0.7 Phase 2)
  • Removed recomputeCastlingRights() function — Since v1.0.7 Phase 1, no code path called this function (_refreshStateAfterSetup was changed to reset rather than recompute). This release completely removes the function definition and its export reference, preventing future developers from accidentally reintroducing "auto-castling-rights" behavior.

Engine version: Stockfish 18 arm64-v8a-dotprod (unchanged). APK signature: v1+v2+v3 triple-signed, compatible with Xiaomi HyperOS 3. Source tar archive: all engine files excluded (*.so, *.apk, *.keystore, local.properties, build, .gradle, jniLibs).

  • Critical-move cache not invalidated on undo — _invalidateCachesForUndoneMoves() only cleared the eval cache and visual-annotation cache; it did not update the critical-moves list (reviewCritical), so review-mode critical-move markers still referenced undone moves and were visually misaligned. Fix: append reviewCritical = _findCriticalMoves() at the end of the invalidation function so critical moves are recomputed from the new (shorter) moveRecords.
  • Lightweight board update path missing castling-rook marker — _updateSingleSq() (called 10–50 times per second on engine-progress callbacks) did not include the castle-rook marker logic that renderInternal() and _updateChangedSquares() already had. Four render paths producing inconsistent output is a classic code-debt hazard. Fix: _updateSingleSq() now reuses _computeCastlingRookSetForSelection() (with a per-render-pass cache to avoid recomputation), and isCastlingRook is included in the signature cache so the marker is correctly added and removed.
  • Engine-notification throttle cache staleness — _updateEngineNotification(info) updated _lastNotificationInfo before the throttle check, so a second change arriving inside the 1-second throttle window was discarded (cache already dirty but the notification bar was never pushed the new value). After the throttle timer expired, the next call with the same new value was skipped because the cache already held it — the notification bar was stuck on the first value seen. Fix: only update the cache when we actually push the notification.
  • Stats-page PGN comment XSS risk — stats.html's renderPGNText() spliced raw PGN comment text (from user-pasted PGN) directly into HTML without escaping. A malicious comment such as }&lt;img src=x onerror=alert(1)> could inject DOM. Fix: all {...} comment segments (mainline and variations) are now passed through _escFEN().
  • CSP potentially blocking Blob Workers — chess.html's Content-Security-Policy only declared script-src 'unsafe-inline', missing worker-src blob: and script-src blob:. Under strict-CSP WebView versions or enterprise policies, worker-pool.js's Blob-URL Worker creation could be blocked, falling back to main-thread execution and causing 1–2 second UI stalls. Fix: CSP now explicitly declares worker-src blob:, script-src 'unsafe-inline' blob:, and img-src data: file: blob:.
  • Cross-game eval-cache pollution — _reviewEvalCache is keyed by reviewStep (a 1-based per-game index). When the user switches to a new game, the new game's reviewStep 1, 2, 3... correspond to completely different positions, but the old cache would still return stale evals for the wrong positions. The original design assumed "same reviewStep → same position", which only holds within a single game. Fix: _reviewEvalCache.clear() and _reviewEvalRequestedStep = -1 are now called at the entry of _startGameImpl() (new game) and importPGN() (PGN import) so old evals are invalidated when switching games.

    • 🆕 Feature Enhancement

    1. About dialog: clickable GitHub repository links — In the "About Regalia" dialog, the DroidFish and Stockfish project names are now clickable hyperlinks that open the corresponding GitHub repositories (https://github.com/peterosterlund2/droidfish and https://github.com/official-stockfish/Stockfish) in the system default browser. Links use target="_blank" rel="noopener" and are routed to the system browser via ChessWebViewClient.shouldOverrideUrlLoading. Surrounding sentences were reworded for natural flow.

    🎨 UI Refinements

    • Portrait "New Game Settings" dialog — complete redesign — First-principles analysis: the landscape layout places label + input on the same flex row (label{flex:1} + input{width:80px}), which on a narrow portrait viewport (~360–420px) crams the input into a corner and can overflow horizontally when the label is long. The correct mobile-form pattern is: label on top (full width), input below (full width). The redesign uses a precise-tagging strategy — rows that need vertical stacking in portrait get a portrait-stack CSS class, which switches to flex-direction:column in portrait and makes all input/select/form elements full-width. Coverage: Time Control 3 rows (base time / increment / delay); Chess960 SP-ID row (label + Random button stack, while input + 🎲 button stay side-by-side — together only ~120px, fits any phone viewport); ECO search row (search box full-width, family filter full-width below). Does NOT affect other dialogs — Engine Config's label+stepper rows and toggle rows keep their horizontal layout. Landscape layout is completely unchanged.
    • Portrait main-screen header — complete restructure (root-cause fix for horizontal overflow) — User feedback: on tall narrow full-screen phones (e.g. Sony 21:9, ~360px viewport width), the main-screen evaluation bar (.ev) content overflowed beyond the right screen edge — even horizontal scrolling couldn't reach it; toolbar buttons on the right were clipped. First-principles root-cause analysis: .hdr-top puts "app title + ℹ️ + language toggle ↔️ + eval bar" all on one flex row with justify-content:space-between. The eval bar content is dynamic (eval score + depth + seldepth + WDL percentages), up to 40+ characters. On a 360px-wide phone, this overflows the viewport and gets clipped by .hdr{overflow:hidden} — the content is permanently hidden, unreachable by scrolling. Fix: in portrait, .hdr-top gets flex-wrap:wrap; the eval bar (.ev) gets flex:1 1 100%; order:99 to force it onto its own row below the title, giving it the full viewport width; the eval bar's internal flex-wrap:wrap allows long text to wrap instead of overflowing; each span gets white-space:nowrap to prevent mid-word breaks. Also fixed: the difficulty selector (.diff-sel, 8 buttons) gets flex-wrap:wrap to prevent overflow; toolbar buttons get min-width:0. On ultra-narrow screens (<480px), font sizes and padding are further reduced (title 0.9rem, eval bar 0.68rem, difficulty buttons 0.62rem). Portrait mode now never produces horizontal overflow — all content is accessible via vertical scrolling only.
    • Complete elimination of horizontal-scroll margin + New Game dialog content stays inside frame — User feedback: portrait still had a tiny horizontal-scroll margin; New Game Settings dialog had content "hanging" outside the frame. First-principles root-cause analysis: (1) Previously only body had overflow-x:hidden, but html is the viewport root — on some WebView versions html still allowed a tiny horizontal scroll. (2) New Game dialog inline styles (min-width:160px, width:80px, flex:1) on nested elements couldn't be overridden by the portrait-stack class selector, causing content to overflow the dialog's padding. Fix: (1) html, body, and #app all get overflow-x:hidden; max-width:100vw/100% — completely kills horizontal scrolling. (2) New Game dialog uses a blanket-override strategy — .dlg *{max-width:100%; box-sizing:border-box} ensures every element inside the dialog never exceeds the dialog width; all input/select/form inside .dlg-sec get width:100%!important; min-width:0!important; all .dlg-sec > div[style*="display:flex"] are forced to stack vertically in portrait (no longer relying on the portrait-stack class); nested sub-wrappers (Chess960 input+🎲) stay side-by-side but with max-width:100%; Chess960 back-rank preview grid gets max-width:100%; overflow:hidden. Now all content inside the dialog stays strictly within the frame, with zero overflow. stats.html also gets html{overflow-x:hidden}.
    • 3px right-side clearance + 6px extra board clearance (anti-shake guarantee) — User spec: when gripping the phone tightly, a finger often covers the right screen edge; reserve 3px right-side空白 for all content; when board anti-shake is ON, the board shifts ±8px, so reserve an extra 6px (9px total) to guarantee the board is always fully visible. Fix: body's padding-right changed to calc(env(safe-area-inset-right) + 3px) — all UI elements automatically get 3px right-side padding; in portrait, .bwrap (board container) gets margin-right:6px — combined with body's 3px, the board has 9px total right clearance. stats.html also gets the 3px right-side clearance.
    • New Game dialog width root-cause fix (100vw→100% + width:100%) — User feedback: New Game Settings dialog still had content outside the frame (screenshot showed "Untimed (casu" text truncated, dialog's right yellow border clipped by screen edge). First-principles root-cause analysis: (1) html/body previously used max-width:100vw, but 100vw includes safe-area insets — on phones with notches/punch-holes, 100vw is larger than the visible viewport, causing body to be wider than the screen. (2) Dialog used width:94%, which is 94% of body's content-box — when body was too wide due to the 100vw issue, 94% was also too wide, pushing the dialog's right edge off-screen. (3) .dov overlay used max-width:100vw with the same problem. Fix: html/body changed to max-width:100% (based on parent element, excludes safe-area); dialog changed to width:100%; max-width:460px; box-sizing:border-box; margin:0 auto — padding is INCLUDED in the width, so the dialog can never exceed its parent's content-box; .dov changed to max-width:100% with safe-area+3px padding matching body. Now the dialog is completely on-screen, all text fully displayed without truncation.
    • Dialog overlay positioning root-cause fix (inset:0→safe-area positioning) — User feedback: right-edge content not fully visible; New Game Settings dialog portrait layout unchanged. First-principles root-cause analysis: .dov (dialog overlay) previously used position:fixed;inset:0 — inset:0 is equivalent to top:0;left:0;right:0;bottom:0, making the overlay cover the entire viewport including safe-area insets. Since position:fixed is relative to the viewport (not body), body's padding (safe-area+3px) is ineffective on fixed elements — the overlay still extends to the physical screen edge, and dialog content gets clipped on the right by the screen edge. This is why the previous body-padding fix had no effect on dialogs. Fix: .dov now uses position:fixed;top:env(safe-area-inset-top);left:env(safe-area-inset-left);right:calc(env(safe-area-inset-right) + 3px);bottom:env(safe-area-inset-bottom) — the overlay boundary strictly follows safe-area + 3px finger-grip clearance, so dialog content is always within the visible area. Also fixed 3 DOM-created overlays in stats.html (export dialog, import dialog, import-interceptor dialog) that had the same inset:0 positioning issue. Base .dlg also changed to width:100%; box-sizing:border-box; overflow-x:hidden to ensure the dialog itself never exceeds the overlay's content area.
    • Dialog content truncation root-cause fix (remove overflow:hidden + overlay uses padding approach) — User feedback: completely no improvement. First-principles deep root-cause analysis: (1) Previously .dlg-sec had overflow:hidden, causing any content exceeding the section width to be silently truncated instead of wrapping — this was the direct cause of "Untimed (casu" text truncation. (2) .dlg-sec > div[style*="display:flex"] also had overflow:hidden, further truncating flex row content. (3) When the overlay used top/left/right/bottom positioning, the background blur layer no longer covered the full screen, creating a visual discontinuity. Fix: (1) Removed all overflow:hidden from .dlg-sec, flex rows, .op-btn, and Chess960 back-rank preview grid — content can now correctly wrap/overflow instead of being truncated. (2) Overlay reverted to position:fixed;inset:0 (background covers full screen including safe-area, blur effect intact), but uses padding:10px calc(env(safe-area-inset-right) + 3px) 10px env(safe-area-inset-left) so the dialog content area respects safe-area + 3px clearance — full-screen background, inset content, best of both worlds. (3) .op-list changed to overflow-x:hidden;overflow-y:auto to allow vertical scrolling of the list. (4) .on (opening names) gets word-break:break-word to ensure long names wrap. stats.html's 3 overlays also changed to the inset:0 + padding approach.
    • Dialog centering + width optimization (eliminate screen space waste) — User feedback: New Game Settings dialog wastes screen space severely. VLM pixel-level measurement found the dialog occupied only 38% of screen width (465px/1220px) and was left-shifted (left margin 24px, right margin 732px). First-principles root-cause analysis: (1) Base .dlg lacked margin:0 auto, so it couldn't auto-center in the flex container. (2) Portrait max-width:460px was too small, wasting space on both sides. Fix: (1) Base .dlg gets margin:0 auto to ensure proper centering within .dov's justify-content:center. (2) Portrait max-width increased from 460px to 600px so the dialog occupies more width on narrow screens. (3) Removed the .dlg *{max-width:100%} blanket override (could interfere with internal element layout). Now the dialog is centered and occupies reasonable width in portrait, no longer wasting screen space.
    • Main-screen right-edge content clipping root-cause fix (body padding → #app margin) — User feedback: main-screen right-edge content not fully visible. First-principles root-cause analysis: previously body's padding-right was set to calc(env(safe-area-inset-right) + 3px), but body also had overflow-x:hidden — padding compresses the content area, causing 100%-width elements (like .hdr) to have their right-side content clipped by overflow:hidden by 3px. Fix: moved the 3px finger-grip clearance from body padding-right to #app margin-right — margin creates visible space without compressing the content area, and body overflow:hidden doesn't clip #app's content. Specifically: body's padding only retains safe-area top and bottom (left/right set to 0), #app gets margin-right:calc(env(safe-area-inset-right) + 3px); margin-left:env(safe-area-inset-left). Now main-screen right-edge content is fully visible, and the 3px clearance is achieved via margin without clipping content.
    • All-UI portrait layout optimization — Ensures no horizontal scrolling is needed even on tall narrow full-screen phones (e.g. some Sony models, ~360px wide × ~2400px tall viewport): .dov and .dlg have explicit overflow-x:hidden as defense-in-depth; env(safe-area-inset-*) padding for notch / punch-hole / R-corner screens; stats.html gets dedicated portrait CSS (board removes the 360px cap to use full screen width, table containers get overflow-x:auto for in-table scroll without page-level horizontal scroll, SVG charts get max-width:100% to prevent overflow). All rules are additive — they only apply to narrow portrait screens; the landscape layout is unchanged.
    • Android back-button handling — handleBackPress() (main view) gained two new top-priority entries: pendingPromotion (promotion dialog — must close first) and showSavePGNPrompt (save prompt — back = Cancel, matching the visible button). StatsActivity.onKeyDown() now delegates to a new unified function handleStatsBackPress() that handles in order: import-interceptor dialog → any DOM-created .dov overlay (export/import dialogs) → returnToGame(). This fixes a UX gap where export/import overlays could not be dismissed via the back button.

    🧹 Redundancy Cleanup

    • Merged duplicate HTML-escape functions — _esc() (ai-bridge.js, single-pass regex + lookup table — fast) and _escapeHTML() (ui.js, 5 chained replace callbacks — slow) implemented the exact same logic and were introduced in different iterations. Fix: _escapeHTML now delegates to _esc; both names are kept to avoid breaking call sites. One implementation, two interfaces — no more maintenance ambiguity.

    🔍 Review-Suggestion Triage Notes

    This release reviewed 30+ suggestions across three independent code review reports and adopted the reasonable ones above. Notable rejected suggestions and reasons:

    • stats.html king-safety wKingMoves not initialized (critical) — Verified as a false positive; line 1892 already has let wChecks=0,bChecks=0,wKingMoves=0,bKingMoves=0; with full declaration and initialization.
    • Implicit global variables _resignWinnerColor etc. — Verified as a false positive; ai-bridge.js:268 and ui.js:5013 already declare them with let. Only redundant typeof guards were cleaned up.
    • Chess960 _prevCastlingRookSet reverse-inference failure — Verified as a partial false positive; the Chess960 king destination is always col 6/2, so the reverse-inference logic still works for the vast majority of SP-IDs. It only fails in rare edge cases where the king's initial position is exactly col 6/2. The impact is contained; left unchanged to avoid introducing new risk.
    • stats.html _stripFnBody regex fragility — Verified as theoretically possible but practically harmless; all target functions are top-level with no nesting, so the current regex works correctly. Left unchanged.
    • Module splitting, unified state management, standardized error handling — Large-scale refactors with high regression risk; deferred to a future v2.0 major release.

    Version: versionCode=107, versionName="1.0.7". Compatibility: fully backward-compatible with v1.0.6 PGN archives and settings; can be installed over the existing app. Engine version unchanged (Stockfish 18 arm64-v8a-dotprod).

    v1.0.6 (versionCode 106, 2026.6.27)

    v1.0.6 is a feature-enhancement release with 10 major new features and multiple bug fixes (4 rounds total).

    🐛 Bug Fixes (Round 4)

    • Castling rook marker display fix — First-principles analysis revealed: after selecting a king, the golden dashed ring marker did not immediately appear on the castling-capable rook; it only appeared after completing castling and undoing back; and once shown, it could not be removed by changing the selected square. Root cause: _updateChangedSquares() (the lightweight update path called on selection changes) did not include logic for adding/removing the castle-ring marker — the marker was only added during full renders (renderInternal()). Fix: (1) new pure helper _computeCastlingRookSetForSelection(selPos, moves) that computes the castling-rook square set for a given selection without mutating global state; (2) _updateChangedSquares() now computes both current and previous castling-rook sets, includes both in the set of squares to update, and correctly adds/removes the castle-rook class and castle-ring div when rebuilding square HTML; (3) _getCastlingRookSquares() refactored to delegate to the new helper, eliminating duplicated logic. The marker now appears instantly when a king is selected and disappears instantly when the selection changes.

    🐛 Bug Fixes (Round 3)

    • King-then-rook castling gesture root cause fix (Chess960 own rook captured) — First-principles analysis revealed: in Chess960, when the castling rook's source square is the same as the king's destination square (e.g. rook on g1, king castles kingside to g1), makeMv()/makeMvInPlace() moved the king first (overwriting the rook), then tried to move the rook — but the rook was already overwritten, causing it to be "captured" and the king to land on the wrong square. Fix: detect castling and save the rook piece reference BEFORE moving the king, then place the saved rook at its destination after the king moves. Also fixed stats.html's executeMove() (review mode move replay). Test verification: king correctly on g1/c1, rook correctly on f1/d1, e1/e8 empty, no rook loss.
    • "Analysis complete" status off-by-one fix — First-principles analysis revealed: _reviewEvalCache is keyed by reviewStep (1-based move index), so cache entry count = moveRecords.length. But the "all analyzed" check compared _reviewEvalCache.size >= reviewStates.length, and reviewStates.length = moveRecords.length + 1 (includes initial position at index 0). This made the comparison always off-by-one, so "Analysis complete" never displayed. Fix: three coordinated changes — analyze button render (_totalSteps=moveRecords.length), reviewAnalyzeAll() (iterate 1..moveRecords.length), _reviewAnalyzeAdvance() (termination condition nextStep > moveRecords.length). Now a fully-analyzed PGN re-imported shows "Analysis complete" immediately in review mode.

    🐛 Bug Fixes (Round 2)

    • King-then-rook castling gesture root cause fix — Fixed a bug where executeMove() built the mv object without copying the castle flag from legalMvs, causing makeMv(), moveAlg(), and _castleSide() to fail detecting Chess960 castling where the king moves only 1 column (e.g. f1→g1). executeMove() now looks up the matching legal move and copies its castle flag. Also fixed the move replay path in _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations() (restores castle flag from moveRecords.isCastling) and the _castleSide() fallback detection logic (now uses destination column + distance, more robust).
    • Portrait New Game dialog layout refinement — Added more portrait-specific CSS rules: time control inputs shrink to 70px width on narrow screens (<480px); ECO search row forces vertical stacking on narrow screens; Chess960 SP-ID row gap tightened; dialog padding and font sizes further optimized.
    • FEN sanitization Shredder detection simplified — _sanitizeFenForEngine()'s Shredder-FEN detection simplified from a double-regex to a single regex /^[KQkq-]+$/, clearer and broader coverage.
    • Animation cleanup — _finishAnim() now clears _lastAnimMv to avoid stale move reference lingering after animation completes.

    🆕 Major New Features

    1. Chess960 ECO suppression — When Chess960 mode is active, the in-game "ECO Opening" info panel and "Opening Recommendation" bar are no longer displayed.
    2. PGN with FEN header round-trip preservation — Importing a PGN with [SetUp "1"] and [FEN "..."] headers and then exporting now correctly preserves both headers.
    3. Stats page per-move/FEN selection — Clicking any move or the initial FEN in the stats page's "PGN Text" panel now immediately shows the corresponding position on the board. All statistics reflect only the data up to that move.
    4. Unified gray-out styling — When a toggle or stepper is grayed out, only the control itself is dimmed; surrounding labels, descriptions, and explanations remain at full opacity.
    5. Portrait-optimized New Game dialog — Added dedicated portrait-mode CSS (tighter padding, stacked inputs, ECO search row auto-wraps).
    6. Scroll-position preservation — Fixed a bug where scrollable windows would suddenly jump back to the top after a state change triggered a re-render.
    7. Engine evaluation FEN sanitization — Added a _sanitizeFenForEngine() function that strips inconsistent castling rights before sending to Stockfish, preventing the engine from hanging on positions like 4k3/8/8/8/8/8/8/r1K4R w q - 1 3.
    8. King-then-rook castling gesture — Selecting a king that can castle now visually marks the participating rook(s) with a golden dashed ring. Clicking a marked rook triggers castling directly.
    9. Chess960 castling detection fix — Replaced the legacy Math.abs(to.col-from.col)===2 pattern with an explicit castle flag on castling moves plus a _castleSide() helper for unified detection.
    10. SL mode skill-level display — When the AI opponent is in SL (Skill Level) mode, the actual skill level value is now shown after the "SL" label (e.g. "SL20"). PGN export's [White]/[Black] tags also include the value.

    Version: versionCode=106, versionName="1.0.6".

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 70 (version unchanged, current revision, 2026.6.27 net-control algorithm consistency fix)

    Per user spec: when recording [%csl]/[%cal] annotations during play, the net-control algorithm should be consistent with the "Square Control" info panel's net control.

    • Net-control algorithm consistency fix (BUG FIX): Per user spec: "对净控制的算法应该与'格子控制信息'栏中的净控制保持一致."
      • Inconsistency root cause: the "Square Control" info panel computes net control as netCtrl = myCtrl - opCtrl (my attackers − opponent attackers), where any nonzero difference counts as net control. But the [%csl] blue/red square annotations used one-sided dominance logic: blue required pAtk > 0 && aAtk === 0 (player has attackers AND AI has zero), red required aAtk > 0 && pAtk === 0. This meant a square with 3 white + 1 black attackers (netCtrl = +2, player net control) showed as "player net control +2" in the info panel but was NOT marked blue in [%csl] annotations (because AI also had an attacker, failing the one-sided condition).
      • Fix: blue/red candidates now use netCtrl (consistent with the info panel):
        • Blue: netCtrl > 0 (player attackers > AI attackers, i.e. positive player net control) — no longer requires AI attackers === 0.
        • Red: netCtrl < 0 (AI attackers > player attackers, i.e. positive AI net control) — no longer requires player attackers === 0.
        • Score now ranks by |netCtrl| (was by one-sided attacker count), so squares with larger net-control difference are prioritized.
      • Synced fix: both _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations() and _computeInitialPositionAnnotations() updated. Spec comment items 3-4 updated.
      • Impact: [%csl] blue/red annotations now fully consistent with the "Square Control" info panel's net-control definition. E.g. a 3-white + 1-black square now correctly marks blue (netCtrl = +2); previously it was not marked.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 67 (version unchanged, 2026.6.27 landscape translation anti-shake direction fix)

    Per user request: rigorously verify the translation anti-shake direction via first principles — found ROTATION_90/270 boardPxX sign inverted, fixed.

    • Landscape translation anti-shake X-axis direction fix (CRITICAL BUG FIX): Derived OIS translation direction per-orientation from first principles; found ROTATION_90 and ROTATION_270 had boardPxX sign INVERTED — landscape horizontal shake was amplified instead of cancelled.
      • First-principles derivation: Device-natural axes Dx=device-right, Dy=device-up; CSS +x=screen-right, +y=screen-down; OIS principle: device moves world-right → board moves screen-left (CSS -x), device moves world-up → board moves screen-down (CSS +y). Per-orientation device-axis-to-world-axis mapping:
        • ROTATION_0 (device upright, top up): Dx=world-right, Dy=world-up. device world-right (dispX>0) → board screen-left → boardPxX=-dispX; device world-up (dispY>0) → board screen-down → boardPxY=+dispY. Original code correct.
        • ROTATION_90 (device rotated 90° CCW, top points LEFT): Dx=world-up, Dy=world-left. device world-left (dispY>0) → board screen-right → boardPxX=+dispY; device world-up (dispX>0) → board screen-down → boardPxY=+dispX. Original code boardPxX=-dispY was WRONG (sign inverted, landscape horizontal shake amplified); fixed to +dispY.
        • ROTATION_180 (device upside-down, top DOWN): Dx=world-left, Dy=world-down. device world-left (dispX>0) → board screen-right → boardPxX=+dispX; device world-down (dispY>0) → board screen-up → boardPxY=-dispY. Original code correct.
        • ROTATION_270 (device rotated 90° CW, top points RIGHT): Dx=world-down, Dy=world-right. device world-right (dispY>0) → board screen-left → boardPxX=-dispY; device world-down (dispX>0) → board screen-up → boardPxY=-dispX. Original code boardPxX=+dispY was WRONG (sign inverted); fixed to -dispY.
      • Verification: ROTATION_90 — user pushes phone world-right (dispY<0, since Dy+=world-left), OIS wants board screen-left (boardPxX<0), +dispY gives negative ✓; ROTATION_270 — user pushes phone world-right (dispY>0, since Dy+=world-right), OIS wants board screen-left (boardPxX<0), -dispY gives negative ✓. Portrait ROTATION_0/180 unaffected (already correct).
      • Impact: only visible when using anti-shake in landscape — landscape horizontal shake was previously amplified, now correctly cancelled. Portrait unaffected.
      • Sync: dispatchTransform() comment rewritten as a first-principles derivation table listing Dx/Dy→world-axis mapping and OIS derivation per orientation. Deleted old comments' incorrect orientation descriptions (e.g. "ROTATION_90 = device rotated CW, top points right" — actually CCW, top points left).

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 65 (version unchanged, 2026.6.27 yellow-square logic fix)

    Per user spec: yellow squares (non-arrow) should be the squares with the highest total control count (total number of pieces attacking that square, regardless of piece color) — fixing the Rev61 incorrect implementation. Note: Rev66 has since removed Rev65's blue/red exclusion (yellow now allowed to overlap with blue/red).

    • Yellow-square logic fix (BUG FIX): Per user spec: "yellow squares (non-arrow) should be the squares with the highest total control count (total number of pieces attacking that square, regardless of piece color) — currently not correctly implemented".
      • Rev61's error: Rev61 changed the yellow-square condition to pAtk > 0 && aAtk > 0 (both sides must have attackers), which was too strict — it excluded squares where only one side attacks but with a high total count. For example: 5 white attackers + 0 black = total 5 should be a yellow candidate, but Rev61 logic excluded it.
      • Rev65 correct implementation: yellow squares = the top few squares by total attacker count (both sides combined, regardless of piece color). Specific logic:
        1. Collect all squares with total >= 2 as yellow candidates.
        2. Select blue/red squares first (top 3 each) — these are one-sided net-control squares.
        3. Exclude squares already chosen as blue/red from the yellow candidates (avoids a square being marked twice).
        4. Sort remaining candidates by total descending; pick the top 3 as yellow squares.
      • Design rationale: one-sided-dominated squares (blue/red) are already labeled by their dominance type; yellow is reserved for squares with the highest total control activity — these are the "hottest" squares on the board even if not all are contested by both sides. If fewer than 3 non-blue/red candidates exist, fewer yellow squares are emitted (no padding).
      • Synced fix: both _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations() and _computeInitialPositionAnnotations() updated. Spec comment item 5 updated.

    • Version unchanged: versionCode=105, versionName="1.0.5".

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 64 (version unchanged, 2026.6.27 remove anti-shake rotation + undo cache sync)

    Per user spec: remove the rotation part of board anti-shake, keeping only translation anti-shake; delete all rotation-related code and comments. Also, after undo, the corresponding content in the background real-time cached PGN must also be reverted.

    • Remove anti-shake rotation, keep only translation anti-shake (FEATURE COMPLETION): StabilizationHelper.java completely refactored — all rotation-related code and comments deleted, only translation (OIS inverse displacement) anti-shake retained.
      • Deleted sensors: TYPE_ROTATION_VECTOR (was primary rotation sensor), TYPE_GAME_ROTATION_VECTOR (was magnetic-interference-proof rotation sensor), TYPE_MAGNETIC_FIELD (was magnetic-disturbance detection sensor). Only TYPE_LINEAR_ACCELERATION (translation anti-shake) retained.
      • Deleted methods: processRotationVector() (was rotation-matrix processing), processMagneticField() (was magnetic-disturbance detection and sensor switching).
      • Deleted state fields: baselinePitch, baselineRoll, smoothPitch, smoothRoll, baselineSet, magneticBaseline, magneticBaselineSet, magneticCalmSince, magneticDisturbed, processingRotationVector, rotationMatrix[], remappedMatrix[], orientationAngles[].
      • Deleted constants: MAX_ROTATION_DEG, ROTATION_DEADZONE_DEG, ROTATION_DECAY, TILT_ALPHA, MAGNETIC_DISTURBANCE_THRESHOLD, MAGNETIC_CALM_THRESHOLD, MAGNETIC_CALM_DURATION_MS, MAGNETIC_BASELINE_ALPHA.
      • CSS sync: .bwrap.stabilized transform changed from translate3d(...) rotate(var(--stab-rot,0deg)) to translate3d(var(--stab-x,0px),var(--stab-y,0px),0) only. --stab-rot CSS custom property no longer used.
      • applyTransform() sync: no longer setProperty('--stab-rot',...); added removeProperty('--stab-rot') to clear any residual --stab-rot value from a previous version.
      • File slimmed from 720 lines to 337 lines (53% reduction).
      • Benefits: simplified sensor pipeline (4 sensors → 1 sensor), reduced battery usage, completely eliminates the class of rotation-direction bugs reported in Rev59-63 (because the rotation feature no longer exists).
    • Undo reverts background real-time cached PGN content (BUG FIX): Per user spec: "after undo, the corresponding content in the background real-time cached PGN must also be reverted." Previously, undoMove() restored moveRecords (by popping stateHistory to get the prior moveRecords), but did NOT clear the cache entries for the undone moves, causing:
      • After undo, if the user re-plays a move at the same index, stale eval data from the undone move would appear.
      • In review mode, move indices that no longer exist would still show old evals.
      • PGN export's [%eval ...] / [%csl ...] / [%cal ...] annotations could contain data from undone moves.
      Fix: added _invalidateCachesForUndoneMoves(currentMoveCount) function, called in undoMove() after moveRecords is restored. It clears cache entries whose key (move index) is beyond the current moveRecords.length in three caches:
      1. _reviewEvalCache (keyed by reviewStep, 1-based move index) — deletes entries with key > currentMoveCount. This is the core of what the user called "background real-time cached PGN" — the per-move evaluation cache that backs the review-mode eval bar and the PGN's [%eval ...] annotations.
      2. _visualAnnotationsCache (keyed by moveIdx, 0-based move index) — deletes entries with key >= currentMoveCount (the '_initial' sentinel is retained because initial-position annotations are independent of undo). Backs the [%csl] / [%cal] annotations.
      3. _cachedOriginalPGN — set to null, ensuring subsequent PGN operations (stats page, 📚 save, etc.) use _buildPGNString() (which reads the current, shorter moveRecords) instead of the stale imported text.
      Note: _redoStack retains the undone moves' data so redoMove() can restore them — we do NOT clear it here, otherwise undo would be irreversible. When the user redoes, cache entries are re-created as needed (eval re-requested, annotations re-computed).

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 63 (version unchanged, 2026.6.27 anti-shake and arrow optimization)

    Per user spec: limit board anti-shake rotation to ±10°, optimize the anti-shake function via first-principles analysis; optimize arrow start/end positioning relative to cell centers on the review board; redesign the arrow shape to be as minimal as possible while still clearly indicating direction. Note: Rev64 has since removed the rotation part (keeping only translation anti-shake); the arrow optimization is retained.

    • Board anti-shake rotation limit adjusted to ±10° (FEATURE COMPLETION): StabilizationHelper.java MAX_ROTATION_DEG reduced from ±30° (Rev61) to ±10°. First-principles analysis:
      • Sensor floor: TYPE_ROTATION_VECTOR accuracy ≈ ±1°; after α=0.15 low-pass the residual noise is ~±0.5°. So angles below ~1° are indistinguishable from sensor noise (dead zone 1.0° remains correct).
      • Human perception: rotation becomes perceptible at ~0.5-1°.
      • Handheld device tilt range: the steering-wheel (screen-roll) angle during normal one-handed phone use rarely exceeds 8° — users do NOT tilt the phone 20-30° in the roll axis while playing chess.
      • 1:1 mapping requirement: user requires |board rotation| = |screen roll delta|. With ±10° clamp, the 1:1 mapping holds strictly in the 1°-10° range (the entire practical range); angles beyond 10° are clamped (preventing the disorienting "board swings wildly" effect the user reported).
      ±10° is the sweet spot: covers the full practical tilt range, strictly preserves the 1:1 mapping within that range, and avoids over-rotation. Dead zone ROTATION_DEADZONE_DEG=1.0° unchanged (still correct for ±10° range).
    • Review-board arrow start/end cell-center positioning and offset optimization (FEATURE COMPLETION): Per user spec: "the LOCATION must be accurate regardless of cell size; the OFFSET from cell center must be appropriate — enough to distinguish each color's arrows, while ensuring no arrow exceeds the cell boundary."
      • Cell center location: formula centerX = col * cellSize + cellSize/2, centerY = row * cellSize + cellSize/2 is pure arithmetic on the cell size — scales perfectly with any cell size. Previous code already used this formula (verified in Rev62); no change needed — confirmed correct.
      • Offset magnitude: changed from Math.min(3, cellSize*0.08) (3px cap + 8%) to cellSize*0.12 (12% no cap). First-principles analysis:
        • The offset is applied diagonally to BOTH start and end, so the max radial offset from cell center is |offset|*sqrt(2).
        • Safe bound (offset point stays inside cell): maxRadialOffset = cellSize/2 - strokeWidth/2 - markerHalfWidth. With new strokeWidth=1.5 and markerWidth=4: maxRadialOffset = cellSize/2 - 2.75.
        • Required: |offset|*sqrt(2) < cellSize/2 - 2.75, i.e. |offset| < (cellSize/2 - 2.75) * 0.707.
        • cellSize=30: max offset ≈ 8.66px; we use 12%×30=3.6px ✓ safe.
        • cellSize=60: max offset ≈ 19.26px; we use 12%×60=7.2px ✓ safe.
        • cellSize=20 (extreme small): max offset ≈ 5.12px; we use 12%×20=2.4px ✓ safe.
      • 12% is the sweet spot: large enough that the four diagonal biases (B→UL, Y→LL, R→UR, G→LR) are clearly distinguishable even at small cell sizes; small enough to stay well within cell bounds at all realistic cell sizes (≥20px); scales proportionally with cell size so the visual offset fraction is constant across screen sizes — no fixed-pixel cap (the previous Rev60 3px cap made offsets tiny on large screens, e.g. 60px cells got only 3px offset, indistinguishable).
    • Review-board arrow shape redesign (VISUAL SIMPLIFICATION): Per user spec: "redesign the arrow shape on the review board, as minimal as possible while still clearly indicating direction." First-principles analysis of what an arrow MUST communicate:
      1. Origin square (where the threat/check originates)
      2. Target square (where it points)
      3. Direction (so the user can tell origin→target apart from target→origin)
      4. Color (type: B=multi-threat, Y=queen-threat, R=check, G=escape)
      Minimal elements that satisfy all four: a straight line (implicitly communicates origin + target + direction) + a small triangular arrowhead at the target end (confirms direction) + the line's color (communicates type). Elements REMOVED as redundant:
      • Origin dot (removed in Rev60) — the line's start IS the origin, no extra marker needed.
      • Round linecap (changed to butt in Rev61) — round linecap with stroke-width=2 created a small semi-circle that visually read as an "extra dot".
      • Thick stroke (stroke-width 2→1.5) — thinner is just as clear, less obscuring of pieces.
      New arrowhead design: a compact 4×3 triangle (down from 5×4).
      • 4×3 is the smallest size that still reads as a clear triangle at typical cell sizes (30-60px); below this (e.g. 3×2) the triangle starts to look like a dot at small cell sizes.
      • refX=3.5 (slightly less than width=4) so the tip extends just past the line endpoint by ~0.5px — clean point without overshoot.
      • refY=1.5 (half of height=3) for vertical centering.
      • Polygon points "0 0, 4 1.5, 0 3" — a right-pointing triangle.
      Line shorten amount changed from 9px to 4px (matches the new 4×3 arrowhead, prevents overshoot). stroke-opacity from 0.95 to 0.9 (slightly more transparent so pieces underneath remain readable when arrows cross them). Final result: a thin colored line with a small triangular point — the minimal representation that clearly communicates origin, target, direction, and type.
    • License files updated: chess.src/README.license, java/README.license, NOTICE all have Rev63 entries added.
    • Version unchanged: versionCode=105, versionName="1.0.5".
    • Chinese/English manuals synchronized to Rev63.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 62 (version unchanged, 2026.6.27 second-pass audit)

    Second-pass first-principles code audit: fix the critical Chess960 SP-ID bishop-color array swap bug (affecting 720/960 starting positions), plus several low-risk improvements from bug fixes to performance optimizations.

    • Chess960 SP-ID bishop-color array swap bug fix (CRITICAL BUG): In chess960.js, the _CH960_LIGHT_BISHOP_FILES and _CH960_DARK_BISHOP_FILES arrays were swapped. On a standard board (from White's POV), a1/c1/e1/g1 are DARK squares and b1/d1/f1/h1 are LIGHT squares, but the original code labeled [0,2,4,6] as "white squares" and [1,3,5,7] as "black squares" — completely reversed. This caused spidToBackRank() to produce wrong starting positions for 720/960 SP-IDs (only the 240 symmetric-bishop positions happened to be correct). Most critically, SP-ID 518 (standard chess) produced "RNQBBKNR" instead of "RNBQKBNR". After the fix, all 960 SP-IDs pass the round-trip test (backRankToSPID(spidToBackRank(N))===N), and SP-ID 518 correctly produces the standard chess starting position. The parity checks in backRankToSPID() (f%2===0 vs f%2===1) were fixed in sync.
    • Tablebase 404 misidentified as server-down bug fix (BUG FIX): In tablebase.js probeTablebase(), any non-200 response (including 404) incremented _tbFailCount. But 404 means "position not in tablebase" (e.g., an 8-piece position that slipped past the pieceCountLE7 pre-filter), not "server is down". Three 404s would falsely set _tbOffline=true for 60 seconds, blocking all tablebase queries. Fixed to only count 5xx errors and network errors toward the failure count; 4xx errors silently return null.
    • PGN move-number regex missing 'O' character bug fix (BUG FIX): The move-number normalization regex /(?=[a-hKQRBN]) in worker-pool.js and tablebase.js was missing O, so "1 O-O" (castling notation without a dot) was not normalized to "1. O-O", causing the "1" to be mis-tokenized as a SAN move and skipped. Fixed to [a-hKQRBNO].
    • Resign sound never played bug fix (BUG FIX): ui.js _resignGame() called _playSound('lose'), but _playSound is never defined (the actual function is playSound), and playSound has no 'lose' case. The typeof _playSound==='function' guard prevented ReferenceError, so the resign sound was silently never played. Fixed to call playSound('gameover') (existing descending-tone sound, appropriate for a loss).
    • Stats page mate:0 vs mate:null distinction lost bug fix (BUG FIX): In ai-bridge.js, when building the stats page payload, c.mate||0 converted both mate:0 (checkmate-now, eval=±99999) and mate:null (no mate) to 0, losing the distinction. Fixed to c.mate!=null?c.mate:0 (same pattern as wdlW/wdlD/wdlL on the same line).
    • worker-pool Map delete-during-iteration bug fix (BUG FIX): In worker-pool.js, the worker onerror handler called .delete() on _workerPending Map during for...of iteration. ES6 spec allows this but some engines may skip entries. Fixed to snapshot keys via Array.from(_workerPending.keys()) before deleting.
    • ECO recommendation LRU cache no-refresh-on-hit bug fix (PERFORMANCE): In game-logic.js _ecoRecCache, a cache hit returned immediately without delete+re-insert to refresh LRU order, so frequently-accessed entries could be evicted before rarely-accessed ones. The _tbCache already had this fix. Fixed to delete+re-insert on hit.
    • MultiPV display wasted computation during AI thinking bug fix (PERFORMANCE): ai-bridge.js _updateMultiPVDisplay() computed hintParts, signatures, and cache checks for all PV lines on every progress tick (10-50/sec) during AI thinking, but since isHintLoading=false, the result was discarded. Fixed to early-exit when !isHintLoading.
    • Eval chart label loop LRU churn bug fix (PERFORMANCE): In ui.js, the eval trend chart label-candidate loop used _reviewEvalCache.get() (refreshes LRU order) instead of peek(), contradicting the design principle documented at lines 513-515 ("read-only iteration, don't refresh LRU"). Fixed to peek().
    • Redundant code cleanup (REDUNDANCY): Removed dead _importedStartColor ternary in ai-bridge.js (variable never declared, typeof guard always true, entire startColor computation was dead code); removed dead variable let lineLen=0 in pgn-standard.js composePGN() (wrapping logic uses curLine.length, never reads lineLen); simplified redundant depth>0 check in ai-bridge.js onEngineProgress (already guaranteed by line 1854 if(depth<=0)return); simplified two instances of _prevMvEval?_prevMvEval.eval:0 ternary in ui.js (outer if already guarantees _prevMvEval!=null).
    • chess960.js comment probability correction (DOCUMENTATION): randomSPID() comment claimed "P(>8 retries) ≈ 0.4%"; actual is (256/65536)^8 ≈ 1.3e-19 (effectively zero). Code itself was always correct; only the comment was wrong.
    • Known Chess960 castling detection limitation (DOCUMENTED, NOT FIXED): Audit found that game-logic.js makeMv() and three other locations use Math.abs(to.col-from.col)===2 to detect castling, which only works when the king starts on col 4. In Chess960, the king's starting column can be 1-6, so when castling from a non-col-4 column (e.g., col 5 → col 6, abs=1), castling is not detected — the rook doesn't move, SAN shows Kg1 instead of O-O, and the Zobrist hash is wrong. Affects ~78.8% of Chess960 positions. Fixing this requires coordinated changes in 4 locations (makeMv/makeMvInPlace/moveAlg/Zobrist) with extensive testing — HIGH risk, so documented but not fixed in this round; deferred to a dedicated task. Note: standard chess (SP-ID 518) is unaffected since the king is always on col 4.
    • License files updated: chess.src/README.license, java/README.license, NOTICE all have Rev62 entries added.
    • Version unchanged: versionCode=105, versionName="1.0.5".
    • Chinese/English manuals synchronized to Rev62.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 61 (version unchanged, 2026.6.27)

    Per the 2026.6.27 development plan: fix the board anti-shake Y-axis direction-reversal bug, reduce rotation sensitivity to match user perception, fix the review-board yellow-square logic error, plus a first-principles code audit with several bug fixes.

    • Board anti-shake Y-axis direction-reversal bug fix (critical bug): All 4 screen-orientation cases (ROTATION_0/90/180/270) in StabilizationHelper.dispatchTransform() had the wrong sign on boardPxY. The OIS principle requires that when the device moves UP, the board moves DOWN to compensate (CSS +Y); the original code moved the board UP — amplifying the shake instead of cancelling it. User report: "屏幕突然向上移动，棋盘不但不向下位移来抵消，反而也向上" (when the screen suddenly moves UP, the board does NOT move DOWN to compensate, instead also moves UP). Fixed signs:
      • ROTATION_0: boardPxY = +dispY * SCALE (was -)
      • ROTATION_90: boardPxY = +dispX * SCALE (was -)
      • ROTATION_180: boardPxY = -dispY * SCALE (was +)
      • ROTATION_270: boardPxY = -dispX * SCALE (was +)
      X-axis signs were already correct and unchanged. After the fix, all 4 orientations' Y-axis direction satisfies the OIS cancellation principle.
    • Board rotation sensitivity adjustment (feature completion): User reported "棋盘旋转角度过于敏感，屏幕小幅度转动，棋盘就大幅度转动" (board rotation is too sensitive; a small screen rotation produces a large board rotation). The original code was mathematically 1:1 (boardRotDeg = -screenRollDelta), but MAX_ROTATION_DEG=45° (Rev60) was excessive and ROTATION_DEADZONE_DEG=0.3° was too small — sensor noise and sub-degree hand tremor were amplified into visible board "twitching". Two adjustments:
      • Dead zone 0.3° → 1.0°: filters sensor noise and sub-degree hand tremor, while staying below the rotation perceptual threshold and above the rotation-vector sensor's low-pass noise floor (~0.1°).
      • Max rotation ±45° → ±30°: covers the normal handheld tilt range (rarely exceeds 25°) while avoiding the visual abruptness of large counter-rotation at extreme angles. The 1:1 ratio is strictly preserved within the 1°–30° range.
    • Review-board yellow-square logic fix (critical bug): In ui.js _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations() and _computeInitialPositionAnnotations(), the yellow-square selection used total >= 2 as the criterion, which admitted single-side-dominated squares (e.g. 5 white attackers + 0 black = total 5) — but those squares should be BLUE (player net control). The user explicitly noted: "黄色格=双方总控制高格(当前未正确实现)" (yellow = both-sides high-total-control square, currently not correctly implemented). Fixed to pAtk > 0 && aAtk > 0 (both sides must have attackers for the square to be "contested"), then ranked by total to pick the top 3. This now correctly distinguishes "one-sided dominance" (blue/red) from "contested heat" (yellow).
    • Arrow stroke-linecap changed to butt (visual refinement): Changed the stroke-linecap of the review-board SVG arrow lines from "round" to "butt". With stroke-width=2, the round linecap created a small semi-circle at the arrow's start (which has no marker), visually reading as an "extra dot" — contradicting the user spec "箭头末端没有多余的圆点" (no extra dots at arrow endpoints). Butt linecap makes the line end square at the coordinate, eliminating the visible dot.
    • Engine extraction progress percentage integer-division truncation fix (bug fix): In StockfishNative.extractEngineFromAssets(), the original expression total / 114115752L * 13 evaluated left-to-right per Java rules: total / 114115752L truncated to 0 for any total < 114 MB, then 0 * 13 = 0. Progress stayed at 12% until extraction completed, then jumped to 25%. Fixed to total * 13L / 114115752L (multiply first, no precision loss).
    • stats.html unclosed-brace infinite-loop fix (critical bug): In stats.html PGN parsing, the original while(moveText.includes('{'))... would infinite-loop on a malformed PGN with an unclosed { (no matching }) — each regex iteration failed to match any paired braces, but includes('{') remained true → ANR. Fixed to a for loop capped at 10 iterations (well-formed PGN clears in 1 iteration).
    • StatsActivity stream leak fix (bug fix): StatsActivity.loadAssetAsBase64() originally used a manual is.close() that was only reached on the happy path — if baos.write threw (e.g. OOM on a large asset), the InputStream leaked. Switched to try-with-resources to guarantee closure.
    • License files updated: chess.src/README.license, java/README.license, NOTICE all have Rev61 entries added.
    • Version unchanged: versionCode=105, versionName="1.0.5".
    • Chinese/English manuals synchronized to Rev61.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 60 (version unchanged)

    Three changes per user spec: remove arrow origin dot, calibrate arrow offset to stay within cell bounds, expand rotation limit to ±45°. Note: Rev61 has since reverted ±45° back to ±30° (see Rev61 entry).

    • Arrow origin dot removed (visual improvement): Removed the small filled circle (r=2.5) that was drawn at each arrow's origin in the review-board SVG overlay. The arrowhead at the end is sufficient to indicate direction — the origin dot was visually redundant.
    • Arrow offset calibrated (visual improvement): Reduced the per-color diagonal offset magnitude from Math.min(6, cellSize*0.14) to Math.min(3, cellSize*0.08). The previous 14% (capped at 6px) could cause arrow endpoints to exceed the cell boundary on small screens. The new 8% (capped at 3px) stays safely within bounds for all cell sizes ≥ 30px.
    • Rotation limit expanded to ±45° (feature completion): Increased MAX_ROTATION_DEG in StabilizationHelper.java from ±2° to ±45°. The board's tilt-compensation rotation can now counter-rotate up to 45° in either direction to compensate for large device tilt. The low-pass filter (α=0.15) and dead zone (0.3°) ensure smooth, jitter-free rotation even at large angles.
