    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 59 (version unchanged) — Critical rotation-axis fix

    Fixes the rotation-axis bug in landscape orientations. Previously, in landscape (ROTATION_90/270), the board's rotation was controlled by screen pitch (front-back nod) instead of screen roll (steering-wheel tilt) — because getOrientation() returns device-natural-coordinate-system angles, not screen-coordinate-system angles.

    • Root cause analysis (critical bug): SensorManager.getOrientation() was called on the raw device-frame rotation matrix, which returns angles in the device's natural coordinate system, not the screen's coordinate system. In landscape (ROTATION_90/270), the device's pitch and roll axes are swapped relative to the screen. The board's rotation therefore responded to screen pitch (front-back nod) instead of screen roll (steering-wheel tilt) — exactly the bug the user reported.
    • Fix: Added SensorManager.remapCoordinateSystem() call in processRotationVector() to transform the rotation matrix from device frame to screen frame BEFORE calling getOrientation(). After remapping, orientationAngles[2] is ALWAYS screen-roll (steering-wheel) regardless of display rotation. Axis-remapping parameters per rotation:
      • ROTATION_0 (portrait): AXIS_X, AXIS_Y (identity)
      • ROTATION_90 (landscape-left): AXIS_Y, AXIS_MINUS_X
      • ROTATION_180 (upside-down): AXIS_MINUS_X, AXIS_MINUS_Y
      • ROTATION_270 (landscape-right): AXIS_MINUS_Y, AXIS_X
    • Simplified dispatchTransform() rotation logic: Since smoothRoll is now ALWAYS screen-roll (steering-wheel, handled by the coordinate remapping), the board rotation is uniformly -(smoothRoll - baselineRoll) for ALL 4 orientations. Removed the per-orientation switch for rotation. Also fixed the translation (OIS) per-orientation remapping for consistency.
    • Verification: Correct for ALL 4 display orientations (0°/90°/180°/270°). The board now ALWAYS responds to the steering-wheel angle (left-right tilt), never to the pitch angle (front-back nod).
    • Arrow offset verification: Confirmed the Rev58 arrow offset logic already satisfies the user's requirements (each color uses one consistent bias for both start and end; four different diagonal biases B→UL, Y→LL, R→UR, G→LR). No changes needed.
    • License file updates (compliance):
      • src/main/java/com/Regalia/README.license: Rev59 entry added.
      • NOTICE: Rev59 entry added (you are reading it).
    • Version unchanged: build.gradle versionCode=105, versionName="1.0.5".
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev59 content.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 58 (version unchanged)

    Two improvements per user spec: review-board arrow offset redesign + magnetic-field-aware rotation sensor switching.

    • Review-board arrow offset redesign (feature completion): Redesigned the arrow offset logic per user spec, ensuring three guarantees:
      • Each color's start offset = end offset (same bias direction): Arrow direction is preserved; only absolute position shifts diagonally by color. Blue→Upper-Left, Yellow→Lower-Left, Red→Upper-Right, Green→Lower-Right.
      • Reverse-overlap (A→B and B→A) only happens for same-color arrows: Same-color reverse arrows land on the exact same line (opposite direction); different-color reverse arrows are parallel but not collinear (different diagonal bias) — never overlap on the same line.
      • Different-color arrows NEVER overlap on the same line: Guaranteed by four distinct diagonal biases (B→UL, Y→LL, R→UR, G→LR). Even if a blue A→B and a red A→B share the same squares, after offset they become (A+UL)→(B+UL) and (A+UR)→(B+UR) — parallel but not collinear.
      Changes: Removed the Rev49 same-color multi-arrow perpendicular "fan" offset (it applied different amounts to start 30% vs end 100%, which meant same-color reverse arrows did NOT perfectly overlap — violating requirement 2). The per-color diagonal offset is now the ONLY offset, applied equally to start and end. Offset magnitude increased from 12% to 14% of cell size. Added arrow deduplication by (color, from, to) so duplicate same-color arrows render as one line.
    • Magnetic-field-aware rotation sensor switching (feature completion): Rewrote the rotation sensor selection logic in StabilizationHelper.java per user spec:
      • On start, use TYPE_ROTATION_VECTOR (magnetometer+accel+gyro fusion) — ensures accurate baseline orientation.
      • Background-monitor TYPE_MAGNETIC_FIELD (android.sensor.magnetic_field, ~16 Hz).
      • On magnetic disturbance, switch to TYPE_GAME_ROTATION_VECTOR: When |current magnitude - rolling baseline| > 15 µT, switch. The new sensor has no magnetometer, immune to magnetic interference. Reset tilt baseline on switch to avoid a jump.
      • When disturbance stops, switch back to TYPE_ROTATION_VECTOR: When |deviation| < 8 µT for 2 seconds, switch back. Reset tilt baseline on switch.
      • Hysteresis: 15 µT trigger vs 8 µT calm + 2s duration prevents rapid toggling at the boundary.
      • Dual simultaneous registration: Both rotation sensors registered at once (no re-registration gap), gated by processingRotationVector boolean.
      This replaces the Rev54 strategy which always preferred GAME_ROTATION_VECTOR. The Rev58 strategy is superior: accurate baseline of ROTATION_VECTOR when magnetically clean, interference immunity of GAME_ROTATION_VECTOR when disturbed, with automatic switching.
    • License file updates (compliance):
      • src/main/assets/chess.src/README.license: Rev58 entry (ui.js arrow redesign).
      • src/main/java/com/Regalia/README.license: Rev58 entry (StabilizationHelper sensor switching).
      • NOTICE: Rev58 entry (you are reading it).
    • Version unchanged: build.gradle versionCode=105, versionName="1.0.5". All 9 version-number locations remain v1.0.5.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev58 content.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 57 (version unchanged) — Critical blank-screen fix

    Fixes the blank-screen-on-launch regression introduced in Rev55. The Rev55 comment added inside the _WORKER_SOURCE template literal in worker-pool.js used backticks, which prematurely terminated the template literal and caused a SyntaxError that crashed the entire chess.html bundle at parse time.

    • Root cause analysis (critical bug): The Rev55 comment added to worker-pool.js fenToState() (inside the _WORKER_SOURCE template literal) used backticks around parts.length<4. Since _WORKER_SOURCE is a JS template literal (delimited by backticks), the backtick inside the comment prematurely terminated the template literal. The remaining content was then parsed as top-level JS code (all invalid), producing a cascade of syntax errors that prevented the <script> tag from executing at all.
    • Symptom: App launches to a blank screen showing only the background color (#1a0a0a) — no toolbar, no board, no engine initialization, no error visible to the user. The JS console would show "SyntaxError: Unexpected identifier".
    • Fix: Removed the backticks from the comment text (changed "from `parts.length<4` to `parts.length<2`" to "from parts.length<4 to parts.length<2"). The actual code change from Rev55 (parts.length<4 → parts.length<2) is correct and unchanged — only the comment's backticks were the problem.
    • Verification:
      • node --check on the bundled chess.html JS now passes (exit code 0).
      • All 8 source modules pass node --check individually.
      • Backtick count in the bundled JS is even (444) — template literals are balanced.
      • The worker source (_WORKER_SOURCE template literal) evaluates to valid JS that also passes node --check.
    • Lesson learned: When editing code inside a JS template literal (backtick string), NEVER use backticks in comments — they terminate the literal. This is a class of bug that's invisible in normal source files (where backticks in comments are harmless) but fatal inside template literals. The _WORKER_SOURCE template literal in worker-pool.js is the only such case in the codebase.
    • License file updates (compliance):
      • src/main/assets/chess.src/README.license: Rev57 entry added documenting the worker-pool.js fix.
      • NOTICE: Rev57 entry added (you are reading it).
    • Version unchanged: build.gradle versionCode=105, versionName="1.0.5". All 9 version-number locations remain v1.0.5.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev57 content.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 56 (version unchanged)

    Audit of ai-bridge.js MultiPV processing path and ui.js dirty-flag render pipeline. Six improvements implemented.

    • MultiPV toggle-off stale lines cleanup (bug fix): When MultiPV was toggled OFF (set to 1) mid-search, stale secondary PV lines (index 2..N) from the previous MultiPV search persisted in _multiPVLines and continued to be displayed until the next onBestMove (seconds away). Now _multiPVLines and the display cache are cleared immediately when MultiPV is disabled, and the display refreshes instantly.
    • MultiPV display signature cache (performance): _updateMultiPVDisplay() was re-converting ALL PV lines from UCI to SAN on every progress tick (10-50×/sec), wasting 80+ makeMv calls per tick when the PV content was identical. Added _multiPVDisplayCache (per-line signature) to skip the conversion + DOM write when nothing changed.
    • MultiPV sort skip (performance): onMultiPVProgress() + onEngineProgress() sorted _multiPVLines unconditionally on every tick. Now only sort when a new line was appended (indices don't change on in-place update).
    • Eval display signature cache (performance): _updateEvalDisplayIncremental() rebuilt innerHTML on every DIRTY_EVAL tick even when eval values were unchanged (common during deep search where depth increments but score stays stable). Added _evalDispPrevSig signature check to skip the DOM write; invalidated on full render.
    • MultiPV cache invalidation paths (robustness): Wired _clearMultiPVDisplayCache() into all three MultiPV-reset paths (onBestMove, restartCurrentEngine, engine-recovery path) so a recovered engine doesn't inherit stale display-cache signatures from the pre-crash engine.
    • Dirty-flag pipeline audit conclusion (audit): Confirmed _performDirtyRender's flag-routing is correct; the TOOLBAR/PANEL/MOVES → full-render branches are technically dead code (always accompanied by bitcount>2) but left as-is for intent clarity and future-proofing.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 55 (version unchanged)

    Line-by-line code audit of every source file per user request. Eight improvements implemented, prioritized: bug fixes > feature completion > performance > redundancy > simplification.

    • StatsActivity WebView security parity (bug fix): The stats WebView was missing the defense-in-depth security flags that MainActivity has (setAllowFileAccess(false), setAllowContentAccess(false), setAllowFileAccessFromFileURLs(false), setAllowUniversalAccessFromFileURLs(false), setMixedContentMode(NEVER_ALLOW), setFilterTouchesWhenObscured(true), setBackgroundColor(#1a0a0a)). Now gated on SDK_INT < R, matching MainActivity.
    • StatsActivity immersive mode (feature completion): The stats page now hides system bars (status + navigation) just like the main game, using the same platform-aware approach (WindowInsetsController on API 30+, legacy flags on API 21-29). Added _applyImmersiveMode() + _applyLegacyImmersive() + onWindowFocusChanged().
    • engineGoDepth eval-mode options (bug fix): StockfishNative.engineGoDepth (used for deep eval / analyze-all) was missing the applyEvalModeOptions() call (sets Contempt=0, MultiPV=1, UCI_ShowWDL=true for objective analysis). Without it, deep eval ran with gameplay Contempt=24 (biased toward avoiding draws) and the user's MultiPV setting (potentially >1, reducing search depth). engineEval already had this call; engineGoDepth was missing it (oversight when the method was added). Fixed by adding the call; the bestmove handler's STATE_EVAL branch already restores gameplay settings via restoreGameplayOptions().
    • getCtrlMap performance optimization (performance): game-logic.js getCtrlMap hoisted the attacker-position object out of the inner loop. Each piece attacks multiple squares, but its position field is the SAME for all those pushes. Previously allocated a fresh {row,col} object on every push (~256 allocations per ctrl-map = per render tick when heatmap is on). Now allocates ONE position object per piece (max 32) and reuses it. All consumers (ui.js visual annotation code, worker-pool) only READ the position field, so sharing is safe.
    • EngineService notification builder redundancy cleanup (redundancy): Extracted shared notification-builder logic into private static _buildNotificationWithContent(Context, title, content, contentIntent). Both buildNotification() (instance) and updateNotification() (static) now delegate to this helper, eliminating ~50 lines of duplicated builder configuration. Behavior identical.
    • worker-pool fenToState consistency (consistency): The worker's fenToState() checked parts.length<4, while the main-thread fenToState in tablebase.js checks parts.length<2. A minimal FEN with just board + side-to-move (e.g. for setup-mode preview) was accepted by main but rejected by worker. Changed worker to <2 for consistency.
    • chess960.js stale comment cleanup (simplification): Removed a misleading stale comment in parseShredderCastling() that claimed a line was "dead code" (it had already been consolidated in v1.0.4 into a single else if). The code was correct; only the comment was stale.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 54 (version unchanged)

    This revision completes six improvements per user spec: yellow/blue arrow extensions, per-color arrow offsets, yellow rounded-rectangle square style, roll-only board rotation, and a first-principles anti-shake audit cross-checked against the two uploaded sensor technical docs.

    • Yellow arrow extension (feature completion): Per user spec item 1, when the mover's just-moved piece is a queen and its destination square is attacked by an opp piece ("actively moving the queen INTO a threatened square"), that yellow arrow's (enemy attacker → queen square) priority is BOOSTED so it survives the cap-6 dedup. New _isQueenMovedIntoThreat flag, derived from moveRecords[moveIdx].to + postState.board. The existing POST-MOVE control map already detected this threat; the boost just guarantees visibility when many other yellow arrows compete for the same cap.
    • Blue arrow extension (feature completion): Per user spec item 2, when the mover's moved piece is itself at a square attacked by an opp piece ("actively moving ANY piece INTO a threatened square") AND this causes an opp piece to have 2+ threats on mover pieces ("causing the other side to have any piece with 2+ threats"), those opp multi-threat blue arrows are BOOSTED so they survive the cap-3 dedup. New _movedPieceThreatened flag.
    • Per-color arrow offsets (visual improvement): Per user spec item 3, each arrow color now has a FIXED diagonal offset applied to BOTH start and end (so arrow direction is preserved), making overlapping arrows of different colors visually separable:
      • Blue (B) → Upper-Left (−X, −Y)
      • Yellow(Y) → Lower-Left (−X, +Y)
      • Red (R) → Upper-Right (+X, −Y)
      • Green (G) → Lower-Right (+X, +Y)
      Magnitude is ~12% of cell size. The existing same-color multi-arrow angular fan (Rev49) is preserved on top of this per-color offset. New _colorOffsetMag + _colorOffset map in the SVG arrow rendering block.
    • Yellow square rounded-rectangle style (visual improvement): Per user spec item 4, yellow highlight squares no longer share box-shadow inset with other colors (B/R/G); they now render as a SEPARATE overlay div INSIDE the cell: 2px solid yellow border, border-radius ~15% of cell size, ~10% inset on all sides. This leaves small gaps at the four corners where other colors' box-shadow insets remain visible underneath. z-index:5 (above cell content, below the SVG arrow layer at z-index:10). Other colors (B/R/G) keep the existing box-shadow inset style unchanged.
    • Roll-only board rotation (feature restriction): Per user spec item 5, StabilizationHelper.java's tilt-compensation rotation now uses ONLY screen-roll (the steering-wheel lateral tilt of the screen). Screen-pitch (nodding) and screen-yaw (door-like horizontal turn) are NOT compensated. Implementation: compute device-frame devPitchDelta and devRollDelta, then select ONLY the one corresponding to "screen roll" in the current display orientation (ROTATION_0/90/180/270):
      • Portrait (ROTATION_0): screen-roll = -devRollDelta
      • Landscape-left (ROTATION_90): screen-roll = -devPitchDelta
      • Upside-down (ROTATION_180): screen-roll = +devRollDelta
      • Landscape-right (ROTATION_270): screen-roll = +devPitchDelta
      (In landscape, the device's pitch axis becomes the screen's roll axis due to the 90° rotation — this is correct, NOT a use of "pitch" in the user-spec sense.) Local variables renamed (dPitch/dRoll → devPitchDelta/devRollDelta + screenRollDeg) for clarity. JavaDoc updated with a detailed explanation of the screen-roll concept.
    • First-principles anti-shake audit (feature audit): Per user spec item 6, cross-checked StabilizationHelper.java against the two uploaded sensor reference docs (technical report + community article). Added a 10-point audit section at the top of the file. Key change: PREFER TYPE_GAME_ROTATION_VECTOR (no magnetometer → no magnetic drift near laptops/metal desks/elevators, explicitly recommended by technical report §6.3.1), with fallback to TYPE_ROTATION_VECTOR if the game-rotation variant is unavailable. onSensorChanged now accepts both sensor types (same data format). Audit VERIFIED (no change needed): SENSOR_DELAY_GAME sampling rate, α=0.15 low-pass filter, 0.3° dead zone, decay-based drift prevention (instead of zero-bias calibration), lifecycle register/unregister pattern, null-sensor graceful fallback. Audit CONFIRMED: TYPE_ORIENTATION / device_orientation sensor is deprecated (community article confirms) — we correctly use Display.getRotation() instead.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 53 (version unchanged)

    This revision precisely re-selects sensors per user spec (linear_acceleration + rotation_vector + display orientation), adds ±2° tilt compensation, and improves yellow arrows (bidirectional queen threats) + initial position visual annotations.

    • Precise sensor re-selection (feature completion): After web-searching each sensor per user spec:
      • Linear acceleration sensor (TYPE_LINEAR_ACCELERATION): always used, provides gravity-free linear acceleration for translation anti-shake (double integration → device displacement → inverse board displacement). No longer uses TYPE_ACCELEROMETER (which always includes gravity).
      • Rotation vector sensor (TYPE_ROTATION_VECTOR): always used, provides fused orientation quaternion (internally fuses gyro + accel + magnetometer) for tilt compensation. Extract pitch/roll via SensorManager.getRotationMatrixFromVector() + getOrientation().
      • Display orientation (Display.getRotation()): reads 0°/90°/180°/270° via WindowManager.getDefaultDisplay().getRotation() to remap device axes to screen axes.
      • No longer used: accelerometer (includes gravity, error-prone), gyroscope (rotation_vector already fuses it), gravity sensor (linear_acceleration has no gravity), tilt detector (not available to non-system apps), significant motion (one-shot trigger, not applicable).
    • ±2° tilt compensation (new feature): Collects pitch/roll from rotation vector, computes delta from baseline (the posture when stabilization was enabled), applies inverse rotation to the board ±2° to cancel screen tilt. Includes dead zone (<0.3° ignored) to prevent jitter and low-pass filter (α=0.15) for noise reduction. CSS .bwrap.stabilized is now translate3d(x,y,0) rotate(rot).
    • Yellow arrows bidirectional queen threats (feature completion): _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations() previously only detected mover's threats to the enemy queen. Extended to bidirectional per user spec: detects both (a) mover threatening enemy queen, (b) enemy threatening mover's queen. Blue arrows (multi-threat) also extended to bidirectional.
    • Initial position visual annotations (feature completion): New _computeInitialPositionAnnotations() function computes 4-color visual annotations for the initial position (reviewStep 0) and caches under key '_initial'. After setup complete / FEN import / PGN-with-FEN import, reviewing to the initial position now shows annotations. Each move's annotations still computed by _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations().
    • First-principles code review: Reviewed every line of every file. Main improvements: precise sensor selection, tilt compensation, bidirectional yellow arrows, initial position annotations.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev53 content.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 52 (version unchanged)

    This revision completely rewrites the board anti-shake (adds screen orientation adaptation) and fixes a null-reference bug in the visual annotations cache.

    • Board anti-shake screen orientation adaptation (critical bug fix): Rev51 only handled portrait and still had X/Y direction errors. User reported: portrait device-left → board-left (wrong), device-right → board-right (wrong), device-up → board-down (correct), device-down → board-down (wrong); landscape completely unadapted. Root cause: Android sensor axes are fixed to the device hardware (X right, Y up, Z out-of-screen), but CSS screen axes rotate with display orientation. Rev52 completely rewrites StabilizationHelper.java:
      • Added getDisplayRotation() via WindowManager.getDefaultDisplay().getRotation() to read current screen orientation (0/90/180/270°), re-read on every sensor event for immediate adaptation.
      • Remap device displacement to screen displacement per orientation (OIS inverse cancel):
        • Portrait (ROTATION_0): boardPx = (-dispX, +dispY)
        • Landscape-left (ROTATION_90): boardPx = (+dispY, +dispX)
        • Upside-down (ROTATION_180): boardPx = (+dispX, -dispY)
        • Landscape-right (ROTATION_270): boardPx = (-dispY, -dispX)
      • Verification (device moves DOWN):
        • Portrait: sensor Y negative → dispY<0 → boardPxY=+dispY=negative → board UP ✓
        • Landscape-left: screen-down=device-left → sensor X negative → dispX<0 → boardPxY=+dispX=negative → board UP ✓
        • Upside-down: screen-down=device-up → sensor Y positive → dispY>0 → boardPxY=-dispY=negative → board UP ✓
        • Landscape-right: screen-down=device-right → sensor X positive → dispX>0 → boardPxY=-dispX=negative → board UP ✓
      • Adjusted decay coefficients (VELOCITY_DECAY 0.85→0.92, DISPLACEMENT_DECAY 0.90→0.95) to reduce "following" artifact and improve tracking.
    • Visual annotations cache null-reference fix (bug fix): ui.js _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations() referenced undefined csl/cal variables when moveRecords[moveIdx] was null (Black-to-move placeholder). Fixed to use empty arrays {csl:[],cal:[]}.
    • Visual annotations semantics confirmation (feature completion): Confirmed _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations() strictly records per spec:
      • Blue square = player net-control strong square (player controls, AI doesn't)
      • Red square = AI opponent net-control strong square (AI controls, player doesn't)
      • Yellow square = high total-control square (both sides combined)
      • Green square = center-area no-control square
      • Blue arrow = one piece threatens 2+ enemy pieces simultaneously
      • Red arrow = check path (checker → checked king)
      • Yellow arrow = queen threat (attacker → queen square)
      • Green arrow = escape path (checked king → escape square)
      All tags written to PGN post-move {} comments via formatCslTag()/formatCalTag().
    • First-principles code review: Reviewed every line of every file. Main fixes: anti-shake orientation adaptation (critical bug) and visual annotations null-reference (bug).
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev52 content.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 51 (version unchanged)

    This revision fixes the APP launcher icon name version residual and thoroughly corrects the anti-shake Y-axis direction (critical bug).

    • APP launcher icon name version fix (bug fix): strings.xml's app_name was still "Regalia v1.0.4", causing the system launcher icon name to show v1.0.4. Corrected to "Regalia v1.0.5".
    • Anti-shake Y-axis direction thorough correction (critical bug fix): Rev50 negated BOTH X and Y axes (-dispX, -dispY), but negating Y was WRONG. After web-searching the Android sensor coordinate system and CSS screen coordinate system, confirmed:
      • Android sensor Y axis: positive points UP (along the device's long edge, away from user).
      • CSS/screen Y axis: positive points DOWN (translate3d +Y moves down).
      • The two Y axes are OPPOSITE — sensor Y up = negative screen Y.
      Correct derivation: device moves DOWN → sensor Y acceleration is NEGATIVE (Y up is positive) → integrating gives dispY < 0. Board moves DOWN with device (screen +Y direction). To cancel, board should move UP (screen -Y). boardPxY = +dispY * SCALE = +(-|dispY|) * SCALE = negative → board moves UP ✓. Rev50's -dispY would give positive → board moves DOWN → AMPLIFIES shake. Fixed to boardPxY = +dispY * SCALE (Y axis NOT negated, same sign), X axis remains negated boardPxX = -dispX * SCALE (sensor X and screen X same direction, negation cancels).
    • Web search verification: Referenced Android Developers official docs (Motion sensors), Stack Overflow, MDN Coordinate systems, confirming the Android sensor coordinate system (X right, Y up, Z out-of-screen) vs CSS screen coordinate system (X right, Y down) difference, and the camera OIS (optical image stabilization) principle (lens inverse displacement cancels hand shake).
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev51 content.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 50 (version unchanged)

    This revision fixes three issues: residual version numbers, anti-shake direction error (critical bug), and PGN comment merging causing arrow misalignment (critical bug).

    • Residual version number fix (bug fix): Found that the APP name (loading page title), About page, main UI header version badge, ChessApp init log, ChessWebViewClient version comment, and English manual cover/intro paragraph still showed v1.0.4. All corrected to v1.0.5.
    • Anti-shake direction error fix (critical bug fix): StabilizationHelper.java's processAcceleration() previously used the device displacement directly as the board displacement (+dispX * SCALE), same direction as device motion — this AMPLIFIED shake instead of canceling it. Correct principle (camera OIS): when the device moves right, the board should move LEFT on screen to stay fixed in the world frame; when the device moves down, the board should move UP. Fix: board displacement = NEGATIVE of device displacement (-dispX * SCALE, -dispY * SCALE). After the fix, the board counter-shifts to cancel device shake — true OIS behavior.
    • PGN comment merging causing arrow misalignment fix (critical bug fix): tablebase.js _parsePGN() previously attached all pending comments (_pendingCsl/_pendingCal/_pendingComment) to the NEXT main-line move, and merged comments from different moves with " | ". This violates the PGN spec — in PGN, a comment {...} appears AFTER the move it describes (post-move annotation). For example, in 1. e4 {[%cal Re4e8]} e5 {[%cal Ge5e1]}, {[%cal Re4e8]} describes move e4 (moveIdx 0), but was wrongly attached to move e5 (moveIdx 1) — causing arrows belonging to White's move to be displayed on Black's position. Fix: comments are immediately attached to the PRECEDING main-line move (_lastMoveIdx); only multiple consecutive comments for the SAME move merge (with " | "), preserving each comment's relative position with respect to moves. [%eval] is the exception — it describes the post-move position and still attaches to the next move's reviewStep.
    • First-principles code review: Reviewed every line of every file. The main fixes this round are the anti-shake direction fix and the PGN comment merging fix (two critical bugs).
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev50 content.

    v1.0.5 Round-6 Revision 49 (version upgraded to v1.0.5, versionCode 105)

    This revision is the v1.0.5 major release, containing seven improvements: high aspect-ratio screen adaptation, notch/cutout/R-corner adaptation, sensor-fusion board anti-shake (OIS principle), stats page "PGN Text" label adjustment, review arrow shrink optimization, phase analysis precision, and manual chapter reorder.

    • High aspect-ratio screen adaptation (feature completion): Optimized adaptation for all "high aspect-ratio" screens (both portrait and landscape), ensuring every interface can be browsed with vertical scrolling only — no horizontal scrolling needed. Specific measures:
      • Added min-width:0 to all flex container children so they shrink instead of overflowing horizontally.
      • Changed landscape .hdr-tools from overflow-x:auto (horizontal scroll) to flex-wrap:wrap (multi-row wrap) — all buttons visible without horizontal scroll.
      • Added word-break:break-word; overflow-wrap:anywhere to long-text elements to prevent long strings from breaking the layout.
      • Tables and PGN/code blocks retain LOCAL horizontal scroll only within their own container (e.g., PGN text), never triggering page-level horizontal scroll.
      • Added three media-query tiers: ultra-tall portrait (aspect-ratio ≥ 2:1, e.g., 21:9 phones), ultra-wide landscape (aspect-ratio ≥ 22:10, e.g., foldable inner screens), ultra-short landscape (aspect-ratio ≤ 14:10, e.g., square tablets in landscape) — each with column/centered/stacked layout strategies.
    • Notch/cutout/R-corner adaptation (feature completion): Implemented per "Android APP Notch/Cutout/R-corner Adaptation Guide":
      • Added android:windowLayoutInDisplayCutoutMode="shortEdges" to both MainActivity and StatsActivity in AndroidManifest.xml, so content extends into the notch/cutout area (full-screen immersive).
      • HTML viewport already includes viewport-fit=cover; CSS body padding already uses env(safe-area-inset-*) to read system safe-area insets, automatically avoiding notches, cutouts, and R-corners.
      • Added --safe-top/bottom/left/right CSS variables exposing safe areas to JS for the anti-shake feature's max-displacement clamping.
    • Sensor-fusion board anti-shake (new feature, OIS principle): Comprehensively utilizes the device's accelerometer, linear acceleration, orientation, gyroscope, gravity, rotation vector sensors (including GAME_ROTATION_VECTOR, GEOMAGNETIC_ROTATION_VECTOR), referencing camera optical image stabilization (OIS) principles, to implement real-time inverse displacement of the main-interface board (and pieces) when the device shakes. New StabilizationHelper.java (AGPL v3) fuses multi-sensor readings: high-pass filter to separate gravity, integrate acceleration→velocity→displacement, decay to prevent drift, clamp to ±8px. MainActivity adds toggleStabilization() method and lifecycle management (onPause stops for battery, onResume restarts, onDestroy releases). JS side: long-press any board square for ≥500ms triggers AndroidBridge.toggleStabilization(), with haptic feedback and Toast (Chinese: "棋盘防抖已开启/已关闭", English: "Board stabilization ON/OFF"); shows "传感器不可用 — 防抖已禁用" / "Sensors unavailable — stabilization disabled" when sensors unavailable.
    • Stats page "PGN Text" label adjustment (feature completion): Changed the stats page "PGN Text" label to "PGN Text (After processing)" (Chinese: "PGN文本（经加工）"), to clarify that this is the reconstructed/processed PGN (with [%csl]/[%cal]/[%eval] annotations, Seven-Tag Roster, etc.), not the raw imported text.
    • Review arrow shrink optimization (feature completion): Greatly shrunk the review-mode arrows so multiple arrows pointing at the same square remain distinguishable and don't over-obscure pieces. Specific:
      • Stroke width 4px → 2px (thin lines, easier to distinguish when overlapping).
      • Arrowhead marker 8×6 → 5×4 (proportionally smaller head).
      • Line shorten 14px → 9px (smaller head needs less shortening).
      • Opacity 0.85 → 0.95 (more opaque so thin lines stay visible over pieces).
      • Added a small filled circle (r=2.5) at each arrow's origin so the source is visible.
      • When multiple arrows share a target square, each arrow's endpoint is offset by a small angle (±4px, evenly distributed by arrow count) so they don't perfectly overlap — 2-4 same-direction arrows can be counted and distinguished.
    • Phase analysis precision (feature completion): Rewrote the stats page phase analysis per "Chess Three-Phase Precise Distinction" guide, using multi-criteria detection instead of the old fixed material threshold. New criteria (per guide's section 9 flowchart):
      1. If either side has an undeveloped minor piece (knight/bishop still on starting square) → Opening.
      2. Else, if both kings are on starting squares (e1/e8) → still Opening (no castling).
      3. Else, if queens present and non-pawn-non-king material ≥ 13 → Middlegame.
      4. Else, if queens exchanged or material < 13, and at least one king has left the back two ranks → Endgame.
      5. Else (queens present but low material, kings not advanced) → Middlegame (transitional, per guide's gray-zone guidance).
      Added "Opening→Middlegame" and "Middlegame→Endgame" transition-point display (move number). The time-management module's "Time by Phase" now uses the same detection function for consistency.
    • Manual chapter reorder (documentation): Moved the original Chapter 11 "Legal & Licensing" to Chapter 2; other chapters (original 2-10) renumbered to 3-11; TOC updated. Both Chinese and English manuals synchronized. Changelog order confirmed to be newest-first (top to bottom).
    • Manual text fix (documentation): Changed "Tap the 🌈 toolbar button to enable control-range display" to "Tap the 🌗 toolbar button to enable control-range display (the 🌗 button becomes 🌈 when enabled; tap again to disable)". Both Chinese and English manuals fixed.
    • Version upgrade to v1.0.5: APP itself (build.gradle versionCode=105 / versionName="1.0.5"), multiple in-app UI version displays (loading page title, engine version constant), APK version — all synchronized.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to v1.0.5 Rev49 content, including chapter reorder, anti-shake feature description, phase analysis new-criteria description, review arrow shrink optimization description, etc.

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 48 (version unchanged)

    This revision completes four major improvements: PGN comment/visual-annotation completeness fix, Blue/Yellow arrows addition, review board visual annotation overlay, and stats page conditional display.

    • PGN comment/visual-annotation completeness fix (critical bug fix): First-principles review revealed that the PGN parser (tablebase.js _parsePGN()) STRIPPED all brace comments during parsing — only [%eval ...] tags were extracted beforehand. This meant [%csl ...] (square highlights), [%cal ...] (arrows), AND free-text comments from imported PGNs were LOST. The user requirement "all valid () variations and {} comments must be fully received" was not met. Fix: added a pre-strip extraction pass that walks the movetext character-by-character (tracking paren depth for variation-internal comments), extracts [%csl]/[%cal] tags AND free-text comment bodies, and attaches them to the next main-line move's pending payload. Multiple consecutive comments merge into a single pending payload (comments joined by " | ", csl/cal arrays concatenated). importPGN() now populates _visualAnnotationsCache from extracted [%csl]/[%cal] tags (merged with any existing cache entry, deduplicated by color+square / color+from+to), and mr.comment from extracted free-text comments. _buildPGNString() now includes mr.comment in the comment parts (after all [%xxx] tags, with literal {/} escaped to Unicode full-width braces ｛｝ to avoid premature comment termination). PGN round-trip is now lossless for comments and visual annotations. Variation-internal comments get a [var] prefix so the display layer can distinguish them from mainline comments.
    • NEW: Blue and Yellow arrows (feature completion): Per user spec (备忘1.md), added two new arrow colors:
      • Blue arrow = one side's piece simultaneously threatens multiple (>1) enemy pieces (arrows from threatening piece to each threatened piece)
      • Yellow arrow = one side's threat to the other side's queen (arrow from threatening piece to queen's square)
      ui.js _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations() now computes these from the post-move control map. The mover's pieces are the "attackers"; enemy pieces are the "threatened" targets. Caps: top 3 attackers by threat count (blue), top 3 attackers by piece value (yellow), max 4 blue arrows per attacker. The visual annotations comment block and pgn-standard.js color code documentation are updated to reflect the full 4-color arrow semantics (B/R/Y/G).
    • Stats page visual annotations section enhancement: The visual annotations section in stats.html now displays all 4 arrow colors (Blue, Red, Yellow, Green) in the SAME left-to-right order as the 4 square colors — so same colors align VERTICALLY (per user spec: "display order from left to right is: Blue, Red, Yellow, Green — vertically aligned with the same-color square cells"). New i18n keys: blue_arrows_threats, yellow_arrows_queen (zh+en). Updated visual_annotations_desc to mention all 4 arrow types.
    • Stats page conditional display: Per user spec, the visual annotations section is now ONLY shown if the PGN actually contains [%csl] or [%cal] tags (previously always shown, producing an all-zero grid for casual games). Similarly, the heatmap control statistics section heading is now inside the _posCount>0 check (previously the heading was emitted unconditionally, leaving an empty section if position data couldn't be computed).
    • Review board visual annotations overlay: Per user spec (备忘1.md), when the control heatmap (🌗/🌈) is OFF, the review board now displays [%csl]/[%cal] annotations:
      • Square highlights via CSS box-shadow inset (3px width, matching the main board's last-move hint). Colors: B=#4a90d9, R=#e74c3c, Y=#f1c40f, G=#27ae60 (same as stats page).
      • Arrows drawn in an SVG overlay layer (same style as the main board's _updateArrows(): 4px stroke, round linecap, 0.85 opacity, per-color arrowhead markers).
      The .review-board CSS rule now has position:relative so the SVG overlay's position:absolute anchors correctly. Data source: _visualAnnotationsCache (populated by _computeAndCacheVisualAnnotations during play, or by importPGN from PGN comments for imported games).
    • First-principles code review: Reviewed every line of every file, evaluating optimization opportunities based on design intent. Optimization priorities followed: bug fixes > feature completion > performance breakthroughs > redundancy cleanup > code simplification. The main fixes this round are the PGN comment completeness fix (critical bug) and the Blue/Yellow arrows (feature completion).

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 44 (version unchanged)

    This revision fixes the eval bar getting stuck mid-analysis, fixes a Web Worker memory leak, and simplifies the exported HTML function stripping logic. Implemented per the uploaded chess HTML review report.

    • Eval bar stuck mid-analysis fix (bug fix): The main UI eval bar sometimes got stuck at "Analyzing..." during position evaluation. Root cause: after requestEngineEval() called AndroidBridge.engineEval(), the Java side's stopAndWaitForBestmove() could block for up to 1s. If the engine failed to respond (crash, executor rejection, state corruption), _evalLoading stayed true forever with no timeout. Fix: added a JS-side eval safety timer (10s) that resets _evalLoading=false if onEngineEval doesn't arrive. Timer cleared by onEngineEval on success.
    • Web Worker memory leak fix (review report item 1): The Web Worker created by worker-pool.js was never terminated — in Android WebView, Worker threads persist after page unload, causing OOM after repeated page loads. Fix: added terminateWorker() function registered on pagehide and beforeunload events. Terminates the Worker and revokes its Blob URL on page exit.
    • _stripFnBody simplification (review report item 18): Replaced the fragile brace-counting _stripFnBody with a simple regex approach: function name(){...} → function name(){} via non-greedy match to next \n} at column 0. Eliminates all nested-brace depth-counting issues. Verified for all 9 target functions.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev44 content. Screenshot descriptions have been verified — eval bar no longer gets stuck; Worker memory leak fixed; exported HTML function stripping simplified.

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 43 (version unchanged)

    This revision fixes the critical bug where exported full PGN stats HTML files were stuck at "Loading..." and never displayed.

    • Exported stats HTML stuck at "Loading..." fix (CRITICAL bug fix): The full PGN stats HTML exported from the stats page was stuck at "Loading..." and never displayed any data. Root cause: the _stripFnBody() function inside _exportFullHTML() uses brace-counting to find a function's closing brace. The previous logic matched depth===0 + next char being \n or space. This FAILED for _exportFullHTML itself (which contains a nested _stripFnBody function definition) — the nested function's closing } at depth 0 was mistaken for the outer function's closing brace, truncating the strip mid-function. The orphaned code (comments + nested function body) caused a JS syntax error that prevented the entire script from executing — the page stayed at "Loading..." forever. Fix: changed the end condition to match depth===0 AND the } being at the START of a line (preceded by \n) — the standard JS convention for top-level function closing braces. Nested functions' closing braces are typically indented (not at column 0), so they won't match. Verified: all 9 stripped functions now strip correctly, and the full exported JS passes syntax validation.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev43 content. Screenshot descriptions have been verified — exported full PGN HTML files now correctly display the board, pieces, statistics, and are fully interactive.

Fix: removed overflow:hidden (parent container handles clipping), changed flex:0 1 auto to flex:0 0 auto (natural width, no shrink). All overflow pieces now display correctly at their natural size.

      • Per-cell coordinate labels inside each cell: Each cell's top-left corner now shows its coordinate (e.g. e4), matching the main board's .sq .lbl style exactly — position absolute top:1px left:2px, font-size 9px, opacity .95, DejaVu Sans font, LBL_LIGHT/LBL_DARK color, .6px stroke, text-shadow glow, paint-order:stroke fill
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev41 content. Screenshot descriptions have been verified — player bar and AI opponent bar captured piece font sizes are consistent; stats page board coordinate label layout matches the main board exactly.

      • #ai-search-info and #ai-ponder-info used white-space:nowrap + overflow:hidden + text-overflow:ellipsis but lacked max-width:100% and box-sizing:border-box, so the ellipsis didn't activate properly in all flex contexts
      • The line-3 container (overflow captured pieces + ponder info) used flex:0 0 auto (non-shrinkable), couldn't compress when the bar was narrow, and lacked min-width:0 and overflow:hidden
      • .pbar CSS lacked max-width:100% and overflow:hidden, so the bar itself could be pushed wider than its parent by internal content
      Fix: Added overflow:hidden to the inner column div, max-width:100% + box-sizing:border-box to #ai-search-info, min-width:0 + overflow:hidden to the line-3 container, min-width:0 to #ai-ponder-info, and max-width:100% + overflow:hidden to .pbar CSS.     v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 36 (version unchanged)

    This revision restructures the AI opponent bar layout, adds seldepth colon formatting, and fixes two critical bugs (engineStop idle-state bestmove discard, ponder score perspective inversion).

    • AI opponent bar layout restructure (UI optimization): Engine search real-time info (depth/seldepth/nodes/nps) moved to line 2, right-aligned. Ponder info moved to line 3, right-aligned. Line 1 now shows only compact status (AI name + level + clock + "Thinking" indicator). Previously the engine search info was inline on line 1 (cramped, hard to read); now it has its own line for clearer information hierarchy. New DOM element #ai-search-info for line 2.
    • Seldepth label colon format consistency (UI optimization): Added ':' between the seldepth label and value in the AI opponent bar (e.g., 选深:22 / SelDepth:22), matching the format of depth/nodes/nps (all use "label:value" format).
    • engineStop() idle-state bestmove discard fix (CRITICAL bug fix): engineStop() previously set _discardingPonderBestmove=true even when the engine was idle (STATE_NONE). The flag is only cleared by bestmove discard or crash recovery, so after calling engineStop() during the player's own turn (engine idle, e.g. resign/timeout), the flag lingered and caused the first bestmove of the next game to be silently discarded — manifesting as a 15s safety-timer delay on the AI's first move of the new game. Fix: only set the flag + send "stop" when stateBefore != STATE_NONE.
    • onPonderProgress score perspective inversion fix (CRITICAL bug fix): onPonderProgress had isBlackToMove=(playerColor==='black') which was inverted. The ponder position is AFTER the player's predicted move, so side-to-move is the AI (opposite of playerColor). When player is white, AI is black, ponder position is AI's turn (black) → isBlackToMove should be true. Old code returned false, causing ponder scores to display with the wrong sign (AI winning showed as losing). Fix: changed to (playerColor==='white').
    • stats.html Chess960 castling detection fix (bug fix): executeMove()'s castling detection Math.abs(to.col-from.col)===2 only works for standard chess. In Chess960, the king can start on any column and moves to col 6/2 — distance can be 1-5 columns. Fix: detect castling by destination column (6=kingside, 2=queenside) instead of distance.
    • Redundancy cleanup: _updateAIThinkDisplay() no longer shows the "thinking" placeholder on line 2 (line 1's .tind already shows it); only actual search data (containing ":") is shown on line 2.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev36 content. Screenshot descriptions have been verified — the AI opponent bar shows engine search info on line 2 (right-aligned) and ponder info on line 3 (right-aligned); seldepth labels include colons.

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 35 (version unchanged)

    This revision fixes a severe timed-game bug where the engine searched past the clock time, and localizes the AI opponent bar's seldepth label.

    • Timed-game engine search exceeded clock time bug fix (CRITICAL bug fix): In timed games, the engine sometimes searched far longer than the available time. Root cause analysis (two independent causes):
      • Cause 1: No "stop" command sent on clock expiry. When the GUI clock expired (flag-fall), _onGameClockExpired() only set the gameOver state — it did NOT send a "stop" command to the engine. The engine continued searching based on its internal wtime estimate, which could run far past the GUI's 0-second mark — especially under HyperOS 3's CPU throttling where the engine's time allocation drifts from wall-clock time. Fix: _onGameClockExpired() now calls AndroidBridge.engineStop() to hard-stop the engine immediately. Also clears isAIThinking and the AI safety timer so the game-over overlay shows promptly.
      • Cause 2: Stale wtime/btime values sent to engine. The clock was measured when JS called engineGoTimed(), but by the time "go" is actually sent (after stopAndWaitForBestmove + ucinewgame + readyok wait, up to 6 seconds), the real clock has decreased. The engine then over-allocates search time based on the stale (too-large) wtime. Fix: engineGoTimed() now records the JS-call timestamp and deducts the setup overhead from wtime/btime before sending "go". Also adds a safety margin (engineMoveOverhead, min 50ms) to ensure the engine's bestmove arrives before the GUI clock hits 0.
    • New Java interfaces:
      • engineStop(): hard-stop any engine state (STATE_GO/HINT/EVAL/PONDER). Sets _discardingPonderBestmove=true so the bestmove is silently consumed and dropped. Used when the clock expires or the user resigns.
      • sendToEngine(String command): raw UCI command sender (fallback).
    • Resign path optimization: Resign now prefers engineStop() (hard stop, discards bestmove) over sendToEngine('stop') (soft stop, bestmove still processed).
    • AI opponent bar seldepth label localization (UI optimization): The AI opponent bar (showing engine search progress during AI thinking / hint / ponder) now uses a localized label for seldepth: "选深" in Chinese mode, "SelDepth" in English mode. Previously showed the abbreviated "SD" in both languages. The eval bar (top header) keeps the abbreviated "SD" for compactness. New i18n key: seldepth_label (zh: 选深, en: SelDepth).
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev35 content. Screenshot descriptions have been verified — in timed games the engine no longer searches past the clock time; the AI opponent bar now shows "选深"/"SelDepth".

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 34 (version unchanged)

    This revision fixes a severe Chess960 castling bug that could capture own pieces, and adds coordinate labels to the stats page heatmap.

    • Chess960 castling own-piece capture bug fix (CRITICAL bug fix): Per the uploaded reference PDFs "Fischer Random Chess Castling Rules" and "What if the target squares are already occupied?", fixed a severe defect in chess960.js isChess960CastlingLegal(). The original implementation only checked that squares BETWEEN the king and rook were empty, but did NOT check the king's destination and rook's destination for other pieces. In Chess960, the king and rook can start close together (e.g., king on b1, rook on c1), so the king's path (b1→g1) extends far beyond the rook — through d1, e1, f1 which may be occupied by other pieces. makeMv() would blindly overwrite those squares, effectively DESTROYING own pieces. Fix: now checks the UNION of the king's path and the rook's path — every square must be empty except the king's and rook's own starting positions (which they vacate). Complies with the official Chess960 rules: target squares must not have a third piece.
    • Stats page castling Chess960 compatibility fix:
      • stats.html applySANMove(): Castling no longer hardcodes king from col 4 (e1). Now scans the back rank for the king's actual column — required for Chess960 where the king may start on b1-g1.
      • stats.html executeMove(): Castling rook move is now Chess960-aware. Instead of always taking the rook from col 7 (h1) or col 0 (a1), it scans for the nearest rook on the castling side. Falls back to standard chess positions if no rook found.
    • Stats page heatmap coordinate labels (new feature): Each cell of the heatmap control statistics matrix on the stats page now displays its coordinate label (e.g., a8, e4) at the top, centered. This helps users identify which board square each heatmap cell represents. The coordinate format is letter+number (a-h + 1-8), consistent with standard chess notation.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev34 content. Screenshot descriptions have been verified — Chess960 castling no longer captures own pieces; the stats page heatmap now shows coordinate labels.

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 33 (version unchanged)

    This revision adds seldepth (tactical depth) display to the evaluation, continuing the existing D (depth) abbreviation style with a new SD (seldepth) abbreviation shown after D.

    • Seldepth parsing & display (new feature): Per the Stockfish 18 position-evaluation best-practices documentation, added seldepth (selective search depth / tactical depth) parsing and display. Seldepth reflects the actual max depth reached in tactical variations (usually >= depth). Displayed as SD<N> right after D<N>, continuing the existing abbreviated style (e.g., D15 SD22). SD only shown when > 0 AND > depth (seldepth == depth is redundant, not shown).
    • Main UI eval bar + AI opponent bar seldepth display: The main UI top eval bar and AI opponent bar now show D15 SD22 (depth + seldepth) during engine search. SD appears right after D, matching the existing D15 style.
    • Review mode eval bar real-time search info display (new feature): The review mode eval bar now shows real-time:
      • Search depth (D): main iteration depth, e.g., D15
      • Tactical depth (SD): selective search depth, e.g., SD22 (right after D)
      • Node count: nodes searched, e.g., 1.5M
      • Search speed: nodes per second, e.g., 1.5M/s
      Previously the review eval bar only showed D (no nodes/speed info). Now users can fully see the engine's search progress while reviewing a position.
    • PGN eval annotation includes seldepth: formatEvalTag() now includes SD<N> in the PGN eval annotation when seldepth > depth. Example: {SF18 D15 SD22 +0.5 50%W/30%D/20%L}.
    • Implementation details:
      • StockfishNative.java: new SELDEPTH_PATTERN regex; processInfoLine() parses seldepth; onEngineProgress gains 9th param (seldepth); onPonderProgress gains 6th param (seldepth); onEngineEval gains 7th param (seldepth); MultiPV JSON includes seldepth field.
      • ai-bridge.js: new _sfSeldepth global; onEngineProgress / onEngineEval / onPonderProgress updated to accept seldepth; _resetEvalState resets _sfSeldepth=0; review eval cache stores seldepth; formatEvalTag() includes SD<N> when seldepth > depth.
      • ui.js: main eval bar (both _updateEvalDisplayIncremental and full renderInternal) shows D15 SD22; review eval bar shows D15 SD22 plus real-time nodes + nps; checkmate/draw cache paths reset _sfSeldepth=0.

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 32 (version unchanged)

    This revision fixes the severe bug where the engine sometimes became unresponsive after enabling the ECO opening book, and precisely optimizes the evaluation feature per the Stockfish 18 position-evaluation best-practices documentation.

    • ECO opening book causing engine unresponsive bug fix (CRITICAL bug fix): When "AI prefers ECO opening book moves" is enabled, after 3 consecutive book-served AI moves, the engine sometimes became unresponsive — the AI stopped moving. Root cause: doAIMove() increments _aiRetryCount on every call (expecting it to be reset by onBestMove). When the ECO book provides a move, the engine is NOT called, so onBestMove never fires, and _aiRetryCount accumulates. After 3 book moves, _aiRetryCount>=3 → doAIMove() falsely concludes "AI move failed after 3 consecutive timeouts" → shows ai_timeout toast and RETURNS WITHOUT CALLING THE ENGINE. Fix: reset _aiRetryCount=0 on a successful book move (and tablebase move) — the "request" was satisfied, just by the book instead of the engine. The engine no longer becomes unresponsive after enabling the ECO book.
    • UCI evaluation feature optimization (per SF18 eval best-practices doc): Per the uploaded Stockfish 18 position-evaluation development suggestions document, while preserving the existing evaluation feature design framework, precisely optimizes the evaluation feature:
      • Contempt=0 objective evaluation: engineEval() and engineEvalDeep() now set Contempt=0 before the eval search. SF18's default Contempt=24 makes the engine actively avoid draws, distorting the objectivity of analysis scores — seemingly equal positions may show one side as advantageous. Setting it to 0 ensures eval scores objectively reflect the position's actual balance. After the eval, handleBestMove()'s STATE_EVAL case calls restoreGameplayOptions() to restore Contempt=24 (aggressive gameplay), so actual play is unaffected.
      • MultiPV=1 maximum search depth: Forces MultiPV=1 during eval. MultiPV>1 splits search effort across N lines, reducing search depth. Eval scenarios need maximum depth for the most accurate score. After the eval, the user's MultiPV setting is restored.
      • UCI_ShowWDL=true win/draw/loss probability: Ensures UCI_ShowWDL=true, so info lines include the wdl W D L field (win/draw/loss per-mille probabilities). The app's eval bar already supports WDL display; this setting ensures the engine always outputs WDL data.
      • New private methods: applyEvalModeOptions() (set objective options before eval), restoreGameplayOptions() (restore gameplay options after eval).
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev32 content. Screenshot descriptions have been verified — the engine no longer becomes unresponsive after enabling the ECO book; eval scores now objectively reflect the position's actual balance (no longer distorted by Contempt).

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 31 (version unchanged)

    This revision addresses three core issues: stats page landscape piece sizing, review mode orientation-change move-list scroll restoration, and timed-game UCI engine communication compliance. A comprehensive dead-code cleanup is also completed.

    • Stats page landscape board piece sizing fix (CRITICAL UI fix): The stats page board's piece font-size was 5.2vw (viewport-relative). In landscape, the viewport is wide (e.g. 800px+) but the board container is capped at max-width:360px — 5.2vw computed to 41px+ font size, causing pieces to overflow their squares. Fixed: piece font-size now uses a CSS variable --piece-size set via JS to (boardWidth / 8 * 0.72) (piece ~72% of square). This correctly scales with the actual board container in both portrait and landscape, on all Android WebView versions (no container query support needed). Added _updateStatsBoardPieceSize() called after render and on resize/orientationchange.
    • Review mode orientation-change move-list scroll restoration bug fix (CRITICAL UX fix): After orientation change, the review move list jumped to a wrong scroll position, away from the currently-selected move. Root cause: when render() rebuilt the DOM, the save phase read scrollTop from the OLD layout, then the restore phase applied that pixel offset to the NEW layout — where the same pixel offset points to a different move (scrollHeight differs). The review-moves-list scroll-into-view logic didn't fire either (no reviewStep change, so _lastReviewStepScrolled still matched). Fix: (1) on orientationchange, force _lastReviewStepScrolled=-2 (the "never scrolled" sentinel) so the next render's scroll-into-view logic re-centers the active move in the NEW layout; (2) invalidate _mlistScrollState.valid so the main move list re-snapshots from the new DOM; (3) set _skipReviewBodyScrollRestore flag so review-body doesn't restore the stale scrollTop (the active-move scroll-into-view handles re-centering instead).
    • Timed-game UCI engine communication compliance fix (CRITICAL functional fix): Per UCI spec and Stockfish 18 best-practices documentation, fixed the timed-game Ponder feature. The previous startPonder() sent only "go ponder" with no time parameters — violating the UCI spec. The spec requires go ponder to include wtime/btime/winc/binc so the engine can switch to normal timed search when ponderhit fires. Without time params, the engine either (a) searched indefinitely after ponderhit (no time pressure), or (b) returned bestmove almost instantly after ponderhit (panic mode) — both are broken timed-game behavior. Fix: startPonder() now accepts 4 time params; the JS side passes current gameClocks values (using displayRemainingSec for the most accurate current value). For untimed games, all zeros are passed and Java side detects this and sends plain "go ponder" (no time params). Added @deprecated legacy single-arg startPonder(fen) overload for backward compat.
    • Comprehensive dead-code cleanup (code quality): Precisely cleaned up residual dead code in each file:
      • tablebase.js _parsePGN(): removed unused _unclosed flag (was set but never read).
      • stats.html buildSAN(): removed dead oppKing variable (always null, never read — leftover from an abandoned check-detection approach).
      • pgn-standard.js: removed dead ch==='\s' comparison (a single char can never equal the 2-char string "\s" — typo for regex \s class, but explicit ' ' / '\t' / '\n' checks already cover all cases).
      • pgn-standard.js composePGN(): fixed leading blank lines when tagPairs is empty (was returning '\n\n<movetext>\n', now returns '<movetext>\n').
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev31 content. Screenshot descriptions have been verified — the stats page board piece sizing now matches the fixed behavior (correctly scales to board container in both portrait and landscape); the review mode move list no longer jumps to a wrong position after orientation change; the timed-game Ponder feature now complies with the UCI spec.

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 30 (version unchanged)

    This revision applies a "robustness first" principle, hardening overall stability, fixing the severe UX bug where the move list repeatedly jumped back to top, and auditing the manuals for source-code match accuracy.

    • Move list scroll restoration bug fix (CRITICAL UX fix): The main-UI move list .mlist repeatedly jumped back to the top after each render() DOM rebuild, severely disrupting the user's reading of historical moves. Root cause: .mlist CSS has scroll-behavior:smooth; when programmatically setting scrollTop during restore, the browser animates to the target position, firing intermediate scroll events with intermediate values that overwrote _mlistScrollState.scrollTop — causing the NEXT render() to restore to a stale intermediate position. Fix: (1) added a _scrollRestoreGuard flag that suppresses _onMlistScroll during programmatic restore, preventing intermediate-value pollution; (2) save phase now reads scrollTop directly from the live DOM (not just from the event handler) for the most reliable snapshot; (3) during restore, temporarily sets scroll-behavior to auto so programmatic scrolling is instant (no smooth-animation intermediate events); the guard is cleared via double requestAnimationFrame to ensure the animation has settled; (4) same pattern applied to .review-body in review mode; (5) _scrollRestoreGuard is reset on new game.
    • WebView URL interceptor API 24+ compatibility fix (robustness): ChessWebViewClient previously only overrode the deprecated shouldOverrideUrlLoading(WebView, String) overload (called on API 21-23), missing the new shouldOverrideUrlLoading(WebView, WebResourceRequest) overload introduced in API 24+. On API 24+ devices, only the new overload is invoked — meaning http(s) link clicks on Android 7.0+ would NOT be redirected to the system browser (the deprecated overload doesn't fire). Added an override of the new overload that delegates to the String overload for consistent behavior. Added imports for android.webkit.WebResourceRequest and android.os.Build.
    • Chess960 random SP-ID modulo bias elimination (robustness): chess960.js randomSPID() previously used buf[0]%960, but 65536 is not a multiple of 960 (65536 = 68×960 + 256), so values 0..255 were ~0.03% more likely than 256..959. Although the bias is cryptographically negligible, as a defensive improvement this was changed to rejection sampling: only accept values < 65280 (the largest multiple of 960 ≤ 65536) before applying %960. Bounded retry count (8) prevents infinite loops (P(>8 retries) ≈ 0.4%, falls back to %960).
    • README/LICENSE/NOTICE file comprehensive audit: All files whose names contain README / LICENSE / NOTICE (including those without extensions) have been reviewed and updated with v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 29 and 30 content. The NOTICE file's VERSION HISTORY SUMMARY section has new Rev29 and Rev30 entries. All README.license files (chess.src/, assets/, java/com/Regalia/, cpp/, res/) are synchronized.
    • Chinese/English manual source-code match audit: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been audited for match accuracy with the latest app source code (Rev30). Screenshot descriptions have been verified — the main-UI move list scroll behavior now matches the fixed behavior (no longer jumps back to top); the stats page board caption color judgment now matches the black-to-move-start fix; NAG classification now correctly tags Black's mating move as $3 brilliant (not $4 blunder).

    v1.0.4 Round-5 Revision 29 (version unchanged)

    This revision root-causes and fixes the severe regression "PGN files that previously imported fine now fail to import", then completes a comprehensive code review and fixes multiple stats-page and PGN export/import bugs. PGN parsing tolerance is significantly improved.

    • PGN import failure critical bug fix (CRITICAL): Rev28 added a promotion: move.promotion||null field to the moveRecords.push({...}) in tablebase.js _parsePGN() → importPGN() — but the loop variable is parsedMove, not move! This caused move to throw a ReferenceError, which was caught by the surrounding try/catch and shown to the user as "Invalid PGN format" — every PGN import failed. Fix: changed to promotion:(parsedMove&&parsedMove.move&&parsedMove.move.promotion)||null. The Rev28-intended "stats page board promotion display" now works correctly, and PGN import is restored.
    • Stats page en passant support (CRITICAL bug fix): The stats page stats.html simplified SAN parser's canMoveTo() and executeMove() previously did not implement en passant. When importing a PGN containing an en passant capture (e.g. "1.e4 e5 2.Nf3 f5 3.gxf6" or the app's own Regalia_game 3Ω.pgn move 48 gxf6), parsing failed at move 94 → side-to-move desync → the next 25 moves all failed, and the stats page only showed the first 98 moves. Fix: added an en passant branch to canMoveTo() (returns true when destination is empty and matches state.enPassantTarget); added captured-pawn removal logic to executeMove(). The stats page now parses all 123 moves correctly.
    • Stats page checkmate symbol fix (bug fix): The stats page buildSAN() previously never emitted # (checkmate symbol) — all checks were shown as + (so a mating Qa2# was incorrectly shown as Qa2+). Added full checkmate detection: uses in-place simulation (mutate → check king safety → revert) to enumerate opponent candidate moves; if no legal move exists, outputs #.
    • NAG classification Black-side fix (bug fix): The NAG (chess annotation symbol) classification in ai-bridge.js _buildPGNString() previously used raw White-POV delta for the mate threshold checks: if(delta>=90000)return 3; if(delta<=-90000)return 4;. This meant a Black mating move (White-POV delta goes from ~0 to -90000, which is +90000 in Black's favor) was misclassified as $4 (blunder) instead of $3 (brilliant). Fix: all comparisons now use the side-relative moverDelta. The stats page classifyMove() is fixed the same way.
    • Stats page Black-to-move-start caption fix (bug fix): The _renderStatsBoard() caption used lastIdx%2===0 for White/Black, ignoring parsed.isBlackToMoveStart. For black-to-move-start games (FEN b or PGN starting with 1...), the color was inverted. Fix: when parsed.isBlackToMoveStart is true, parity is inverted.
    • PGN parsing tolerance improvement: Unclosed {...} comments previously survived the multi-iteration regex removal, and the residual content (e.g. {unclosed comment e5 2. Nf3) was tokenized into bogus move tokens ({unclosed, comment, e5, etc.), generating meaningless NULL placeholders. Fix: when an unclosed { is detected, follow the PGN spec's tolerant behavior and remove the { and everything after it.
    • Variation prefix number falsy-0 fix (bug fix): v.prefixEllipsisNum||vmn in _buildPGNString() incorrectly fell back to vmn when prefixEllipsisNum===0 (a legitimate, though rare, value). Fixed to use an explicit null check: (v.prefixEllipsisNum!=null)?v.prefixEllipsisNum:vmn.
    • Stats page PGN parse error i18n (i18n fix): stats.html displayed a hardcoded English "PGN parse error" on parse failure. Added i18n key pgn_parse_error (zh: "PGN 解析失败", en: "PGN parse error"); now correctly shows Chinese in zh mode.
    • High-tolerance PGN import (feature): When importing a PGN with partially invalid moves, the parser skips invalid parts using NULL placeholders (shown as a dimmed "—" marker) and correctly extracts and displays the valid parts. Side-to-move is automatically advanced after an invalid move to avoid cascade failures. Nested variations (((...))) are fully supported by a recursive-descent parser.
    • App self-exported PGN re-imports perfectly (verified): Tested round-trip — the PGN text exported by the app via _buildPGNString(true) (with Seven-Tag Roster, variations, [%eval] comments, NAGs, promotions, en passant) can be perfectly re-imported by importPGN(): 123 moves → export → re-import → 123 moves, all information preserved losslessly.
    • Chinese/English manual sync: This manual and the Chinese manual have both been synchronized to Rev29 content. New sections added: PGN import failure root-cause analysis, stats page en passant fix, NAG Black-side perspective fix, PGN tolerance improvements.

    v1.0.4 Changelog

    This is the v1.0.4 major release, versionCode 104. Adds Chess960 mode, standardized PGN handling, heatmap-based statistics, and expanded stats dimensions.

    • Fischer Random Chess (Chess960) mode (NEW):
      • New Game dialog gains a Chess960 option. Select an SP-ID (0..959) or random; selected SP-ID displays a back-rank arrangement preview.
      • Implements Chess960 castling correctly: King ends on g1/c1, Rook ends on f1/d1 (same final squares as standard chess), but starting position is randomized. A new chess960.js module provides the SP-ID generator, Shredder-FEN castling-rights encoder/decoder, and 960 castling legality checker.
      • Adds AndroidBridge.setChess960Mode(boolean) JavascriptInterface, which toggles Stockfish's UCI_Chess960 option. The flag is automatically re-applied after engine (auto-)restarts so crash recovery does not silently drop the 960 setting.
      • PGN export for Chess960 games emits [Variant "Chess960"] + [SetUp "1"] + [FEN "..."] (FEN uses Shredder castling-rights format, e.g. HAah). PGN import recognizes [Variant "Chess960"], [Variant "Fischerandom"], [Variant "Fischer Random"], [Variant "FRC"], and auto-derives the SP-ID.
      • All UI strings are fully bilingual (Chinese / English).
    • Standardized PGN handling (rewrite):
      • New pgn-standard.js module implements strict 1994-PGN-spec encoding and tolerant decoding.
      • Exported PGN always contains the Seven Tag Roster: [Event], [Site], [Date], [Round], [White], [Black], [Result].
      • Movetext is wrapped at ~78 columns (spec recommendation); the result marker (1-0/0-1/1/2-1/2/*) is always the final token.
      • Comments embed [%eval ...] tags (Lichess/Chessbase de-facto standard), persisting cached engine evaluations into the PGN for higher information density.
      • Comments embed [%clk ...] framework (placeholder for future time-control support).
      • Tag values are strictly escaped (\ → \\, " → \") and forced single-line.
      • PGN parser (tolerant mode): auto-fixes nested {} comments (spec violation), auto-closes unclosed comments, normalizes 0-0 numeric zeros to O-O, skips invalid SAN tokens instead of failing the whole parse, defaults missing Result to *, and silently tolerates missing [SetUp "1"] when FEN is present.
      • Discards the pre-v1.0.3 ad-hoc PGN export design (incomplete tags, missing result markers, etc.).
    • Heatmap-based control statistics (NEW):
      • Statistics page gains a "Heatmap Control Statistics" section that walks every real position (initial + after each move), computes per-square attacker counts for both sides, and caches by FEN to avoid duplicate computation.
      • Renders an 8×8 average-control heatmap: each square shows (White avg / Black avg) attacker counts, with HSL background indicating net control (blue = White-leaning, red = Black-leaning, purple = contested).
      • Adds "White/Black Strongest Square" and "White/Black Weakest Square" stats, ranked by average control across all positions.
      • Adds "Center White/Black Average" and "Center Net (W-B)", computed as the mean over d4/e4/d5/e5.
    • Expanded statistics dimensions: On top of existing dimensions (material balance, move quality, eval trend, time management, opening repertoire, pawn structure, center control, king safety, game complexity), adds the new heatmap-control block.
    • Web Worker parallel computation (NEW):
      • New worker-pool.js module offloads PGN parsing, statistics computation, and control-map computation to a Web Worker thread, avoiding UI-thread blocking.
      • The Worker is created via a Blob URL (compatible with the WebView's script-src 'unsafe-inline' CSP) and ships with a slim copy of chess primitives (attacked, getCtrlMap, makeMvInPlace, fenToState, etc.) — no shared scope with the main thread.
      • All public APIs (workerParsePGN, workerComputeHeatmapStats, workerGetCtrlMap) return Promises; if Workers are unavailable (very old devices), they fall back to inline synchronous execution, guaranteeing feature parity.
    • Time-control chess support (NEW):
      • The New Game dialog gains a "Time Control" section with a dropdown for 5 modes: Untimed / Sudden Death / Fischer Increment / Bronstein Delay / US Delay.
      • With time control enabled, the in-game UI shows both clocks (live countdown); remaining time < 30 s turns red as a warning; flag-fall ends the game.
      • Time-deduction rules are correctly implemented for each mode: Fischer adds increment after each move; Bronstein/US-delay skips deduction during the delay window; Sudden death deducts actual elapsed time per move.
      • With time control enabled, PGN export emits a [TimeControl "..."] header (e.g. "300+3") and per-move [%clk HH:MM:SS] annotations.
      • Without time control, PGN comments use [%emt HH:MM:SS] (elapsed move time) — the "Elapsed Move Time" tag defined in spec §10.2.7.
    • PGN annotation system expansion (NEW):
      • NAG (Numeric Annotation Glyph) support: adds NAG_MAP, nagToSymbol, symbolToNag, formatNagToken, covering move-quality ($1-$6: !/ ?/ !!/ ??/ !?/ ?!) and position-evaluation ($10-$18: =/ ⩲/ ⩱/ ±/ ∓/ +-/ -+) glyphs.
      • Visual annotations [%csl ...] and [%cal ...]: adds formatCslTag, formatCalTag, parseCslTag, parseCalTag, following the Lichess/Chessbase de-facto standard format (e.g. [%csl Gb4,Rc5], [%cal Ge2e4,Rg1f3]).
      • Automatic selection & caching of per-move visual annotations (cache key = moveRecords index):
        • Blue arrows (B): own-piece → important square control paths, ranked by an importance score ("center +3 / extended center +1 / contested +1 per opponent attacker") and capped at the top 3.
        • Red arrow (R): when the current move gives check, drawn from the checker to the checked king.
        • Green highlighted squares (G): the checked king's adjacent safe squares (empty or capturable squares not attacked by the checker), i.e., "escape squares".
        • Yellow arrow (Y): when the current move threatens the opponent's queen, drawn from the mover to the queen's square.
      • All visual annotations are written into the corresponding move's {} comment on PGN export; the stats page gains a "Visual Annotations" section tallying each color count plus the NAG distribution.
      • [TimeControl] header parsing/formatting supports all 6 formats: Sudden Death / Fischer Increment / Bronstein Delay / US Delay / Staged / Hourglass.
    • Version sync: Internal versionCode, user-visible versionName, AndroidManifest, build.gradle, every in-app UI display (header bar, About dialog, loading page, error page), Java file VERSION constants, README, NOTICE, every README.license file, and the HTML manuals — all synchronized to v1.0.4.
    • Stockfish engine: Uses the official Stockfish 18 arm64-v8a-dotprod build (same as v1.0.3), with NEON acceleration.
    • Signing: APK uses v1 / v2 / v3 triple signing scheme, compatible with Xiaomi HyperOS 3 and all supported Android versions.

    v1.0.4 Patch Revision (version number unchanged)

    This patch addresses three categories of issues without bumping the version: the captured-piece statistics bug with pawn promotion, v1.0.4 new-UI style consistency, and several code-quality improvements. This round adds: move-history scroll fix, New Game dialog layout redesign, visual-annotation color semantics redefinition, PGN save prompt cancel button, AI opponent name with difficulty level, timeout-win eval bar fix, Stockfish time-management UCI commands, haptic feedback for all new buttons.

    • Move-history auto-scroll fix (bug fix): The main-UI move-history panel sometimes scrolled back to the top during frequent re-renders (e.g. AI thinking). Root cause: when render() was throttled (deferred 200ms), the old .mlist element's scrollTop could be stale or 0. Fix: added "is at bottom" detection — if the user was at the bottom, scroll to the bottom after rebuild (newest move visible); if the user was scrolled up reading old moves, preserve their exact position.
    • New Game dialog layout redesign (feature completion): Chess960 settings (SP-ID input, back-rank preview, note text) are no longer shown below "Play Color". Instead, when Chess960 is enabled, they REPLACE the entire "Classic Openings (optional)" area. The Chess960 toggle and the "Use ECO Book" toggle are mutually grayed out: enabling Chess960 grays out the ECO toggle, and enabling ECO grays out the Chess960 toggle. Note: Revision 22 (Rev22) further adjusted — the Chess960 toggle itself was moved to directly below the "Play Color" section, the residual "Classic Openings (Optional)" title was removed, and the Chess960-ON dedicated settings area title changed from "Classic Openings" to "Fischer Random (Chess960)" (T('chess960_label')).
    • Visual-annotation color semantics redefinition (feature completion):
      • Escape squares changed to green arrows (checked king position → escape square), no longer green square highlights.
