      • New red squares = AI opponent's net-control strong squares, blue squares = player's net-control strong squares, yellow squares = high total-control squares (both sides combined), green squares = center-area squares with no control from either side.
      • Red arrow retained = checker → checked king.
      • 📊 Statistics page "Visual Annotations" section updated to the new semantics.
    • PGN save prompt cancel button (feature completion): The "Save PGN?" prompt shown before New Game / FEN import / PGN import now has a "Cancel" button. Clicking Cancel returns to the original screen without clearing any cache or executing any action.
    • AI opponent name with difficulty level (feature completion): The AI opponent's name in exported PGN now includes the difficulty level suffix, e.g. [Black "AI Opponent SL"], [White "AI Opponent Lv.4"], [Black "AI Opponent Custom"].
    • Timeout-win eval bar fix (bug fix): When one side's clock ran out and the other side won by timeout, the eval bar incorrectly showed the draw emoji (🤝). Now correctly shows the winner 🏆 / loser 💀 emoji with "Winning/Losing" text.
    • Stockfish 18 time-management UCI commands (feature completion): In timed games, the AI now uses the go wtime <ms> btime <ms> winc <ms> binc <ms> UCI command, letting Stockfish 18 manage its own time allocation (think longer in critical positions, shorter in simple ones) instead of fixed movetime. New AndroidBridge.engineGoTimed() bridge method.
    • Haptic feedback for new buttons (feature completion): Chess960 random button, SP-ID random button, time-control dropdown, and PGN save prompt buttons (Yes/No/Cancel) now all have HapticManager.fire('BUTTON_PRESS') haptic feedback, respecting the Android system global vibration preference.
    • Captured-piece statistics fix (bug fix): The original getCapturedPieces() inferred captured pieces by comparing current board piece counts against starting counts, which was wrong for pawn promotion. Fix: prefer moveRecords[i].captured as the authoritative source.
    • Piece-symbol display styling unification: The piece symbols in the Chess960 back-rank preview now use the EXACT same styling as board pieces (color + stroke + glow + font + weight).
    • Time-control clock UI rendering: Fixed a feature gap where the time-control clocks were never displayed in the UI; clock display elements are now added to both player bars.

    v1.0.3 Changelog

    A patch revision was applied after v1.0.3's initial release (version number unchanged, still v1.0.3 / versionCode 103). See the "v1.0.3 Patch Revision" section below for details.

    • Stats page time-management analysis (new feature): The "Time Management" module on the stats page is upgraded from v1.0.2's bare [%clk] counter to a full time analysis. The new extractMoveTimes() function auto-detects per-move thinking times in PGN comments {}, supporting:
      • v1.0.3 direct format: {3.2s +0.5 略优} (time + space + eval)
      • Standard PGN clock format (requires [TimeControl] header): [%clk HH:MM:SS] + [TimeControl "BASE+INC"]. The app tracks each player's previous remaining clock and derives each move's used time via used = previousClock + increment - currentClk. Three TimeControl notations are supported: "7200+60", "1800", "40/7200". Example: under [TimeControl "7200+60"], {[%clk 02:01:00]} yields used = 7200+60-7260 = 0s.
      • Earlier em-dash format: {3.2s——+0.5 略优} (backward-compatible)
      Displayed metrics: total time, White/Black time used, average per move, slowest/fastest move (with move number), time volatility (standard deviation), long-think count (>10s), quick-move count (<1s), per-phase time share (opening/midgame/endgame), and a per-move SVG bar chart (White = white bars, Black = blue bars, hover for move number and time). When a [TimeControl] header is present, a blue info bar at the top lists the base time and per-move increment.
    • Stats page PGN-text variation italics: Starting in v1.0.3, the variation portion wrapped in () (including the parentheses themselves and all content inside) is rendered in italic in the PGN text panel, visually distinguishing it from mainline moves.
    • Stats page PGN import fix (critical bug): Fixed the root cause of "importing a new PGN still shows the old game's stats". Root cause: when the user opens the stats page from the main game, _payload.moveRecords carries the current game's authoritative move records. When the user then taps "🗃️Import" to paste or select a new PGN file, _statsPastePGN() / onStatsPGNFileRead() updated only _payload.pgn and did NOT clear _payload.moveRecords. As a result, parsePGN() detected the non-null moveRecords and called parseFromMoveRecords() — replaying the OLD game's moves instead of parsing the newly imported PGN text. This manifested as "Game Metadata (headers) correct but moves/positions/stats all wrong". v1.0.3 adds _payload.moveRecords=null; _payload.evals=null; plus variation-selection state reset at both import entry points, forcing parsePGN to fall back to the simplified SAN parser for the new text.
    • Review mode crash fix (critical bug): Fixed crash when entering review mode. Root cause: _rvCell variable (declared with let) was referenced before its declaration — JavaScript's Temporal Dead Zone caused ReferenceError: Cannot access '_rvCell' before initialization. v1.0.3 moves the _rvCell calculation before its first use.
    • Settings auto-close after import: Settings window now closes automatically immediately after import completes. Added a 300ms secondary safety check to handle late-arriving onEngineInfo callbacks that might re-open the dialog.
    • 💾HTML export redesigned as static snapshot: The 💾HTML button no longer copies the entire page (including JS code). Instead, it outputs a pure static HTML file containing only the current selection state's UI and statistics (CSS + content), with no <script> tags, functions, or interfaces. The exported file can be opened in any browser, frozen at the selection state at export time.
    • Stats page clickable variation moves (new feature): In v1.0.2 only mainline moves were clickable for per-position statistics. Starting in v1.0.3, variation moves inside () are also clickable. When a variation move is clicked, the stats page automatically replaces the mainline move immediately to the LEFT of () with the ENTIRE series of variation moves from the first move to the clicked move (not just the clicked move), building a synthetic move sequence: mainline[0..mainIdxBefore-1] + variation moves[0..clickedIdx] where mainIdxBefore is the index of the mainline move to the LEFT of ( (the move being replaced). Note: the entire variation series replaces the single mainline move — not just the clicked move. The synthetic sequence feeds ALL stats computation. Variation moves are re-parsed via applySANMove() (handles castling, promotion, captures, disambiguation, etc.). The clicked variation move is highlighted in dark blue; preceding variation moves in the same series are highlighted in light blue, visually communicating that the entire series is included in the stats.
    • Stats page FEN Position panel (new feature): A new FEN panel is added below the PGN text panel, showing the FEN of the position right after the selected move (auto-generated in the background via stateToFEN()). The title is "Position FEN". The "Copy" button is at the bottom-right in its own row (flexbox right-aligned) to avoid overlapping the FEN text. Uses navigator.clipboard with document.execCommand('copy') fallback. When no move is selected, the initial position FEN is shown with a hint message.
    • Stats page selection banner (new feature): A selection banner above the PGN text panel shows the currently selected move number (mainline or variation), making it clear which position the stats below correspond to. Mainline selection shows a gold banner; variation selection shows a blue banner noting "Variation moves 1–N selected (N moves, replaced mainline move M)", explicitly indicating that the entire variation series replaces the single mainline move.
    • PGN comment format: _buildPGNComment() uses a space as separator between thinking time and eval annotation, e.g. {3.2s +0.5 略优}. Comments containing only eval (no time data) keep the original format {+0.5 略优}. Backward-compatible: the stats page also recognizes the earlier em-dash format {3.2s——+0.5 略优}.
    • Bilingual adaptation: All new UI strings (FEN panel label, time-management metrics, variation selection banner, etc.) ship with Chinese + English translations, supporting the existing ↔️ language toggle.
    • Version sync: APP itself (build.gradle versionCode=103 / versionName="1.0.3", AndroidManifest.xml), in-app UI display (header <span class="ver"> tag, About page v1.0.3, loading title, built_in_only notice, strings.xml app_name), manuals (cover, footer, title) — all synchronized to v1.0.3.
    • README/LICENSE/NOTICE file audit: Reviewed every file whose filename contains README / LICENSE / NOTICE (regardless of extension), updating each with v1.0.3 changes. NOTICE file gains a "VERSION HISTORY SUMMARY" section summarizing each release.

    v1.0.3 Patch Revision (version number unchanged)

    This revision does NOT bump the version number (still v1.0.3 / versionCode 103). The patch is split into eleven rounds: …round 10 (v1.0.3-p10) made review nav buttons stretch full width in portrait + unified scroll logic; round 11 (v1.0.3-p11) chart uses full horizontal space + fixed portrait move-list scroll root cause; round 12 (v1.0.3-p12) portrait chart width cap removed.

    v1.0.3-p12 (this round)

    • Review mode: portrait chart width cap removed: v1.0.3-p11 only reduced the chart SVG internal padding, but the portrait chart width calculation was still capped at Math.min(window.innerWidth - 48, 400) - 12 (max ~352px), leaving large gaps on wide screens. v1.0.3-p12 removes the 400px cap and -48 offset, unifying to window.innerWidth - 12 for both orientations so the portrait chart also fully utilizes horizontal space.

    v1.0.3-p11 (previous round)

    • Review mode: chart uses full horizontal space: reduced the eval trend chart SVG's left/right padding from 36px to 8px, so the chart points and lines fully utilize the horizontal space with minimal edge gaps.
    • Review mode: portrait move-list scroll root cause fix (critical bug): the v1.0.3-p10 scroll logic used an offsetParent walk to accumulate offsetTop, but in portrait layout .review-moves has CSS position:static (default), so .rmv-block's offsetParent jumps directly to .review-overlay (position:fixed), skipping the .review-moves container. This caused the accumulated offset to include the board and controls height, producing a completely wrong target scrollTop — the active move was scrolled out of view. v1.0.3-p11 replaces this with getBoundingClientRect() to compute the active element's absolute position relative to the scroll container: _offsetTop = _rActRect.top - _rListRect.top + _rList.scrollTop. This method doesn't depend on offsetParent / position CSS, correctly computing the offset in both portrait and landscape, jumping directly to the correct visible position.

    v1.0.3-p10 (previous round)

    • Review mode: nav buttons stretch full width in portrait too: the v1.0.3-p7 .review-nav CSS (flex:1 1 0 for horizontal stretching) was only defined inside the landscape media query, so portrait buttons stayed fixed-width. v1.0.3-p10 promotes .review-nav and .review-nav .btn to base CSS rules (outside media queries), so nav buttons stretch to fill the full row width in both portrait and landscape.
    • Review mode: unified move-list scroll-to-active logic for both orientations: the v1.0.3-p9 scroll logic used _rAct.offsetTop to compute the target position, but offsetTop is relative to offsetParent, which may not be the scroll container itself (especially in portrait where intermediate elements may exist). v1.0.3-p10 changes this to walk up the DOM from the active element to the scroll container, accumulating offsetTop, ensuring correct offset calculation regardless of which element is the offsetParent. This logic works in both portrait and landscape, jumping directly to the correct visible position in one step.

    v1.0.3-p9 (previous round)

    • Review mode: no more scroll-to-top on step navigation (critical improvement): After v1.0.3-p8 enabled sliding on the board to scroll the whole review body, users reported that navigating to a different step (clicking a move, clicking the progress bar, clicking nav buttons) caused the interface to scroll back to the top. Root cause: (1) every renderInternal() call does app.innerHTML=h which rebuilds the entire DOM, recreating the .review-body element and resetting its scrollTop to 0; (2) scrollIntoView({block:'center'}) scrolls ALL scrollable ancestors (including .review-body), so centering the active move also moved .review-body to a different scroll position. Fix: (1) capture .review-body.scrollTop before app.innerHTML=h and restore it after (parallel to the v1.0.3-p4 .mlist scroll preservation); (2) replaced scrollIntoView({block:'center'}) with a manual computation _rList.scrollTop = _rAct.offsetTop - (_rList.clientHeight/2) + (_rAct.offsetHeight/2) that scrolls ONLY the move-list container, leaving .review-body's scroll position untouched. Effect: after switching steps, the move list auto-scrolls to the active move (container-only scroll), while the whole review body's scroll position is preserved.
    • First-principles code audit fixes:
      • ai-bridge.js onBestMove safety timer clear order: previously onBestMove() cleared the safety timer BEFORE checking if the request was stale. If a stale bestmove arrived, the real bestmove was still pending but the safety timer was already cleared — if the real bestmove never arrived, doAIMove() would hang indefinitely. Fixed to check staleness first, then clear the timer.
      • tablebase.js brace-comment loop iteration cap: the while(moveText.includes('{')) loop could infinite-loop on PGNs with an unmatched {. Added _braceIter++<10 iteration cap.
      • ui.js stale comment cleanup: removed // ---- Exports ---- (misplaced, no exports follow) and other stale comments.
      • index.html.tpl stale comment cleanup: removed /* hint-btn removed */ (describes a removed CSS class) and other stale comments.

    v1.0.3-p8 (previous round)

    • Review mode: slide on the board to scroll the whole review body: After v1.0.3-p7 implemented the two-layer scroll layout, the chart and buttons could be accessed by scrolling the whole review body, but sliding on the board didn't trigger scroll — because the global touchmove handler called preventDefault() when a touch moved >10px on the board (designed for the main game to prevent accidental page scroll on board slides), and the base .bgrid CSS set touch-action:none (blocking the browser from handling pan gestures on the board). The v1.0.3-p8 fix:
      • Global touchmove handler skips preventDefault in review mode: added if(reviewMode) return; at the start of the touchmove handler, letting the browser's native scroll take over touch slides on the board.
      • Review board .bgrid gets touch-action:pan-y: in the landscape media query, .review-left .review-board .bgrid gets touch-action:pan-y, overriding the base .bgrid's touch-action:none, so the browser handles vertical pans (scroll). Horizontal pans are still blocked to avoid interfering with potential horizontal gestures.
      • Main game unaffected: in main-game mode (non-review), board slides still don't scroll the page — the original behavior is preserved.

    v1.0.3-p7 (previous round)

    • Landscape review mode: two-layer scroll redesign (critical improvement): In v1.0.3-p6's layout, .review-body was set to overflow:hidden (no scroll), so when the board was tall, the chart and buttons at the bottom were pushed off-screen and inaccessible. The v1.0.3-p7 fix:
      • Two-layer scroll: .review-body changed from overflow:hidden to overflow-y:auto (layer 1 — the whole review body scrolls, so the user can scroll to see the chart, slider, eval bar, nav buttons, and analyze button); .review-moves keeps overflow-y:auto + height:var(--rv-board-h) (layer 2 — move list scrolls independently without affecting the board).
      • Board width always greater than move-list width: board size is determined by "viewport width × 60% ÷ 8" (no longer capped by REVIEW_CELL or viewport height), ensuring board width (60%) is always greater than move-list width (40%).
      • Board + move list fill all width: board 60% + move list 40% = 100% viewport width, flush to left and right edges, continuous from left to right with no gap.
      • Board not fully visible — solved via scroll: if the board is taller than the viewport (e.g. narrow phone in landscape), the user scrolls layer 1 (the whole review body) to see the board's bottom + chart + buttons.
      • JS sets --rv-board-h CSS variable: .review-body's style attribute gains a --rv-board-h variable (= board pixel height); .review-moves's height references this variable, ensuring the move list height matches the board height.

    v1.0.3-p6 (previous round)

    • Review move-list independent scroll — real root cause fix (critical bug): v1.0.3-p5 already gave the move list its own independent scroll viewport via CSS (overflow-y:auto + height:100% + min-height:0), but users reported it still couldn't scroll independently. Real root cause: renderInternal() called scrollIntoView({block:'center'}) on every render to center the active move in the viewport. The engine triggers render() 10–50 times per second during analysis (via onEngineEval/onMultiPVProgress callbacks), and each scrollIntoView yanked the move list back to the active move position — the user's manual scroll was immediately reset, manifesting as "the move list can't scroll independently". Fix: added a global variable _lastReviewStepScrolled (initial -2); scrollIntoView now only fires when reviewStep CHANGES (i.e., when the user navigates to a different step). enterReview() resets _lastReviewStepScrolled=-2 to ensure the first render after entering review mode scrolls the active move into view. Also removed the redundant setTimeout(50) scrollIntoView in reviewGoTo() (renderInternal now handles it via the guard). Verification: manually scrolling the move list in review mode no longer resets during engine analysis; clicking a different step still scrolls the active move to center.

    v1.0.3-p5 (previous round)

    • Landscape review mode: independent move-list scroll viewport: In v1.0.3-p4's landscape review layout, the entire .review-body was set to overflow-y:auto (whole-page scroll), so the move list didn't have its own independent scroll viewport — when moves exceeded the height, the entire page (including the board and controls) scrolled together, pushing the board off-screen. The v1.0.3-p5 fix:
      • Independent move-list scroll: .review-body changed from overflow-y:auto to overflow:hidden (body itself doesn't scroll); .review-top changed from flex:0 0 auto to flex:1 1 0 (fills all height above .review-bottom); .review-moves gets height:100% + min-height:0 + overflow-y:auto so it fills the row height and scrolls independently. The board stays fixed; only the move list scrolls.
      • Board vertically centered: .review-left gets height:100% + justify-content:center so the board is vertically centered in the row.
      • Bottom controls pinned: .review-bottom gets flex:0 0 auto, always pinned at the bottom, no scroll.
    • First-principles code audit fixes: every line of every file was reviewed, thinking about optimization opportunities based on design intent. Main findings and fixes:
      • tablebase.js move-number regex bug: removed a buggy regex text.replace(/(\d+)(\.[^\d])/g,'$1.$2') that added an extra dot to move numbers (turned 1. e4 into 1.. e4). The downstream moveNumRe=/^\d+\.+$/ tolerates any number of dots, so the bug was benign, but the regex was clearly wrong. After removal, the preceding regex (handles 1.e4→1. e4) and the following regex (handles 1 e4→1. e4) cover all cases.
      • tablebase.js dead code cleanup: removed the isCapture variable computation in _executeAndRecord that was never read (and move.enPassant is always undefined since legalMoves doesn't set that flag).
      • game-logic.js ECO hash-index fallthrough bug: fixed queryECOBookMove not falling through to the level-1 hash index when both level-3 and level-2 miss. Previously it degraded to a full ECO_OPENINGS scan, hurting ECO lookup performance for 3+ move openings. Now level-3 miss → level-2 miss → level-1 index → full scan, with graceful degradation at each level.

    v1.0.3-p4 (previous round)

    • Landscape review mode: board+moves fill full width + move list scrollable: In v1.0.3-p2's landscape review layout, the move list had a max-width: calc(var(--rv-board-w) * 0.90) cap, leaving unused whitespace between the board and the move list, and between the move list and the right screen edge. The v1.0.3-p4 fix:
      • Removed the move-list width cap: deleted the max-width rule, changed to flex:1 1 0 so the move list takes ALL remaining width to the right of the board.
      • Board + move list flush to edges, no gap: .review-left (board container) padding changed from 2px 4px to 0; .review-top gap stays 0; .review-moves padding tightened to 2px 2px 2px 4px. The board's left edge is flush with the screen's left edge, the move list's right edge is flush with the screen's right edge, and there is no gap between them — continuous from left to right.
      • Move list scrollable: .review-moves keeps overflow-y:auto; when the number of moves exceeds the visible height, the move list itself scrolls vertically.
      • Board sizing adjusted: board width cap changed from 65% to 55% of viewport width, giving the move list more display space (move list is ~45% of viewport width).
    • Main-UI move-list auto-scroll-to-top fix (critical bug): Fixed the bug where the main-UI move-history list (.mlist) kept scrolling back to the top on its own. Root cause: every renderInternal() call does app.innerHTML=h which rebuilds the entire DOM, recreating the .mlist element and resetting its scrollTop to 0. The engine triggers render() 10–50 times per second during search (via onEngineEval/onMultiPVProgress callbacks), each time resetting the user's manual scroll position back to the top — manifesting as "the move list keeps scrolling back to the top". Fix: capture .mlist's scrollTop BEFORE app.innerHTML=h, and restore it immediately after the innerHTML replacement. Only executed in non-review mode (review mode has its own scrollIntoView logic). Verification: scrolling the move list during engine search no longer resets the position.

    v1.0.3-p3 Hotfix

    • App startup black-screen fix (critical bug, introduced by v1.0.3-p2): Fixed a JavaScript syntax error introduced by v1.0.3-p2 that caused the app to show a completely black screen after opening. Root cause: when v1.0.3-p2 refactored the landscape review-mode layout, it split the original single move-list rendering logic into two branches (if(_isLandscapeReview){...}else{...}) but forgot the closing } for the if(reviewMode){ block. This broke the try{...}catch(e){...} structure of the renderInternal() function — the }catch(e){ appeared at a position with no matching try{, causing the JavaScript parser to throw SyntaxError: Unexpected token 'catch'. The entire chess.html script could not be parsed, so when the app started, the render() function didn't exist and the page was completely blank (black screen). Fix: added the missing } // close if(reviewMode) after the move-list rendering if/else branches and after h+='</div></div>'; // close .review-body, .review-overlay. Verification: ran node --check on ui.js and on the built chess.html's embedded JS — both pass; all 5 chess.src modules (game-logic.js / ai-bridge.js / tablebase.js / eco-data.js / ui.js) pass node --check. Lesson: future structural changes to large functions like renderInternal() should be syntax-checked with node --check immediately after building, rather than waiting until APK build + device testing to discover the error.

    v1.0.3-p2 (previous round)

    • PGN import: cascade-failure fix (critical bug): Fixed the issue where a single illegal move in a PGN caused all subsequent moves to be silently dropped. Root cause: in _parsePGN() Phase 4 (replay loop), when a main-line token's SAN failed to parse (e.g. Nbd7 is illegal when the d7 pawn hasn't moved), the old logic just continued past the token WITHOUT advancing the side-to-move. Because PGN moves strictly alternate White/Black, skipping one move left the side-to-move unchanged, so every subsequent token also failed (wrong side's move) — manifesting as "PGN import only shows the first N moves, the rest are gone". Fix: v1.0.3-p2 does two things when skipping a token: (1) pushes a skipped:true placeholder entry to the moves array, keeping moveRecords indices aligned with PGN move numbers; (2) advances state.currentTurn (and bumps fullMoveNumber if Black was to move), giving subsequent tokens a chance to parse. Safety cap: 5 consecutive skips stops the parse. Effect: a PGN with one illegal move now imports all the OTHER moves correctly, with a single dimmed ... placeholder marker where the illegal move was.
    • Review mode control button shape optimization: The review-mode navigation buttons (⏮ ◀ ▶ ⏭) are changed from fixed-width to flex:1 1 0 horizontal stretching, filling the entire row width for better screen space utilization. The "Analyze All" button also keeps 100% width. In landscape mode, all control buttons (nav, slider, analyze) are grouped in the new .review-bottom section, all horizontally stretched edge-to-edge.
    • Landscape review mode layout redesign (critical improvement): The v1.0.3-p1 landscape review layout still had shortcomings — the chart was squeezed into a small area under the board, and the move list width could exceed the board width. v1.0.3-p2 completely redesigns the landscape review layout:
      • New structure: .review-body is now a vertical flex container with vertical scrolling; it's split into .review-top (board + move list, side by side) and .review-bottom (eval bar + slider + chart + nav buttons + analyze button, FULL width edge-to-edge).
      • Chart gets generous space: the chart now spans the FULL viewport width (window.innerWidth - 12 pixels), with height at ~35% of viewport height (Math.floor((window.innerHeight - 28) * 0.35), range 60–180 pixels). Left and right edges touch the screen edges, no gaps from left to right.
      • Move list always narrower than the board: .review-moves has max-width: calc(var(--rv-board-w) * 0.90) — the move list's maximum width is 90% of the board width, ensuring the move list is always narrower than the board.
      • Overflow content scrolls: .review-body has overflow-y: auto — when the total height of board + move list + chart + controls exceeds the viewport, the whole page scrolls vertically, ensuring all content is accessible.
      • Board sizing: the board+moves row takes 60% of viewport height; the board itself can be up to 65% of viewport width (leaving 35% for the move list).
      Portrait review layout is unchanged (original stacked layout).
    • First-principles code audit: every line of every file was reviewed, thinking about optimization opportunities based on design intent. Main findings and fixes:
      • The PGN cascade-failure bug above was the most severe bug found in this audit.
      • The old landscape review layout (v1.0.3-p1) had defects in chart space and move list width — redesigned.
      • Navigation buttons were too narrow — changed to horizontal stretching.
      • No other bugs or removable redundancies were found.

    v1.0.3-p1 (previous round, still included in this version)

    • PGN import: Type A variation mis-relocation fix (critical bug): Fixed the issue where PGNs exported by the app itself failed to round-trip on re-import — variations were not parsed correctly. Root cause: the importPGN() variation post-processing (relocate) logic did not distinguish Type A (an alternative to the owning move — the variation's first move is the SAME color as the owning move, e.g. 7. Kf2 (7.hxg3 Qxh1 8.Nc3 ...) where 7.hxg3 is White's alternative to 7.Kf2) from Type B (a continuation after the owning move — the variation's first move is the OPPOSITE color, e.g. 7. Kf2 (7... h6 8.Nc3 ...) where 7... h6 is Black's alternative to 7...h5). Both types have a first move that "differs from the actual next move", so the old logic always relocated them to mi+1 and mislabeled them as Type B continuations. As a result, Type A variations were displayed as 7... hxg3 Qxh1 8.Nc3 ... (Black's move) instead of the correct 7. hxg3 Qxh1 8.Nc3 ... (White's alternative to 7.Kf2). The v1.0.3-p1 patch adds a type check at the start of the relocate loop: if (v.firstMoveIsWhite === (mi%2===0)) — if it matches, skip the relocate and keep the variation attached to the owning move, ensuring correct move numbers and side labels.
    • PGN import: embedded FEN header support (feature enhancement): PGN import now fully supports the [FEN "..."] header — not only does it correctly parse the FEN position and continue with subsequent moves (already supported in v1.0.3's initial release), but it also displays correct move numbers. A new global variable _importedStartMoveNum (default 1) is set in importPGN(), _applyImportedFEN(), and _exitSetupImpl() based on the FEN's fullMoveNumber. The main-screen move history, review-mode move list, and PGN export (_buildPGNString()) all use Math.floor(i/2) + _importedStartMoveNum for the move-pair number. For example, a PGN with FEN r1bqkbnr/pppp1ppp/2n5/4p3/2B1P3/5N2/PPPP1PPP/RNBQK2R w KQkq - 0 4 now displays 4. Bxf7+ Kxf7 5. Ne5 ... instead of the previous 1. Bxf7+ Kxf7 2. Ne5 .... startGame() resets this variable to 1. The click-to-review onclick handlers now use the moveRecords index i (stored in pair.wi/pair.bi) to compute reviewStep = i+1, avoiding jump errors caused by the move-number offset.
    • Stale version string cleanup: the ENGINE_VERSION constant in StockfishNative.java, the VERSION constant in MainActivity.java, and the crash-protection startup log message in ChessApp.java were all updated from the stale "v1.0.2" to "v1.0.3", aligning with the actual app version.
    • README/LICENSE/NOTICE file audit: every file whose filename contains README / LICENSE / NOTICE (including those without extensions) has been reviewed and updated with the v1.0.3 patch revision details. NOTICE file's VERSION HISTORY SUMMARY section gains a patch entry; chess.src/README.license, java/com/Regalia/README.license, assets/README.license, cpp/README.license, res/README.license, and src/main/README.license are all synced.
    • Build artifacts: the delivered APK is compatible with Xiaomi HyperOS 3 and ships with all three signature schemes (v1 / v2 / v3, verified by apksigner); a source-code tar backup (without the engine binary) is also delivered.

    v1.0.2 Changelog

    • TXT settings import fix: Root-caused "import occasionally reports success but does not take effect" — when the engine was mid-search (go in flight), setoption + isready could not receive readyok, the 3-second timeout fired, and settings were silently dropped. The import flow now calls stopAndWaitForBestmove first to bring the engine to idle before applying settings; added protection that auto-disables autoConfig when the user explicitly imports threads/hash (so explicit values are not silently overridden by hardware detection); removed the duplicate toast in the file-picker entry point.
    • PGN variation parsing completeness: Changed the variation continuation loop's behavior on the first unparseable token from break (truncate the entire variation) to continue (skip only that token, keep parsing the rest), and applied the moveAlg forgiving fallback uniformly to every token (not just the first). Fixes "PGN variation segments incomplete" — previously, a single non-standard SAN in the middle of a variation caused all remaining moves to be dropped.
    • MultiPV variation extraction completeness: When the primary PV does not start with the bestmove (a rare MultiPV convergence case), no longer fabricate a fake "mainline" variation — instead, include the primary PV as an independent alternative line in the MultiPV iteration (starting from index 0); added fallback to _multiPVResult[0].pv when _lastEngineVariation is empty; fixed the display-side _formatVariationGroups label collision where mainline(1) + multipv(2,3) + pgn(1,2) all produced "🌿 Line 1" — PGN variation line numbers now start at max-engine-line + 1.
    • Frontend audit fixes (per qw3.7max v1.01 audit report):
      • Added a dirty-check at the end of the render() rAF callback — if a new render request was queued during the rAF tick, a compensating render is triggered, preventing UI/state desync.
      • executeMove's setTimeout(..., 420) callback now captures gameState.hash before the timeout and aborts if it changes, preventing stale callbacks from overwriting new state during undo/redo/flip (the "ghost game-over banner" bug).
      • Moved doAIMove() out of the rAF callback into setTimeout(0), letting the browser paint the post-move UI before the engine starts thinking — eliminates the "move then freeze" jank.
      • toggleSetup(): extracted common reset code; replaced if(gameState.wk && gameState.bk){_applyGameOver();} with a gameStatus() check that only applies game-over for actual terminal states, which is clearer.
      • infoCtrl now references the control-map entry directly instead of allocating a fresh {white,black} object on every render, reducing GC pressure.
      • _cachedBwrap liveness check changed from parentNode to document.body.contains() for stricter validation.
    • README.license file system: Supplemented README.license in every folder under src/main/ that contains more than just subfolders (src/main/res/, res/values/, res/xml/, res/mipmap-*/). Note: AAPT2 strictly requires file names in res/ subfolders to end with .xml or .png, so the per-subfolder files were consolidated into a single res/README.license at the res/ root. java/com/Regalia/README.license now includes entries for TlsSecurityHelper.java and RootDetector.java.
    • Version sync: APP itself (build.gradle versionCode=102 / versionName="1.0.2", AndroidManifest.xml), in-app UI display (header <span class="ver"> tag, About page v1.0.2, loading title, built_in_only notice), and APK signing version — all synchronized to v1.0.2.
    • Ponder-Hit fix (critical bug): Discovered that executeMove called AndroidBridge.getLastPonderMove() to check if the player's move matched the ponder prediction — but that method is a one-shot read (clears the Java field after returning), and onBestMove had already consumed it (storing the value in _lastPonderMoveFromEngine). Result: ponderHit() never fired, every player move stopPonder()'d and started a fresh search — the entire ponder optimization was silently broken. v1.0.2 uses the JS-side cached _lastPonderMoveFromEngine instead of re-calling the Java method.
    • "AI never moves" after engine crash fix: The _discardingPonderBestmove flag is set to true when a ponder is stopped, and cleared to false when the next bestmove arrives. But if the engine crashed while waiting (EOF/IOException/zombie), the bestmove never arrived, leaving the flag stuck at true — after recovery, the new engine's first real bestmove was silently discarded as if it were the stale ponder bestmove, manifesting as "AI never moves". v1.0.2 resets _isPondering, _discardingPonderBestmove, _lastPonderMove, _stopLatch, readyOkLatchHolder, and uciOkLatchHolder in cleanupEngineResources().
    • Review eval cache clear on engine restart: restartCurrentEngine() and onEngineRestarting() previously did not clear _reviewEvalCache — after restart, review mode still showed the old engine's evaluations (different hash table state, different time budget → potentially different eval). v1.0.2 adds _reviewEvalCache.clear(); _reviewEvalRequestedStep=-1; to both paths, and also clears _multiPVLines, _multiPVResult, _lastEngineVariation.
    • RejectedExecutionException safety net: The @JavascriptInterface engine methods (engineGo, engineEval, engineHint, startPonder, importSettings, etc.) previously called _engineExecutor.execute(...) directly — if the engine was mid-restart/shutdown, this threw RejectedExecutionException which propagated to the WebView JS thread and left JS-side loading flags stuck. v1.0.2 extracts a _safeExecute(Runnable, tag) wrapper that catches the exception and notifies JS via onEngineError callback to reset state.
    • boardVersion performance optimization: _updateBoardIncremental previously used JSON.stringify(gameState.board) as the "did the board change?" dirty check — serializing an 8×8 array to a ~1KB string at 10-50 engine progress callbacks/sec creates significant GC pressure. v1.0.2 adds a boardVersion integer to game state (incremented in makeMv/makeMvInPlace, restored in unmakeMv, incremented in _refreshStateAfterSetup, initialized to 1 in fenToState), and the dirty check is now an integer compare — ~100x faster.
    • MultiPV progress callback StringBuilder optimization: processInfoLine previously allocated new JSONObject() + 8 put() calls per MultiPV info line — at 10-50 info lines/sec during search, this was 500-2500 JSONObject allocations/sec. v1.0.2 builds the JSON via StringBuilder directly (only the pv field uses JSONObject.quote() for escaping), eliminating HashMap allocations.
    • detectBigCoreCount caching: CPU topology is fixed for the device's lifetime, but detectBigCoreCount() was re-parsing /proc/cpuinfo every time detectHardwareAndConfigure() was called. v1.0.2 adds a _cachedBigCoreCount field to cache the first result.
    • engine_jni.cpp dead-code removal: After v18.5.0 removed the engine-import feature, 500+ lines in engine_jni.cpp implementing nativeLoadEngine/nativeStartEngine/nativeSendCommand/nativeReadOutput/nativeDestroyEngine/nativeIsEngineRunning/nativeGetEngineEntryType + findEngineEntryPoint (8 strategies) + engineThreadFunc (dup2/pipe/pthread_create) + EngineHandle/EngineEntryType structs were completely uncalled — StockfishNative.java declares only nativeChmod and nativeRenice. v1.0.2 deletes all dead code (25.5KB → 4.2KB) and removes the dl link from CMakeLists.
    • applySettings branch consolidation: applySettings() previously had if(autoConfig)/else branches with ~50 near-identical lines each, the only difference being the source of Threads/Hash. v1.0.2 extracts the common options-application logic, branching only on Threads/Hash — reduces ~30 lines of duplication.
    • Dead API removal: postJsCallbackJson() (zero callers), ChessApp.checkEngineThreadCrash() + engineThreadCrashed + engineThreadCrashMessage (flag was set but never checked — the heartbeat mechanism already covers engine-process death) — all deleted. AndroidManifest.xml removes the unused READ_MEDIA_IMAGES permission (the built-in file browser queries MediaStore.Files, not MediaStore.Images, which doesn't require this permission on Android 13+).
    • PGN export to file (new feature): The original copyMoveHistory() only copied PGN to the clipboard. v1.0.2 extracts a _buildPGNString() shared helper and adds exportPGNToFile() which calls a new Java method openPGNExportFilePicker(content) → SAF ACTION_CREATE_DOCUMENT lets the user choose a save location (parallel to the settings-export flow). Adds REQUEST_CODE_EXPORT_PGN=1004 and _pendingExportType to distinguish settings/PGN export callbacks (onSettingsExported vs onPGNExported). A 💾 button is added next to the move-history card header.
    • toggleSetup simplification: The if(_exitSt && _exitSt!=='play') guard checked against 'play' — a value gameStatus() never returns (dead check). _applyGameOver() internally returns null for non-terminal statuses ('check'/'ongoing'). v1.0.2 simplifies to a direct _applyGameOver(gameStatus(gameState)) call.
    • Black-to-move opening move record fix (critical bug): When starting a new game with a Black-to-move ECO/FEN opening, setup mode (turn set to black), or a PGN with a [FEN "... b ..."] header, the move record did not automatically mark White's first-move slot as .... Root cause: with moveRecords=[] empty, Black's first move was pushed by executeMove into moveRecords[0] (which is White's slot), causing Black's first move to incorrectly appear in White's position; PGN export also became 1. e5 instead of the spec-compliant 1. ... e5. v1.0.2 adds the following at all 4 new-game entry points (startGame, _applyImportedFEN, exitSetup, importPGN): if gameState.currentTurn==='black', prepend a null placeholder to moveRecords, so Black's first move lands in moveRecords[1] (Black's slot); null renders as ... (PGN skip marker) in both the UI move list and the exported PGN, correctly indicating that White conceded the move. stateHistory[0].moveRecords is also synced to prevent the placeholder from being lost after undoing back to the opening (which would reintroduce the bug); the render layer and the enterReview review loop also add null safety checks, keeping UI / review / PGN indices consistent.
    • ECO opening moves auto-fill into move records (new feature): When the selected ECO opening's data contains a full move list (non-empty moves array), startGame now builds moveRecords in lockstep as it replays each ECO move — every move gets a proper SAN notation (including captures x, checks +, checkmates #, castling O-O/O-O-O, promotions =Q, etc.) plus from/to/piece/captured/isCheck/isCastling metadata. After the opening is replayed, the user immediately sees the full opening sequence in the move history (e.g. 1. e4 e5 2. Nf3 Nc6 3. Bb5) and can undo/redo or enter review mode to analyze each move. No ... placeholder is needed in this scenario — the ECO moves already fill the correct slots; the black-to-move placeholder only kicks in on the FEN/setup/PGN import paths with no ECO moves. stateHistory is also pushed for each move so undoing back to the opening correctly restores the initial position.
    • First-principles re-audit of previously non-effective fixes: This re-audit found 4 v1.0.2 changelog items that were claimed as fixed but either never took effect or were incompletely implemented. Each was root-caused and precisely fixed:
      • "Play Again" button ⚔️ prefix: The game-over banner's "Play Again" button was previously rendered as plain text ${T('play_again')} with no ⚔️ prefix. Fixed to ⚔️ ${T('play_again')}, matching the New Game toolbar button's style.
      • Redo does not trigger AI: redoMove() still ended with if(!gameOver&&!setupMode&&gameState.currentTurn!==playerColor){doAIMove();} — this would trigger a fresh AI search when the redo stack had only one entry left (e.g. the player undid right after their own move, before the AI replied), instead of redoing the AI's pre-recorded reply from the stack. This corrupted the redo stack and lost the original AI move. The call was removed entirely (requestEngineEval() still refreshes the eval bar for the restored position).
      • Settings import duplicate toast elimination: _fileBrowserSelect() (the file-picker entry path) called showToast(T('settings_imported_ok')) immediately after bridge.importSettings(content) — but importSettings() is asynchronous and eventually fires the onSettingsImported(result) callback, which itself shows a toast. The user saw two toasts: a generic "Settings imported" (from the file-picker entry) + a detailed "Settings imported (autoConfig disabled to honor explicit value, etc.)" (from the callback). Removed the file-picker entry's showToast and the synchronous _cachedMultiPV refresh (the cache refresh was also moved into the callback, since the engine applies settings asynchronously).
      • PGN export evaluation annotations: _buildPGNString() previously only emitted move notations and RAV variations — it did not implement the {score eval_word} and every-5-moves {SF18 D22 +1.0 8%W/91%D/1%L} annotations claimed in the changelog. Added a new _formatPGNEvalAnnotation(reviewStep, moveNum) helper that reads the cached eval for each step from _reviewEvalCache: every move emits a {+0.5 Slight adv.}-style annotation (score + eval word via posDesc(), matching the in-app eval bar), and every 5 moves (moveNum % 5 === 0) emits a full {SF18 D22 +1.0 8%W/91%D/1%L} annotation (engine name SF18, depth Dn, score, W/D/L probabilities). Moves without a cached eval emit no annotation, preserving backward compatibility.
    • README.license file system update: Updated all 6 README.license plain-text files (src/main/, src/main/assets/, src/main/assets/chess.src/, src/main/cpp/, src/main/java/com/Regalia/, src/main/res/) with per-file specifics of every v1.0.2 change (ECO auto-fill, PGN eval annotations, Redo no-AI, settings-import duplicate-toast removal, boardVersion performance optimization, _safeExecute exception safety net, stopAndWaitForBestmove, cleanupEngineResources ponder-flag reset, detectBigCoreCount caching, engine_jni.cpp dead-code removal, applySettings branch consolidation, dead API removal, READ_MEDIA_IMAGES permission removal, etc.) so future maintainers can quickly locate the license attribution for each change.
    • First-principles line-by-line re-audit + performance breakthroughs: After all 16 checklist items passed re-audit, every source file was re-reviewed line by line for design intent, with optimizations applied in priority order "bug fixes > feature completeness > performance breakthroughs > redundancy cleanup > simplification":
      • PV variation cache + fork grafting (performance breakthrough): Added _pvCache (Map) + _convertPVtoSANCached() + _checkPVDivergence(). The N PV lines returned by MultiPV typically share a common prefix (e.g. PV1=e4 e5 Nf3 Nc6, PV2=e4 e5 Nf3 d5 share "e4 e5 Nf3"). Previously each PV independently called _convertPVtoSAN, re-running makeMv+moveAlg for the shared prefix. The new scheme caches the converted SAN + post-state for every UCI prefix keyed by (state.hash, uciPrefix); shared prefixes are converted exactly once. 8 MultiPV lines × 10+ moves typical saves ~35 makeMv+moveAlg calls. Cache is cleared per-search (bounded at 200 entries).
      • moveAlg disambiguation performance breakthrough: The original moveAlg called cloneB(s.board) for every same-type same-color piece during disambiguation — up to 8 full board clones when 8 pawns can capture on the same file. Replaced with makeMvInPlace/unmakeMv (in-place modify + undo) — zero board allocations (mirrors the optimization already applied to legalMoves and hasLegalMoves).
      • _updateSingleSq signature dirty-check (performance breakthrough): The original _updateSingleSq unconditionally rebuilt innerHTML for every square (set style.background, className, built the full innerHTML string) — at 10-50 engine progress callbacks/sec, 64 squares × per-square innerHTML rebuild caused significant GC + layout thrash. The new scheme builds a cheap signature string per square (piece + selection + last-move + check + legal + control-map + anim) and only writes DOM when the signature changes. Most callbacks result in 0 square writes.
      • isDeadPosition single-pass scan (performance breakthrough): The original allocated a pcs[] array then ran multiple .filter()/.map() passes. Replaced with a single 64-square scan + early returns (any pawn/rook/queen → not dead), bishop square-color parity tracked inline. Same FIDE 5.2.2 coverage, ~3x faster. 13 edge-case tests all pass.
      • generateFEN / pieceZobristIdx / _esc lookup-table hoisting (performance breakthrough): generateFEN allocated a fresh {white:{...},black:{...}} piece map on every call; pieceZobristIdx built a fresh {pawn:0,knight:1,...} type index on every call; _esc/_escJs each used 5 chained .replace() calls allocating 5 intermediate strings. All three hoisted to module scope (_PIECE_FEN, _PIECE_TYPE_IDX, _ESC_MAP+_ESC_RE, _ESCJS_MAP+_ESCJS_RE), single regex + callback lookup completes the escape.
      • PGN variation skipped-token turn sync (bug fix): The original importPGN variation continuation loop, on encountering an unparseable token, did continue to skip it but did not advance vIsWhite/vMoveNum — the next token would be misattributed to the wrong side. Fix: a skipped token still consumes a turn per PGN spec; the side-to-move and move number must advance, otherwise the entire remaining variation desynchronizes.
      • _formatPGNEvalAnnotation explicit parens + type coercion (bug fix): The original mate-detection condition cached.mate&&cached.mate!==0||Math.abs(ev)>=90000 relied on JS operator precedence (happened to be correct but hard to read); cached.mate/cached.eval from JSON deserialization may be strings. Replaced with explicit (mateDist!==0)||Math.abs(ev)>=90000 + Number() coercion.
      • _getSqBg dead-code cleanup (redundancy cleanup): Removed the unused _sqBgCache declaration (a caching attempt that was never assigned/read) + the in-function lastFrom/lastTo computation (variables computed but never used in the return value).
    • Stats-page PGN import flow streamlined (UX fix): The "📂 Select PGN File" button on the stats page previously closed the stats page, returned to the main activity, and only then popped up the SAF file picker — one jump + one return, jarring UX. Now StatsActivity invokes ACTION_OPEN_DOCUMENT directly; after the user picks a file, onActivityResult reads the content and refreshes the stats page in place via the onStatsPGNFileRead(content) callback. The whole import flow no longer leaves the stats view. Cleaned up the orphaned statsRequestImport() Java bridge method, the MainActivity.pendingStatsImportRequest static flag, the main WebView's onStatsRequestImport() handler, and the leftover AndroidBridge.statsRequestImport feature check in _statsPastePGN() (paste is now fully contained in stats.html).
    • Variation label sequential numbering fix (critical bug): When the same move carried multiple variations (typical scenario: the player flips the board and the engine re-evaluates, producing new divergent predictions; or several MultiPV predictions diverge at the same move), _formatVariationGroups() previously derived line numbers from group/mpvIndex/lineNum fields — mainline was always 1, mpvIndex=0 was also 1, so two variations could both be labeled "🌿 Line 1". Replaced with positional sequential numbering (1, 2, 3, …) based on the variation's position in the array — labels are now guaranteed unique. Also added a same-SAN dedup guard in _checkPVDivergenceSANs() to prevent redundant variations from being attached in the first place.
    • Promotion UCI letter fix (critical bug): _mrToUci() (used to convert move records to UCI for comparison with the engine's PV) used mr.promotion[0] for the first letter — 'queen'→'q' correct, but 'knight'→'k' wrong (UCI spec uses 'n'). Result: every knight-promotion comparison always mismatched, triggering false divergence and attaching spurious "alternative line" variations at the divergence point. Replaced with an explicit {queen:'q',rook:'r',bishop:'b',knight:'n'} mapping. The ponder-hit check in executeMove() had the same bug (it concatenated the full word 'queen' instead of the letter 'q'), so promotion moves never matched the ponder prediction — every promotion fell back to stopPonder + a fresh search, defeating the ponder optimization for promotions entirely. Both sites fixed uniformly.
    • Stale AI state cleared on new game (critical bug): _resetGameUIState() previously didn't reset isAIThinking, _aiSafetyTimerId, _aiRetryCount, _evalLoading, _sfEvalReady, _ponderGen, _ponderMoveSAN, _ponderBarInfo, _pendingPonderMoveUCI, _multiPVLines, _multiPVResult, _lastEngineVariation. If the user started a new game / imported FEN / imported PGN while the AI was thinking: isAIThinking=true caused the new game's doAIMove() to early-return — the AI never moved on the new game; the old 15s safety timer was still pending and could fire on the new gameState; stale ponder/MultiPV data leaked into the new game's UI. Now uniformly reset for a clean slate.
    • AI first-move variation missing fix (critical bug): onBestMove() previously guarded _pendingBestMoveInfo assignment with if(moveRecords.length>0) — when the player plays Black and the AI plays White first, moveRecords.length===0, the guard skipped the assignment, and _processDeferredVariations() early-returned because _pendingBestMoveInfo was null — the AI's first move never got any 🌿 variation lines. Now lastIdx=-1 is allowed (_processDeferredVariations already resolves it to aiMoveIdx=0), so playing Black also shows the engine's predicted continuation for the AI's first move.
    • AI retry counter reset on engine restart: _aiRetryCount was previously only reset on successful bestmove, 3-time timeout, and engine error — not on engine auto-restart (onEngineRestarting/onEngineReady). If the engine crashed mid-AI-move (where _aiRetryCount had already incremented to 1 or 2) and self-recovered, the next doAIMove() after recovery would immediately increment to 2 or 3, potentially hitting the 3-retry cap and showing "AI timeout" even though the engine just recovered. Both sites now reset _aiRetryCount=0.
    • Review request with no moves shows feedback: onStatsRequestReview() previously returned silently when moveRecords was empty — the user tapped "🗂️ Review" but nothing happened, with no feedback. Now calls showToast(T('no_move_records')) to clearly state "No move records".
    • Tablebase cache LRU refresh on hit: _tbCache (Map) on a hit only did get without delete+set, so frequently-accessed entries could be evicted before cold entries — defeating LRU semantics. Now on hit, delete + set moves the entry to the "newest" position (Map preserves insertion order), matching _reviewEvalCache's implementation.
    • _reviewEvalCache gains a peek() method: The original get() refreshes LRU order on every access (delete + set). In iteration loops like _buildEvalTrendSVG, _findCriticalMoves, the move-list render, and openStatsPage's eval-data collection, every get triggered a Map delete+set — for a 100-step review that's 100 unnecessary Map operations, plus the current iteration's entry got pushed to the newest position while other entries got pushed toward eviction. Added peek(k) that reads without refreshing LRU; iteration loops uniformly switched to peek().
    • makeMv redundant captured variable cleanup: makeMv already extracts the captured piece at line 631 via capPiece=ns.board[to.row][to.col] (before mutation), but the Zobrist hash update at line 646 re-read it from the original state as captured=s.board[to.row][to.col] — ns is a deep clone of s, so the two values are identical. Reuse capPiece directly, eliminating the redundant read.
    • Language-preference SharedPreferences file unified (regression fix): StockfishNative.saveLangPref() in v1.0.2 was changed to write to "RegaliaEngine" (matching what isEnglishMode() reads), but EngineService.isEnglishMode() and updateNotification() still read from "Regalia_prefs" — a file never written to by any code path. Result: the foreground-service notification language always fell back to the system default, ignoring the user's in-app language choice. Unified to PREFS_NAME="RegaliaEngine". Also removed the dead en block in updateNotification() that read from the wrong prefs file and whose computed value was never used.
    • Stats page haptic respects user preference: StatsActivity.performHaptic() previously did a blind v.vibrate(30) — no hapticFeedbackEnabled check, no system haptic check, ignored the type parameter, and used the API 26+ deprecated vibrate(long). Users who disabled haptic in main app settings still felt vibration from stats-page buttons. Now reads hapticFeedbackEnabled from the same "RegaliaEngine" prefs + the system HAPTIC_FEEDBACK_ENABLED setting; both must be on. API 26+ uses VibrationEffect.createOneShot.
    • Stats-page HTML export callback JS injection fix: After exporting HTML, StatsActivity built the JS string with displayName.replace("'", "\\'") — only escaping single quotes, not backslashes, newlines, or control characters. A filename containing \, \', or a literal newline would break the JS string literal. Replaced with JSON encoding (matching the same file's PGN import path and StockfishNative.escapeJsString()), safely escaping all special characters.
    • Process.isAlive/destroyForcibly crash on API 21-25 fix: Process.isAlive() and destroyForcibly() are both API 26+ APIs, but minSdk=21. Three engine-shutdown paths called engineProcess.isAlive()/destroyForcibly() directly — on API 21-25 every shutdown threw NoSuchMethodError (silently swallowed by catch(Throwable), but destroyForcibly() never actually ran). Added a destroyForciblySafe() wrapper: API 26+ calls the real method, API 21-25 falls back to a second destroy(). All three shutdown paths now use isProcessAlive() + destroyForciblySafe().
    • BufferedReader resource leak fix: StockfishNative.handleFilePickerResult() and handlePGNFilePickerResult() previously used try { BufferedReader reader = ...; ... } finally { is.close(); } — is.close() closed the underlying stream, but the BufferedReader itself (and its internal char buffer) wasn't explicitly closed, relying on GC. Switched to try-with-resources wrapping the BufferedReader directly, matching StatsActivity's same-path pattern.
    • StockfishNative dead stats code cleanup (~80 lines): After v1.0.2 moved the stats page to StatsActivity's own JS bridge, the following dead code remained in StockfishNative: getStatsPayload(), closeStatsPage() (activityRef always points to MainActivity, so instanceof StatsActivity was always false), exportStatsHTML(), statsRequestReview(), _pendingStatsPayload (only read by the now-removed getStatsPayload()), _pendingStatsHTML (only set by the now-removed exportStatsHTML()), REQUEST_CODE_EXPORT_STATS_HTML, and the stats-HTML branch in handleExportFilePickerResult() — all removed. _pendingStatsPayload/_pendingStatsHTML were also memory leaks (large PGN payloads could linger until the next call or engine shutdown).
    • processEngineLine dead branch cleanup: The if (_isPondering) { ... return; } branch was unreachable — both stopPonder() and stopAndWaitForBestmove() set _isPondering=false before sending stop, so by the time bestmove arrives the flag is always false. The real discard path is the _discardingPonderBestmove check (set by the same callers). Removed the dead branch.
    • handleBestMove redundant { } block cleanup: In all three cases of the switch(state), the postJsCallback("onMultiPVResult(...)") was wrapped in a redundant { } block — a leftover from a removed if condition. Removed the redundant blocks.
    • ai-bridge.js duplicate function definition cleanup: _checkPVDivergence(pv1Moves, pv2Moves) (finds the longest shared prefix between two PV arrays) and _checkPVDivergence() (iterates over _pendingEnginePVs to attach divergent variations) shared the same name — under JS's last-declaration-wins rule, the former was silently shadowed, every call site used 0 arguments, and the former was never invoked. Removed the dead function and its misleading "finds the longest shared prefix" comment (the active function _convertPVtoSANCached() finds shared prefixes via its own _pvCache, so it doesn't need this helper).
    • Stats page total moves cannot exceed 98 fix (critical bug): The stats page's parsePGN() used a simplified SAN parser (applySANMove/canMoveTo) that doesn't handle check detection, disambiguation, en passant, etc. Once one move failed to parse, the game state didn't advance and all subsequent moves cascade-failed — manifesting as "total moves capped at ~98". Root-cause fix: openStatsPage() now also sends the main app's authoritative parsed move records (from/to/piece/captured/promotion/notation); the stats page replays them via parseFromMoveRecords() (using executeMove() which correctly advances state), completely bypassing the simplified SAN parser. For pasted/imported PGN (no move records available), the simplified parser is still used as fallback.
    • Stats page PGN text panel piece symbol styling fix: The piece symbols (♔♚♘♞ etc.) in the PGN text panel were the same color as the destination-square text (both var(--text) cream) — no white/black color, stroke, or glow matching the main board. Root cause: CSS specificity — .pgn-display .move (specificity 0,2,0) overrode .piece-white/.piece-black (specificity 0,1,0). Fix: (1) increased CSS specificity to .pgn-display .move .piece-white; (2) restructured renderSAN() so the piece symbol gets its own <span class="piece-white/piece-black"> while the destination/capture/check suffix stays in the default text color — matching how the main board separates piece symbol from square label.
    • Manual chapter layout restructure: Consolidated the v1.0.2 and v1.0.1 changelog details (previously scattered before the TOC) into Appendix A: Version Changelogs at the end of the manual (after Chapter 15, before the footer). Added "Appendix A" entry to the TOC. Updated footer version from v1.0.1 to v1.0.2. Variation wireframe description updated to sequential numbering (no longer split into mainline/alternative).
    • qw3.7max external code-review report — all 7 optimizations implemented: Per the external review report (qw3.7max v1.0.2 audit report), implemented every suggestion in priority order (bug fix > feature completeness > performance > redundancy > simplification):
      • P1-1 State-comparison logic simplified: The verbose null-check in _updateBoardLightweight() (_selChanged/_newHover, multiple !! coercions + short-circuit chains) rewritten with optional chaining selectedSquare?.row !== _prevSelSq?.row. Also renamed _newHover → _infoChanged (the variable tracks info-square changes, not just hover).
      • P1-2 innerHTML XSS defense: The review move-classification span's _mcls.color/_mcls.label now wrapped in _esc(). Currently redundant (_classifyMove returns internal constants), but provides defensive protection against future changes that might introduce user-controlled data.
      • P2-1 scrollIntoView compatibility: behavior:'instant' (a newer CSSOM View value not recognized by some older WebViews) → behavior:'auto' at 2 call sites (review-mode auto-scroll).
      • P3-1 Eliminate forced synchronous layout (performance): Review auto-scroll changed from rAF + setTimeout(0) to double rAF (requestAnimationFrame(function(){ requestAnimationFrame(function(){ ... }) })). The first rAF fires after layout, the second after paint; reading layout info (scrollIntoView) in the second rAF guarantees no forced synchronous layout (layout thrashing). The old setTimeout is a macrotask that may run before the browser's layout/paint step.
      • P3-2 DOM cache dimensionality reduction (performance): _sqElCache changed from 2D array-of-arrays _sqElCache[r][c] (array of arrays, two pointer dereferences, non-contiguous memory) to a 1D array _sqElCache[r*8+c] (single contiguous allocation, one dereference). Reduces a small but measurable overhead on the hot incremental-update path (10-50 engine progress callbacks/sec).
      • P4-1 Modulo simplification: ((i+1)%2)===1 → (i%2)===0 (mathematically equivalent, eliminates the unnecessary +1). Updated at 2 call sites.
      • P4-2 DOM query cache: The review-moves-list element _rListEl hoisted to a module-level variable, assigned after full render and cleared on cache invalidation. Avoids getElementById('reviewMovesList') DOM tree walk on every render's scroll-into-view path.
      • P5-1 Template literals: The review move-classification span's string concatenation (+= '') → ES6 template literal for readability.

    v1.0.1 Changelog

    • Simplified Notification Bar: The persistent notification now shows only three states — Ready / Analyzing / Error — and no longer displays search depth or speed. Detailed depth/nodes/speed/score data is still shown in the in-app eval bar; the notification is intentionally minimal to avoid distracting the user.
    • Undo Auto-Select Fix: Fixed a bug where undo did not auto-select the original piece. After undo, the piece that was moved in the undone step is now auto-selected (at its starting square). Works for multiple consecutive undos. The auto-selected square can be tapped to deselect, just like any other selection.
    • PGN Variation Parsing Improved: Fixed a bug where variations were lost or attached to the wrong move during PGN import. Added Type A fallback (moveAlg matching), mainTokenIdx index tracking (handles main lines with invalid moves), and diagnostic logging when the first variation token cannot be matched. Nested RAV (Recursive Annotation Variation) is compliant with PGN spec §8.2.5.
    • PGN Import Undo Fix: Fixed root cause of "cannot undo white's first move after PGN import" — the stateHistory snapshot was taken after moveRecords.push, so the restored moveRecords still contained the undone move. Now matches executeMove's order: snapshot first, then push.
    • Smoother Move Animations: Enabled GPU compositing layers for piece animations (translateZ(0), will-change, backface-visibility), added contain:layout style paint to limit repaint scope, and removed expensive box-shadow transitions. Reduces jank and improves responsiveness.
    • Foreground Service Notification Enhanced: The persistent notification supports click-to-open the app and is non-removable (setOngoing(true) + FLAG_NO_CLEAR). On Xiaomi HyperOS 3, even if the system allows dismissal, the foreground service itself keeps running and the notification auto-restores on the next status update.
    • Language Switch Haptic Feedback: Tapping the Chinese/English toggle button now triggers a TOGGLE_ON haptic feedback, consistent with other button interactions.
    • MobSF Security Audit Fixes: Remediated 5 static-scan findings: JavaScript interface safety documentation, TLS certificate pinning code reference, Certificate Transparency reference, SafetyNet non-applicability statement, and ChessApp exception log minimization.
    • Terminology Sync: English move classification label "Book" changed to "Mediocre" (since v1.0.0).
